## 5. Project Initialization

### 5.1 Clone Upstream

Use PowerShell:

```powershell
mkdir C:\dma
cd C:\dma
git clone https://github.com/ufrisk/pcileech-fpga.git
cd C:\dma\pcileech-fpga
git rev-parse HEAD | Out-File C:\dma\upstream-commit.txt
```

Do not edit random zip downloads if you can avoid it. Use Git so you can compare changes.

### 5.2 Copy the Correct Board Folder

Example for Squirrel:

```powershell
Copy-Item C:\dma\pcileech-fpga\PCIeSquirrel C:\dma\work\squirrel-rtl8125 -Recurse
cd C:\dma\work\squirrel-rtl8125
```

Use your actual board folder.

Do not build CaptainDMA firmware inside the Squirrel folder unless your board actually uses that project.

### 5.3 File Modification Map

Old guides keep sending people to the wrong file. Use this map instead.

| What you want to change | Where to change it |
|-------------------------|--------------------|
| Vendor ID / Device ID | Vivado PCIe IP GUI / `pcie_7x_0.xci` |
| Revision ID | Vivado PCIe IP GUI / `pcie_7x_0.xci` |
| Class Code | Vivado PCIe IP GUI / `pcie_7x_0.xci` |
| Subsystem Vendor / Subsystem ID | Vivado PCIe IP GUI if exposed, otherwise shadow config plan |
| DSN signal | `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv`, `rw[127:64]` / `cfg_dsn` |
| Command auto-set | `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv`, `rw[21]` |
| Status auto-clear | `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv`, `rw[20]` |
| Shadow read zero/data switch | `src/pcileech_fifo.sv`, `rw[203]` |
| Shadow config write enable | `src/pcileech_fifo.sv`, `rw[206]` |
| Shadow config bytes | `ip/pcileech_cfgspace.coe` |
| WriteMask bytes | `ip/pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe` |
| Zero4K BAR bytes | `ip/pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe` |
| BAR routing / BAR responder | `src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv` or board equivalent |
| Generated PCIe core wrapper | `.gen/sources_1/ip/.../pcie_7x_0_core_top.v` if absolutely necessary |

For current upstream-style projects, any tutorial putting `rw[203]` in `pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv` is pointing at the wrong file.

### 5.4 Generate the Vivado Project - GUI Route

1. Open Vivado from Start Menu
2. Open Tcl Console
3. Change to your copied board folder:

```tcl
cd C:/dma/work/squirrel-rtl8125
source vivado_generate_project.tcl -notrace
```

A correctly generated project has:

```text
Project opens.
Sources panel is populated.
PCIe IP appears.
No fatal Tcl errors.
```

These usually mean the folder, part, or path is wrong:

```text
ERROR: file not found
ERROR: part not found
ERROR: IP failed to generate
```

Fix:

- wrong folder
- missing Vivado device support
- bad path
- wrong Vivado version

### 5.5 Build Stock Firmware First

Before customization:

```tcl
source vivado_build.tcl -notrace
```

Baseline pass:

```text
Synthesis completed
Implementation completed
Bitstream generation completed
Timing met
```

Baseline failure:

```text
Synthesis failed
Implementation failed
Timing failed
Critical warning about wrong part or constraints
```

Do not ignore timing and critical warnings. A `.bit` file existing is not enough.

### 5.6 Keep the Stock Build as a Control

Build and save the stock baseline before changing anything:

- project generated
- stock bitstream built
- timing report saved
- stock firmware flashed
- target Windows sees the stock device
- PCILeech works
- cold boot still sees the stock device

If stock firmware fails, custom firmware will not magically fix it.

---

## 6. PCIe Core Configuration

### 6.1 Open the PCIe IP in Vivado GUI

In Vivado:

```text
Sources -> find pcie_7x_0.xci -> double click -> Re-customize IP
```

If you cannot find the PCIe IP, you may be in the wrong generated project or wrong board folder.

### 6.2 Change Identity Fields

Use donor data:

| Field | Source | Example |
|-------|--------|---------|
| Vendor ID | Hardware IDs / Arbor | `10EC` |
| Device ID | Hardware IDs / Arbor | `8125` |
| Revision ID | Hardware IDs / Arbor | `05` |
| Class Code | Hardware IDs / Arbor | `020000` |
| Subsystem Vendor ID | Hardware IDs / Arbor | `10EC` |
| Subsystem ID | Hardware IDs / Arbor | `0123` |

Common class codes:

| Class | Meaning |
|-------|---------|
| `020000` | Ethernet controller |
| `0C0330` | USB xHCI controller |
| `010601` | SATA AHCI controller |
| `040300` | HD Audio controller |

Only changing VID/DID is incomplete.

### 6.3 Configure BARs

In the PCIe IP BAR tab, match the donor:

- enabled or disabled
- memory or I/O
- 32-bit or 64-bit
- prefetchable or non-prefetchable
- size

Example:

```text
BAR0: enabled, memory, 32-bit, non-prefetchable, 16KB
BAR1: disabled
BAR2: disabled
BAR3: disabled
BAR4: disabled
BAR5: disabled
```

Do not copy the Windows runtime memory range into the firmware. Windows assigns that address at boot.

### 6.4 64-bit BAR Rule

If BAR0 is 64-bit:

```text
BAR0 = low 32 bits
BAR1 = high 32 bits
```

BAR1 is not free.

If BAR2 is 64-bit:

```text
BAR2 = low 32 bits
BAR3 = high 32 bits
```

BAR3 is not free.

### 6.5 Generate Output Products

After changing IP:

1. Click OK
2. Let Vivado ask to generate output products
3. Generate
4. Watch the Messages window
5. Save the `.xci` diff if using Git

Regeneration succeeded:

```text
IP output products generated successfully.
```

Stop on any of these:

```text
IP locked
IP upgrade required
Part not found
Output product generation failed
```

Do not continue until the IP actually regenerated.

### 6.6 Generated File Warning

Some guides tell you to edit:

```text
pcie_7x_0_core_top.v
```

That file is usually generated under:

```text
<project>.gen/sources_1/ip/pcie_7x_0/...
```

It can be overwritten by regenerate output products.

If you must edit generated parameters such as extended capability pointers:

- write down the exact file path
- copy the original file first
- make a minimal edit
- rebuild immediately
- confirm the edit survived before bitstream generation
- do not trust line numbers from another Vivado version

Anything under `.gen` is disposable Vivado output. Expect regeneration to replace it.

Every time you regenerate IP output products:

```text
[ ] Check whether generated wrapper edits still exist
[ ] Check whether capability pointer edits still exist
[ ] Check whether BAR/IP parameters still match the donor plan
[ ] Check whether COE files are still attached to the correct BRAM/ROM IP
[ ] Save a git diff or backup patch
```

Do not trust an old tutorial saying "edit line 450". That line number belongs to somebody else's Vivado version, project path, and generated output.

After regeneration, verify:

```text
Your intended generated-file edit still exists.
IP output products are current.
Git diff shows only expected changes.
```

Something got overwritten if:

```text
Your edit disappeared.
Generated file path changed.
COE reverted to old file.
Vivado upgraded IP unexpectedly.
```

If you see the bad case, stop and fix it before building. A regenerated file silently undoing your work is one of the classic ways people waste days.

### 6.7 Check the Core Settings

Before touching shadow config:

- IP GUI has correct IDs
- BARs match donor type and size
- 64-bit BAR pairing is correct
- output products regenerated
- target Windows readback later shows the expected identity

---

## 7. Shadow Configuration Space

### 7.1 What Shadow Config Space Does

Shadow config space lets the FPGA answer selected PCIe config reads from BRAM data.

Use it for:

- subsystem areas if not handled by IP
- capability structures
- extended capabilities
- donor-like config bytes
- DSN capability bytes

Do not blindly use it to override:

- BAR runtime addresses
- BAR sizing behavior
- Command register
- Status register
- fields already owned by the PCIe IP

> [!NOTE]
> **Under the Hood - why native Xilinx config space is detectable**
>
> The Xilinx 7 Series PCIe IP can enumerate cleanly and still look like a generic FPGA endpoint. Writable bits, RW1C status, capabilities, BAR sizing, and enumeration side effects all have to agree with the donor. Windows walks the chains, writes control bits, clears status, and sizes BARs; it does not stop at VID/DID.

### 7.2 Important Files

| File | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `src/pcileech_fifo.sv` | `rw[203]` shadow read behavior and `rw[206]` shadow write enable |
| `src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv` | Config read/write shadow logic |
| `ip/pcileech_cfgspace.coe` | Shadow config-space data |
| `ip/pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe` | WriteMask data |
| `bram_pcie_cfgspace` | Generated BRAM for config data |
| `drom_pcie_cfgspace_writemask` | Generated ROM for WriteMask |

### 7.3 Enable Shadow Read Data

Open:

```text
src/pcileech_fifo.sv
```

Find:

```systemverilog
rw[202] <= 1'b1; // CFGTLP PROCESSING ENABLE
rw[203] <= 1'b1; // CFGTLP ZERO DATA
rw[204] <= 1'b1; // CFGTLP FILTER TLP FROM USER
rw[205] <= 1'b1; // PCIE BAR PIO ON-BOARD PROCESSING ENABLE
rw[206] <= 1'b0; // CFGTLP PCIE WRITE ENABLE
```

For shadow readback:

```systemverilog
rw[203] <= 1'b0; // return BRAM data instead of zero data
```

If config after the takeover point reads as all zero, check this first.

### 7.4 Building the COE on Windows

Config COE input can come from:

- Arbor exported text
- TeleScan exported/saved data
- manually recorded donor fields
- HxD edited binary/hex data
- a Python script that builds 1024 DWORDs

Manual CSV works for a first test. It is still the weakest capture route.

Better priority order:

1. Re-openable TeleScan capture plus exported config data.
2. Arbor export with offsets preserved.
3. Binary/hex export verified in HxD.
4. Structured offset/DWORD CSV generated from tool data.
5. Manually typed CSV from screenshots.

Do **not** blind append hex lines.

Correct rule:

```text
config byte offset -> exact COE DWORD index
DWORD index = offset / 4
```

If one offset shifts, the whole config image becomes invalid.

Your COE process must catch:

- wrong depth
- wrong endian
- missing `0x34` capability pointer
- missing `0x100` extended capability header when the donor has extended capabilities
- standard capability loops
- extended capability loops
- copied Windows runtime BAR addresses

Never bake a runtime BAR address into static config data. A Device Manager range such as `D0000000-D0003FFF` is the OS allocation for that boot, not COE input.

### 7.5 Little-Endian Rule

PCI config bytes at offset `0x00` may look like:

```text
EC 10 25 81
```

That means:

```text
Vendor ID = 10EC
Device ID = 8125
DWORD for COE = 812510EC
```

If your COE has:

```text
EC102581
```

you probably got byte order wrong.

### 7.6 Minimal Windows Config COE Generator

Create a CSV from your donor notes:

```text
C:/dma/donor/rtl8125/config_dwords.csv
```

Format:

```csv
offset,dword
0x000,812510EC
0x004,00100006
0x008,02000005
0x02C,012310EC
0x034,00000040
0x040,48010001
0x100,00030001
```

Then create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/make_cfgspace_coe.py
```

```python
import csv
import sys

if len(sys.argv) != 3:
    print("Usage: python make_cfgspace_coe.py config_dwords.csv pcileech_cfgspace.coe")
    sys.exit(1)

csv_path = sys.argv[1]
out_path = sys.argv[2]

dwords = ["00000000"] * 1024

with open(csv_path, newline="") as f:
    reader = csv.DictReader(f)
    for row in reader:
        offset = int(row["offset"], 16)
        value = row["dword"].strip().replace("0x", "").replace("0X", "").upper()
        if offset % 4 != 0:
            raise SystemExit(f"Offset not DWORD aligned: 0x{offset:03X}")
        if len(value) != 8:
            raise SystemExit(f"DWORD must be 8 hex digits at 0x{offset:03X}: {value}")
        index = offset // 4
        if index < 0 or index >= 1024:
            raise SystemExit(f"Offset out of 4KB config space: 0x{offset:03X}")
        dwords[index] = value

checks = {
    0x000: "VID/DID",
    0x008: "Class/Revision",
    0x02C: "Subsystem IDs",
    0x034: "Capability Pointer",
    0x100: "Extended Capability Header",
}

print("Validation preview:")
for off, name in checks.items():
    print(f"0x{off:03X} {name}: {dwords[off // 4]}")

with open(out_path, "w", newline="\n") as f:
    f.write("memory_initialization_radix=16;\n")
    f.write("memory_initialization_vector=\n")
    for i, value in enumerate(dwords):
        f.write(value)
        f.write(";\n" if i == len(dwords) - 1 else ",\n")
```

Run in PowerShell:

```powershell
python C:\dma\tools\make_cfgspace_coe.py C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\config_dwords.csv C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\pcileech_cfgspace.coe
```

The generator should print:

```text
0x000 VID/DID: 812510EC
0x008 Class/Revision: 02000005
0x02C Subsystem IDs: 012310EC
0x034 Capability Pointer: 00000040
0x100 Extended Capability Header: 00030001
```

Zeroed identity fields mean stop:

```text
0x000 VID/DID: 00000000
0x008 Class/Revision: 00000000
```

That means your CSV is incomplete or offsets are wrong.

### 7.7 Windows COE Sanity-Check Script

After generating `pcileech_cfgspace.coe`, check it before Vivado. Do not build known-bad config data.

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/check_cfgspace_coe.py
```

```python
import re
import sys

if len(sys.argv) != 2:
    print("Usage: python check_cfgspace_coe.py pcileech_cfgspace.coe")
    sys.exit(1)

text = open(sys.argv[1], "r", encoding="ascii", errors="strict").read()
values = re.findall(r"\b[0-9A-Fa-f]{8}\b", text)
values = [v.upper() for v in values]

if len(values) != 1024:
    raise SystemExit(f"Bad COE depth: expected 1024 DWORDs, got {len(values)}")

def dword(off):
    return values[off // 4]

def u32(off):
    return int(dword(off), 16)

def byte_at(off):
    word = u32(off & ~3)
    return (word >> ((off & 3) * 8)) & 0xFF

print("Key offsets:")
for off, name in [
    (0x000, "VID/DID"),
    (0x004, "Command/Status"),
    (0x008, "Revision/Class"),
    (0x02C, "Subsystem IDs"),
    (0x034, "Capability Pointer"),
    (0x100, "Extended Capability Header"),
]:
    print(f"0x{off:03X} {name}: {dword(off)}")

cap_ptr = byte_at(0x34)
seen = set()
while cap_ptr:
    if cap_ptr in seen:
        raise SystemExit(f"Standard capability loop at 0x{cap_ptr:02X}")
    if cap_ptr < 0x40 or cap_ptr > 0xFC:
        raise SystemExit(f"Suspicious standard capability pointer: 0x{cap_ptr:02X}")
    seen.add(cap_ptr)
    cap_id = byte_at(cap_ptr)
    nxt = byte_at(cap_ptr + 1)
    print(f"CAP 0x{cap_ptr:02X}: id=0x{cap_id:02X} next=0x{nxt:02X}")
    cap_ptr = nxt

ext_ptr = 0x100
seen = set()
while ext_ptr and ext_ptr < 0x1000:
    hdr = u32(ext_ptr)
    if hdr == 0:
        break
    if ext_ptr in seen:
        raise SystemExit(f"Extended capability loop at 0x{ext_ptr:03X}")
    seen.add(ext_ptr)
    ext_id = hdr & 0xFFFF
    nxt = (hdr >> 20) & 0xFFF
    print(f"EXT 0x{ext_ptr:03X}: id=0x{ext_id:04X} next=0x{nxt:03X}")
    if nxt and (nxt < 0x100 or nxt >= 0x1000 or nxt % 4):
        raise SystemExit(f"Bad extended capability next pointer: 0x{nxt:03X}")
    ext_ptr = nxt

for off in range(0x10, 0x28, 4):
    val = u32(off)
    if val & 0xFFFF0000 and not (val & 0x1):
        print(f"WARNING: BAR-looking nonzero value at 0x{off:02X}: {dword(off)}")
        print("         Make sure this is not a copied Windows runtime BAR address.")

print("COE sanity check completed.")
```

Run:

```powershell
python C:\dma\tools\check_cfgspace_coe.py C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\pcileech_cfgspace.coe
```

The checker should finish with:

```text
Key offsets print expected values.
Capability chain prints cleanly.
Extended capability chain prints cleanly or stops cleanly.
COE sanity check completed.
```

Fix the COE if you see:

```text
Bad COE depth
Standard capability loop
Bad extended capability next pointer
0x000 VID/DID: 00000000
WARNING: BAR-looking nonzero value
```

Fix the COE before Vivado. A broken COE does not become good because you generated a bitstream.

### 7.8 HxD Method

HxD is useful when you have a binary or hex dump.

Workflow:

1. Open the dump in HxD
2. Go to offset `0x00`
3. Confirm VID/DID bytes
4. Go to offset `0x08`
5. Confirm revision/class bytes
6. Go to offset `0x2C`
7. Confirm subsystem bytes
8. Go to offset `0x34`
9. Confirm capability pointer
10. Go to offset `0x100`
11. Confirm extended capability header if present

If HxD offsets do not match your notes, your capture/export is not trustworthy.

### 7.9 Replace COE in Vivado

Replace:

```text
ip/pcileech_cfgspace.coe
```

Then in Vivado:

1. Find the BRAM IP using the COE
2. Reset output products if needed
3. Generate output products
4. Confirm no COE file error
5. Rebuild

BRAM regeneration succeeded:

```text
BRAM output products regenerated successfully.
```

The COE or path is broken if:

```text
cannot open COE file
invalid radix
invalid memory_initialization_vector
```

Fix the COE format.

### 7.10 Review the Shadow Image

The shadow image is ready for target testing when:

- `pcileech_cfgspace.coe` is generated by offset
- key offsets `0x00`, `0x08`, `0x2C`, `0x34`, `0x100` are checked
- COE depth is verified as 1024 DWORDs if extended config is used
- endian is verified
- standard capability chain does not loop
- extended capability chain does not loop
- runtime BAR addresses are not blindly copied
- `rw[203]` is correctly set in `pcileech_fifo.sv`
- BRAM output products are regenerated
- target readback in Arbor/TeleScan shows the expected bytes

No readback, no result.

---

## 8. Register Write Protection

### 8.1 Why WriteMask Exists

PCIe config space is neither all read-only nor all writable.

Examples:

- VID/DID should not be writable
- Class Code should not be writable
- Command register must have writable bits
- Status register has RW1C bits
- PMCSR has writable power state bits
- MSI address/data are written by Windows
- MSI-X enable/function mask are written by Windows
- PCIe Device Control has writable bits

If your WriteMask is wrong, Windows may enumerate the device but the driver will still fail.

### 8.2 WriteMask Quality Levels

A beginner mask only proves that the write path is alive.

| Level | Name | Meaning | Verdict |
|------|------|---------|---------|
| 0 | All read-only | Nothing can be written | Wrong for real Windows behavior. Good only to prove static readback. |
| 1 | Beginner test mask | A few obvious fields writable | Link test only. Do not call it donor-correct. |
| 2 | Type 0 header mask | Command/Status and basic header behavior handled better | Good for enumeration testing. Still not enough for many drivers. |
| 3 | Capability-aware mask | PM/MSI/MSI-X/PCIe/AER handled at donor capability offsets | Serious config-space behavior. |
| 4 | Driver-binding mask | Mask behavior refined from Windows driver writes and target readback | Required for stubborn drivers. |

One easy file-name trap:

- Command is not simply "all 16 bits writable".
- Status is not normal writable memory; many bits are RW1C.
- Capability offsets are not fixed across donors.
- MSI, MSI-X, PMCSR, PCIe Device Control, Link Control, and AER must be handled at the donor's actual offsets.
- If you use a beginner mask as final firmware, driver failure is normal.

### 8.3 Enable Shadow Config Writes

Open:

```text
src/pcileech_fifo.sv
```

Set:

```systemverilog
rw[206] <= 1'b1; // CFGTLP PCIE WRITE ENABLE
```

Again: this is `pcileech_fifo.sv`, not `pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv`.

### 8.4 Simple Windows WriteMask COE Generator

This is a bring-up mask, not a PCIe register model.

Treat it as Level 1: path proof, not donor correctness.

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/make_writemask_coe.py
```

```python
import sys

if len(sys.argv) != 2:
    print("Usage: python make_writemask_coe.py pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe")
    sys.exit(1)

out_path = sys.argv[1]

mask = ["00000000"] * 1024

# Type 0 header basics.
mask[0x004 // 4] = "0000FFFF"  # Command/Status beginner mask. Refine per donor.

# BARs: prefer PCIe IP ownership. If shadow owns BARs, do not blindly enable all.
# Leave 0x10-0x24 read-only here unless you know your shadow path owns sizing.

# Interrupt Line at 0x3C low byte can be writable on many devices.
mask[0x03C // 4] = "000000FF"

# Example capability areas. Refine after parsing donor capabilities.
# PMCSR usually sits inside PM capability, not fixed for every donor.
# MSI/MSI-X fields are capability-offset dependent.

with open(out_path, "w", newline="\n") as f:
    f.write("memory_initialization_radix=16;\n")
    f.write("memory_initialization_vector=\n")
    for i, value in enumerate(mask):
        f.write(value)
        f.write(";\n" if i == len(mask) - 1 else ",\n")

print("Generated:", out_path)
print("Check 0x000:", mask[0x000 // 4], "(VID/DID should be read-only)")
print("Check 0x004:", mask[0x004 // 4], "(Command/Status beginner writable bits)")
print("Check 0x008:", mask[0x008 // 4], "(Class/Revision should be read-only)")
```

Run:

```powershell
python C:\dma\tools\make_writemask_coe.py C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe
```

### 8.5 What a Better WriteMask Must Handle

The simple generator is only a starting point.

A serious WriteMask must consider:

| Area | Behavior |
|------|----------|
| `0x00` VID/DID | Read-only |
| `0x04` Command/Status | Command writable bits, Status RW1C |
| `0x08` Class/Revision | Read-only |
| `0x10-0x24` BARs | Usually let PCIe IP handle sizing |
| `0x2C` Subsystem IDs | Usually read-only |
| PM Capability | PMCSR writable bits |
| MSI Capability | MSI enable/address/data writable |
| MSI-X Capability | MSI-X enable/function mask writable |
| PCIe Capability | Device Control and Link Control writable bits |
| AER | Error status RW1C, mask/control writable |

Do not pretend the simple mask is perfect. Test it.

### 8.6 Capability Offsets Are Not Fixed

Do not write a mask that assumes:

```text
PM is always at 0x40
MSI is always at 0x50
PCIe capability is always at 0x60
MSI-X is always at 0x70
```

That layout may match one public tutorial and fail on your donor.

Use the donor capability chain:

```text
0x34 -> first capability -> next -> next -> 0x00
```

Apply masks at the offsets found in that chain, not at offsets copied from another card.

### 8.7 Replace WriteMask COE

Replace:

```text
ip/pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe
```

Then regenerate the ROM/IP in Vivado.

The WriteMask ROM rebuilt:

```text
drom_pcie_cfgspace_writemask output products generated.
```

Fix the source or COE if:

```text
COE parse error
memory vector width mismatch
file not found
```

### 8.8 Windows WriteMask Testing

Windows does not include `setpci`.

Use:

- Arbor, if your version supports controlled config writes
- TeleScan PE, if your version supports config writes
- another trusted PCI config-space editor
- your own lab-only Windows PCI config test tool

Test carefully:

| Test | Expected |
|------|----------|
| Try to write VID/DID | Value must stay unchanged |
| Toggle allowed Command bits | Allowed bits should change |
| Write unsupported Command bits | Unsupported bits should not stick |
| Clear Status RW1C bits | Status behavior should be reasonable |
| Enable MSI/MSI-X if exposed | Control bits should reflect Windows configuration |

WriteMask failures look like:

```text
VID/DID changes after write
Command register never changes
MSI Enable cannot be set
Status bits never clear
Device disappears after config write
```

Those are WriteMask/shadow-write problems, not "just change VID/DID again" problems.

### 8.9 Test the Mask

The mask is ready when:

- `rw[206]` in `pcileech_fifo.sv` is enabled
- WriteMask COE exists
- ROM output products are regenerated
- VID/DID stay read-only
- Command writable bits can change
- Status/RW1C behavior is reasonable
- PMCSR/MSI/MSI-X/PCIe control fields are handled at actual donor offsets if exposed
- driver-related capability writes behave as planned
- Windows target remains stable after controlled writes

---

## 9. BAR Implementation

### 9.1 BAR Is Not Just a Size in Vivado

Vivado BAR settings declare the requested resources; the BAR responder handles the reads and writes. They are separate jobs.

If Windows can assign a BAR but your FPGA returns nothing, the driver can still fail.

### 9.2 BAR Types

Record per BAR:

- enabled/disabled
- memory or I/O
- 32-bit or 64-bit
- prefetchable
- size
- Windows resource range
- MSI-X table/PBA references if any

Do not implement I/O BAR behavior as memory BAR behavior.

### 9.3 BAR Emulation Levels

| Level | Name | Meaning |
|------|------|---------|
| 0 | Nothing | BAR exists but custom response is not meaningful |
| 1 | Zero/static 4KB | Simple Zero4K style BRAM |
| 2 | Static donor-like table | Returns captured/planned values for important offsets |
| 3 | Stateful model | Handles writes, status bits, reset bits, interrupts, queues |

Do not claim Level 3 if you only did Level 1.

### 9.4 Windows BAR Readback Tools

Windows does not expose `/sys/bus/pci/.../resource0`.

Use:

- Arbor BAR/resource read view if available
- TeleScan PE BAR/memory read view if available
- vendor diagnostic tool if it can read MMIO
- your own Windows test driver/tool for lab readback

BAR validation has levels:

| Level | What you proved | What you did not prove |
|------|------------------|------------------------|
| 0 | Device Manager shows Resources | Only BAR allocation. Not BAR response. |
| 1 | First DWORD can be read | One read path works. Not the whole BAR. |
| 2 | First 4KB can be read | Static 4KB response works. Not a larger BAR. |
| 3 | Unsupported offsets are safe | Decode/default path is safer. Not stateful behavior. |
| 4 | Writes and readback work | Some register storage behavior works. Not full device behavior. |
| 5 | Stateful registers behave | Reset/status/interrupt-like behavior is modeled for tested paths. |

A BAR in the Resources tab only proves allocation. It says nothing about the responder.

Minimum BAR tests:

| Test | Expected |
|------|----------|
| Read BAR first DWORD | Completion and stable value |
| Read first 4KB | No timeout, no crash |
| Read unsupported offset | Safe default completion |
| Read high offset for larger BAR | Must work if BAR size is larger than 4KB |
| Write expected control register | Expected state change or safe handling |

BAR path failures look like:

```text
read timeout
all 00000000 when not expected
all FFFFFFFF
random changing values
target freezes
driver fails immediately after BAR read
```

Start with the BAR response path.

### 9.5 Dynamic BAR Response State Machine

Static `case` tables are fine for a first readback test. They are not serious BAR emulation.

A Windows driver writes control bits, rings doorbells, polls status, posts descriptors, masks interrupts, and resets engines. It expects state to move. A BAR module that returns the same hardcoded DWORD forever is Level 2 at best.

#### 9.5.1 Stop Confusing BAR Mailboxes with PCIe VDM

Keep the terminology straight:

| Term | What it really means |
|------|----------------------|
| PCIe VDM | Vendor-Defined Message TLP. This is a PCIe Message transaction type, not a normal BAR MMIO register write. |
| BAR mailbox | Vendor-defined command/status protocol implemented through MMIO registers inside a BAR. This is what most Windows drivers actually use. |
| Doorbell | A BAR write that tells the device to consume descriptors, process a command, or update state. |
| Completion | PCIe response to a read request. A BAR read must complete even when the register is unsupported. |

Actual PCIe VDM support belongs in the TLP RX Message decode. A BAR write is not a PCIe VDM. The example below uses a BAR mailbox because that is what most donor drivers hit first.

Keep the layers separated:

```text
Config space:
  src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv
  - CfgRd0 / CfgWr0
  - identity, capabilities, WriteMask

BAR space:
  src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
  - MemRd / MemWr
  - mailbox, doorbell, status, stream counters

Interrupt/control context:
  src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv
  - MSI/MSI-X enable state
  - cfg_interrupt path
```

Keep shadow config and BAR state separate. Config carries identity; the BAR model carries runtime behavior.

#### 9.5.2 Register Map for a Dynamic BAR Mailbox

The example below is a small vendor-defined BAR protocol. Replace its register map with the donor BAR dump and driver trace.

| Offset | Name | Access | Behavior |
|--------|------|--------|----------|
| `0x000` | `DEVICE_SIGNATURE` | RO | Stable donor-like signature |
| `0x004` | `VERSION_CAPS` | RO | Version and capability bits |
| `0x008` | `STATUS` | RO | Ready, busy, IRQ pending, stream mode, error |
| `0x00C` | `CONTROL` | RW | Enable, software reset, IRQ acknowledge, loopback, stream mode |
| `0x010` | `DOORBELL` | WO | Starts command processing |
| `0x014` | `HOST_MSG_LO` | RW | Host command payload low DWORD |
| `0x018` | `HOST_MSG_HI` | RW | Host command payload high DWORD |
| `0x01C` | `HOST_MSG_LEN` | RW | Payload length or descriptor count |
| `0x020` | `RESP_LO` | RO | Device response low DWORD |
| `0x024` | `RESP_HI` | RO | Device response high DWORD |
| `0x028` | `STREAM_COUNTER` | RO | Advances while enabled |
| `0x02C` | `PACKET_COUNTER` | RO | Increments after processed network-like doorbells |
| `0x030` | `AUDIO_FRAME_COUNTER` | RO | Increments in stream mode |
| `0x034` | `IRQ_STATUS` | RW1C-ish | Pending event bits |
| `0x038` | `IRQ_MASK` | RW | Interrupt mask |
| `0x03C` | `ERROR_STATUS` | RW1C-ish | Sticky error bits |

Writes must change state, reads must expose it, status must advance, and unsupported offsets must complete safely.

#### 9.5.3 Drop-In SystemVerilog BAR State Machine

Same port shape as the example BAR implementations in `src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv`.

Use it as a replacement for a selected BAR implementation:

```systemverilog
pcileech_bar_impl_dynamic_mailbox i_bar0(
    .rst            ( rst                           ),
    .clk            ( clk                           ),
    .wr_addr        ( wr_addr                       ),
    .wr_be          ( wr_be                         ),
    .wr_data        ( wr_data                       ),
    .wr_valid       ( wr_valid && wr_bar[0]         ),
    .rd_req_ctx     ( rd_req_ctx                    ),
    .rd_req_addr    ( rd_req_addr                   ),
    .rd_req_valid   ( rd_req_valid && rd_req_bar[0] ),
    .rd_rsp_ctx     ( bar_rsp_ctx[0]                ),
    .rd_rsp_data    ( bar_rsp_data[0]               ),
    .rd_rsp_valid   ( bar_rsp_valid[0]              )
);
```

Full module:

```systemverilog
// ------------------------------------------------------------------------
// Dynamic BAR mailbox/state model.
//
// File target:
//   src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
//
// Purpose:
//   Replace static read-only case tables with deterministic stateful BAR
//   behavior. This keeps config-shadow logic independent while allowing
//   host BAR writes to update later BAR read responses.
//
// Latency:
//   Read response is returned from a registered request path.
// ------------------------------------------------------------------------
module pcileech_bar_impl_dynamic_mailbox(
    input               rst,
    input               clk,

    input [31:0]        wr_addr,
    input [3:0]         wr_be,
    input [31:0]        wr_data,
    input               wr_valid,

    input [87:0]        rd_req_ctx,
    input [31:0]        rd_req_addr,
    input               rd_req_valid,

    output bit [87:0]   rd_rsp_ctx,
    output bit [31:0]   rd_rsp_data,
    output bit          rd_rsp_valid
);

    localparam [31:0] DEVICE_SIGNATURE_RESET = 32'h50414D44; // bytes 44 4D 41 50 = "DMAP"
    localparam [31:0] VERSION_CAPS_RESET     = 32'h0001_0007;

    localparam [11:0] REG_DEVICE_SIGNATURE   = 12'h000;
    localparam [11:0] REG_VERSION_CAPS       = 12'h004;
    localparam [11:0] REG_STATUS             = 12'h008;
    localparam [11:0] REG_CONTROL            = 12'h00C;
    localparam [11:0] REG_DOORBELL           = 12'h010;
    localparam [11:0] REG_HOST_MSG_LO        = 12'h014;
    localparam [11:0] REG_HOST_MSG_HI        = 12'h018;
    localparam [11:0] REG_HOST_MSG_LEN       = 12'h01C;
    localparam [11:0] REG_RESP_LO            = 12'h020;
    localparam [11:0] REG_RESP_HI            = 12'h024;
    localparam [11:0] REG_STREAM_COUNTER     = 12'h028;
    localparam [11:0] REG_PACKET_COUNTER     = 12'h02C;
    localparam [11:0] REG_AUDIO_FRAME_COUNTER= 12'h030;
    localparam [11:0] REG_IRQ_STATUS         = 12'h034;
    localparam [11:0] REG_IRQ_MASK           = 12'h038;
    localparam [11:0] REG_ERROR_STATUS       = 12'h03C;

    localparam [7:0]  PROC_IDLE              = 8'd0;
    localparam [7:0]  PROC_SHORT             = 8'd8;
    localparam [7:0]  PROC_MEDIUM            = 8'd32;
    localparam [7:0]  PROC_LONG              = 8'd96;

    bit [31:0] control_reg;
    bit [31:0] host_msg_lo;
    bit [31:0] host_msg_hi;
    bit [31:0] host_msg_len;
    bit [31:0] response_lo;
    bit [31:0] response_hi;
    bit [31:0] stream_counter;
    bit [31:0] packet_counter;
    bit [31:0] audio_frame_counter;
    bit [31:0] irq_status;
    bit [31:0] irq_mask;
    bit [31:0] error_status;
    bit [31:0] last_doorbell;
    bit [7:0]  process_timer;
    bit [7:0]  reset_timer;

    bit [87:0] rd_req_ctx_d;
    bit [31:0] rd_req_addr_d;
    bit        rd_req_valid_d;

    wire control_enable      = control_reg[0];
    wire control_loopback    = control_reg[3];
    wire control_stream_mode = control_reg[4];
    wire engine_busy         = (process_timer != PROC_IDLE);
    wire reset_busy          = (reset_timer != 8'd0);
    wire irq_pending         = ((irq_status & irq_mask) != 32'd0);

    function automatic [31:0] apply_wstrb;
        input [31:0] old_value;
        input [31:0] new_value;
        input [3:0]  byte_enable;
        begin
            apply_wstrb = old_value;
            if (byte_enable[0]) apply_wstrb[7:0]   = new_value[7:0];
            if (byte_enable[1]) apply_wstrb[15:8]  = new_value[15:8];
            if (byte_enable[2]) apply_wstrb[23:16] = new_value[23:16];
            if (byte_enable[3]) apply_wstrb[31:24] = new_value[31:24];
        end
    endfunction

    function automatic [31:0] make_status;
        begin
            make_status = 32'd0;
            make_status[0]  = 1'b1;                 // ready
            make_status[1]  = engine_busy;          // busy
            make_status[2]  = irq_pending;          // interrupt pending
            make_status[3]  = control_enable;       // engine enabled
            make_status[4]  = control_stream_mode;  // stream mode
            make_status[5]  = reset_busy;           // reset in progress
            make_status[6]  = (error_status != 0);  // sticky error present
            make_status[15:8]  = process_timer;
            make_status[31:16] = packet_counter[15:0];
        end
    endfunction

    function automatic [31:0] read_register;
        input [11:0] offset;
        begin
            case (offset)
                REG_DEVICE_SIGNATURE:    read_register = DEVICE_SIGNATURE_RESET;
                REG_VERSION_CAPS:        read_register = VERSION_CAPS_RESET;
                REG_STATUS:              read_register = make_status();
                REG_CONTROL:             read_register = control_reg;
                REG_DOORBELL:            read_register = last_doorbell;
                REG_HOST_MSG_LO:         read_register = host_msg_lo;
                REG_HOST_MSG_HI:         read_register = host_msg_hi;
                REG_HOST_MSG_LEN:        read_register = host_msg_len;
                REG_RESP_LO:             read_register = response_lo;
                REG_RESP_HI:             read_register = response_hi;
                REG_STREAM_COUNTER:      read_register = stream_counter;
                REG_PACKET_COUNTER:      read_register = packet_counter;
                REG_AUDIO_FRAME_COUNTER: read_register = audio_frame_counter;
                REG_IRQ_STATUS:          read_register = irq_status;
                REG_IRQ_MASK:            read_register = irq_mask;
                REG_ERROR_STATUS:        read_register = error_status;
                default:                 read_register = 32'h00000000;
            endcase
        end
    endfunction

    task automatic start_processing;
        input [31:0] doorbell_value;
        begin
            last_doorbell <= doorbell_value;

            if (!control_enable) begin
                error_status <= error_status | 32'h00000001;
                irq_status   <= irq_status   | 32'h00000004;
                process_timer <= PROC_IDLE;
            end else if (engine_busy) begin
                error_status <= error_status | 32'h00000002;
                irq_status   <= irq_status   | 32'h00000004;
            end else begin
                if (host_msg_len[15:0] <= 16'd64) begin
                    process_timer <= PROC_SHORT;
                end else if (host_msg_len[15:0] <= 16'd1500) begin
                    process_timer <= PROC_MEDIUM;
                end else begin
                    process_timer <= PROC_LONG;
                end

                response_lo <= host_msg_lo ^ doorbell_value ^ 32'hA5A5_5A5A;
                response_hi <= host_msg_hi + host_msg_len + 32'h0000_1001;
            end
        end
    endtask

    task automatic complete_processing;
        begin
            packet_counter <= packet_counter + 1'b1;

            if (control_stream_mode) begin
                audio_frame_counter <= audio_frame_counter + host_msg_len[15:0];
                response_lo <= response_lo + 32'h0000_0040;
                response_hi <= response_hi ^ 32'h55AA_00FF;
            end else begin
                response_lo <= response_lo + 32'h0000_0001;
                response_hi <= response_hi + packet_counter + 32'h0000_0001;
            end

            if (control_loopback) begin
                response_lo <= host_msg_lo;
                response_hi <= host_msg_hi;
            end

            irq_status <= irq_status | 32'h00000001;
        end
    endtask

    always @ (posedge clk) begin
        if (rst) begin
            control_reg         <= 32'd0;
            host_msg_lo         <= 32'd0;
            host_msg_hi         <= 32'd0;
            host_msg_len        <= 32'd0;
            response_lo         <= 32'd0;
            response_hi         <= 32'd0;
            stream_counter      <= 32'd0;
            packet_counter      <= 32'd0;
            audio_frame_counter <= 32'd0;
            irq_status          <= 32'd0;
            irq_mask            <= 32'd0;
            error_status        <= 32'd0;
            last_doorbell       <= 32'd0;
            process_timer       <= PROC_IDLE;
            reset_timer         <= 8'd0;
            rd_req_ctx_d        <= 88'd0;
            rd_req_addr_d       <= 32'd0;
            rd_req_valid_d      <= 1'b0;
            rd_rsp_ctx          <= 88'd0;
            rd_rsp_data         <= 32'd0;
            rd_rsp_valid        <= 1'b0;
        end else begin
            rd_req_ctx_d   <= rd_req_ctx;
            rd_req_addr_d  <= rd_req_addr;
            rd_req_valid_d <= rd_req_valid;

            rd_rsp_ctx     <= rd_req_ctx_d;
            rd_rsp_data    <= read_register(rd_req_addr_d[11:0]);
            rd_rsp_valid   <= rd_req_valid_d;

            if (control_enable && !reset_busy) begin
                stream_counter <= stream_counter + 1'b1;
            end

            if (reset_timer != 8'd0) begin
                reset_timer <= reset_timer - 1'b1;
                if (reset_timer == 8'd1) begin
                    control_reg[1]      <= 1'b0;
                    process_timer       <= PROC_IDLE;
                    response_lo         <= 32'd0;
                    response_hi         <= 32'd0;
                    irq_status          <= irq_status | 32'h00000002;
                    error_status        <= 32'd0;
                end
            end

            if (process_timer != PROC_IDLE) begin
                process_timer <= process_timer - 1'b1;
                if (process_timer == 8'd1) begin
                    complete_processing();
                end
            end

            if (wr_valid) begin
                case (wr_addr[11:0])
                    REG_CONTROL: begin
                        control_reg <= apply_wstrb(control_reg, wr_data, wr_be);

                        if (wr_be[0] && wr_data[1]) begin
                            reset_timer <= 8'd32;
                            control_reg[1] <= 1'b1;
                        end

                        if (wr_be[0] && wr_data[2]) begin
                            irq_status <= 32'd0;
                        end
                    end

                    REG_DOORBELL: begin
                        start_processing(wr_data);
                    end

                    REG_HOST_MSG_LO: begin
                        host_msg_lo <= apply_wstrb(host_msg_lo, wr_data, wr_be);
                    end

                    REG_HOST_MSG_HI: begin
                        host_msg_hi <= apply_wstrb(host_msg_hi, wr_data, wr_be);
                    end

                    REG_HOST_MSG_LEN: begin
                        host_msg_len <= apply_wstrb(host_msg_len, wr_data, wr_be);
                    end

                    REG_IRQ_STATUS: begin
                        irq_status <= irq_status & ~apply_wstrb(32'd0, wr_data, wr_be);
                    end

                    REG_IRQ_MASK: begin
                        irq_mask <= apply_wstrb(irq_mask, wr_data, wr_be);
                    end

                    REG_ERROR_STATUS: begin
                        error_status <= error_status & ~apply_wstrb(32'd0, wr_data, wr_be);
                    end

                    default: begin
                        error_status <= error_status | 32'h80000000;
                    end
                endcase
            end
        end
    end

endmodule
```

`case` remains only as the address decoder. Returned data comes from host writes, timers, control/reset state, interrupt state, stream mode, and prior doorbells.

#### 9.5.4 End-to-End MRd to CplD Closure

Trace this path before debugging a driver handshake.

```text
Windows kernel driver
    |
    | Memory Read TLP (MRd)
    | - requester ID
    | - tag
    | - byte enables
    | - BAR hit address
    v
Motherboard Root Complex
    |
    v
Xilinx 7-Series PCIe Hard IP
    |
    | RX AXI-Stream from PCIe core
    | src/pcileech_pcie_a7.sv
    |
    | .m_axis_rx_tdata  -> tlp_rx.data
    | .m_axis_rx_tkeep  -> tlp_rx.keep
    | .m_axis_rx_tlast  -> tlp_rx.last
    | .m_axis_rx_tvalid -> tlp_rx.valid
    v
PCILeech TLP router
    |
    | src/pcileech_pcie_tlp_a7.sv
    | pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller i_pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller
    v
BAR read engine
    |
    | src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
    | pcileech_tlps128_bar_rdengine
    |
    | rd_req_valid = 1
    | rd_req_bar[0] = 1
    | rd_req_addr = decoded BAR offset
    | rd_req_ctx carries requester/tag/length/low address metadata
    v
Dynamic BAR model
    |
    | pcileech_bar_impl_dynamic_mailbox
    | rd_req_addr[11:0] == REG_DEVICE_SIGNATURE
    | read_register(REG_DEVICE_SIGNATURE) = 32'h50414D44
    | bytes on the bus = 44 4D 41 50 = "DMAP"
    v
Latency shaping
    |
    | pcileech_bar_latency_pipe #(.LATENCY_CLKS(16))
    | makes the completion timing less toy-like and easier to tune
    v
BAR read completion engine
    |
    | src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
    | rd_rsp_ctx / rd_rsp_data / rd_rsp_valid
    | pcileech_tlps128_bar_rdengine preserves original requester tag
    v
PCILeech TX mux
    |
    | src/pcileech_pcie_tlp_a7.sv
    | tlps_bar_rsp -> pcileech_tlps128_sink_mux1 -> tlps_tx
    v
Xilinx PCIe TX path
    |
    | Completion with Data (CplD TLP)
    | original tag returned
    | payload DWORD returned
    v
Windows kernel driver receives the MMIO read result
```

`rd_req_ctx` is not optional. With multiple reads outstanding, the completion needs the original tag and requester context.

For `REG_DEVICE_SIGNATURE`, the state-machine hit is:

```systemverilog
localparam [11:0] REG_DEVICE_SIGNATURE = 12'h000;

function automatic [31:0] read_register;
    input [11:0] offset;
    begin
        case (offset)
            REG_DEVICE_SIGNATURE: read_register = 32'h50414D44;
            default:              read_register = 32'h00000000;
        endcase
    end
endfunction
```

That returns the DWORD `0x50414D44`. On the byte lane it reads as:

```text
44 4D 41 50 = "DMAP"
```

If your Windows BAR read tool shows `444D4150` instead, your display tool is showing byte-swapped DWORD text. Check the raw byte view before blaming the FPGA.

To put the 16-clock timing shaper into the actual BAR0 path, split the raw dynamic model output from the final BAR response output:

```systemverilog
wire [87:0] bar0_raw_rsp_ctx;
wire [31:0] bar0_raw_rsp_data;
wire        bar0_raw_rsp_valid;

pcileech_bar_impl_dynamic_mailbox i_bar0_raw(
    .rst            ( rst                           ),
    .clk            ( clk                           ),
    .wr_addr        ( wr_addr                       ),
    .wr_be          ( wr_be                         ),
    .wr_data        ( wr_data                       ),
    .wr_valid       ( wr_valid && wr_bar[0]         ),
    .rd_req_ctx     ( rd_req_ctx                    ),
    .rd_req_addr    ( rd_req_addr                   ),
    .rd_req_valid   ( rd_req_valid && rd_req_bar[0] ),
    .rd_rsp_ctx     ( bar0_raw_rsp_ctx              ),
    .rd_rsp_data    ( bar0_raw_rsp_data             ),
    .rd_rsp_valid   ( bar0_raw_rsp_valid            )
);

pcileech_bar_latency_pipe #(
    .LATENCY_CLKS(16)
) i_bar0_latency (
    .rst            ( rst                ),
    .clk            ( clk                ),
    .rd_req_ctx     ( bar0_raw_rsp_ctx   ),
    .rd_req_data    ( bar0_raw_rsp_data  ),
    .rd_req_valid   ( bar0_raw_rsp_valid ),
    .rd_rsp_ctx     ( bar_rsp_ctx[0]     ),
    .rd_rsp_data    ( bar_rsp_data[0]    ),
    .rd_rsp_valid   ( bar_rsp_valid[0]   )
);
```

Then `pcileech_tlps128_bar_rdengine` does the packet closure work:

```text
rd_rsp_ctx   -> requester ID, tag, byte count, lower address
rd_rsp_data  -> byte-swapped into CplD payload ordering
rd_rsp_valid -> emits the completion beat
tlps_out     -> forwarded as tlps_bar_rsp
```

In current upstream-style code, the BAR response path feeds the TX mux like this:

```systemverilog
// File: src/pcileech_pcie_tlp_a7.sv
pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller i_pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller(
    .rst            ( rst                           ),
    .clk            ( clk                           ),
    .bar_en         ( dshadow2fifo.bar_en           ),
    .tlps_in        ( tlps_rx                       ),
    .tlps_out       ( tlps_bar_rsp.source           )
);

pcileech_tlps128_sink_mux1 i_pcileech_tlps128_sink_mux1(
    .rst            ( rst                           ),
    .clk            ( clk                           ),
    .tlps_out       ( tlps_tx                       ),
    .tlps_in1       ( tlps_cfg_rsp.sink             ),
    .tlps_in2       ( tlps_bar_rsp.sink             ),
    .tlps_in3       ( tlps_rx_fifo.sink             ),
    .tlps_in4       ( tlps_static                   )
);
```

Packet path:

```text
MRd tag enters on RX.
rd_req_ctx preserves the tag.
BAR model chooses the payload.
latency pipe shapes the response timing.
rdengine emits CplD with the original tag.
pcileech_pcie_tlp_a7.sv muxes it back to the PCIe TX path.
driver receives the exact response for its original outstanding read.
```

A wrong tag associates the completion with the wrong outstanding read. No `rd_rsp_valid` leaves the root complex waiting for timeout. Static payload where the driver expects status movement kills the handshake in software.

#### 9.5.5 Dynamic BAR Validation

Test it like this:

```text
1. Read 0x000 DEVICE_SIGNATURE.
2. Read 0x008 STATUS. Ready should be set, busy should be clear.
3. Write 0x038 IRQ_MASK = 00000007.
4. Write HOST_MSG_LO / HOST_MSG_HI / HOST_MSG_LEN.
5. Write 0x00C CONTROL bit0 = 1.
6. Write 0x010 DOORBELL.
7. Poll 0x008 STATUS until busy clears.
8. Read RESP_LO / RESP_HI.
9. Read PACKET_COUNTER.
10. Write 0x034 IRQ_STATUS with the pending bits to clear them.
```

The transaction path is healthy when:

```text
STATUS busy bit toggles.
RESP_LO/RESP_HI change after doorbell.
PACKET_COUNTER increments.
IRQ_STATUS sets after command completion.
RW1C-style clear works for IRQ_STATUS and ERROR_STATUS.
Unsupported writes do not crash the target.
```

Go back to the responder if:

```text
STATUS never changes.
DOORBELL write has no effect.
Read completion times out.
RESP values are the same before and after command processing.
IRQ_STATUS cannot clear.
BAR read freezes the machine.
```

If the driver sends a BAR handshake and gets a flat static table, implement the state machine or document the missing behavior.

### 9.6 BAR Test Record

Record at least:

- Windows resources show the expected BAR ranges
- Arbor/TeleScan can read tested BAR offsets
- first DWORD read is stable
- first 4KB read is stable if using Zero4K
- unsupported offsets do not kill the machine
- write/readback behavior is tested for registers that need it
- high offsets are tested for BARs larger than 4KB
- MSI-X table/PBA area is handled if MSI-X is exposed
- BAR validation level is documented

---

## 10. Capability Structure Setup

### 10.1 Standard Capability Chain

Standard capability pointer is at:

```text
0x34
```

Each capability has:

```text
byte 0 = Capability ID
byte 1 = Next Pointer
```

Common IDs:

| ID | Name |
|----|------|
| `0x01` | Power Management |
| `0x05` | MSI |
| `0x10` | PCI Express |
| `0x11` | MSI-X |
| `0x09` | Vendor Specific |

A broken capability chain often looks like:

```text
0x40 -> 0x60 -> 0x40
```

That is a loop. Fix it before Windows walks the chain.

### 10.2 Extended Capability Chain

Extended capabilities start at:

```text
0x100
```

Common IDs:

| ID | Name |
|----|------|
| `0x0001` | Advanced Error Reporting |
| `0x0003` | Device Serial Number |
| `0x0018` | Latency Tolerance Reporting |
| `0x001E` | L1 PM Substates |

If your shadow COE only covers 256 bytes, extended capabilities are missing. That is not a complete donor clone.

### 10.3 DSN

DSN in PCILeech 7 Series style projects is commonly driven here:

```text
src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv
```

Look for:

```systemverilog
rw[127:64] <= 64'h0000000101000A35; // cfg_dsn
```

Set it to donor DSN only if donor has DSN and you have verified byte order.

Also make sure the shadow extended capability bytes agree. If `cfg_dsn` says one value and config-space DSN says another, you created a contradiction.

### 10.4 MSI and MSI-X

MSI:

- config-space fields are written by Windows
- WriteMask must allow correct fields
- driver may fail if MSI enable cannot stick

MSI-X:

- capability lives in config space
- MSI-X table lives in BAR memory
- PBA lives in BAR memory
- Windows writes table entries

If you expose MSI-X but do not implement the table/PBA BAR region, expect driver failure.

### 10.5 PMCSR

Power Management is not decoration.

PMCSR can affect:

- D0/D3 state
- PME enable
- PME status
- driver resume/start behavior

Static config bytes with no writable PMCSR behavior can be enough to enumerate but fail driver start.

### 10.6 Capability Sanity Check

Before moving into driver behavior, check:

- standard chain walks cleanly in Arbor/TeleScan
- extended chain walks cleanly if present
- DSN is present/absent consistently
- MSI/MSI-X fields match donor plan
- MSI-X table/PBA BAR region is handled if exposed
- PMCSR writable behavior is considered
- Windows target readback matches the plan

---

## 11. TLP Response Implementation

### 11.1 Enumeration Is Only the Start

Config space gets the endpoint enumerated. BAR and TLP behavior determine what happens when real software touches it.

Drivers read BAR registers to decide whether the device is real. If your BAR logic returns invalid data, zeros, all F, or no completion, you will see Code 10, driver start failure, or crashes.

### 11.2 Where BAR Routing Lives

Common upstream-style location:

```text
src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
```

This routes BAR reads/writes to responder logic.

Do not paste random snippets unless they match the current module ports and signals.

### 11.3 Pseudocode Trap

Many public snippets use fake or old signal names:

```systemverilog
base_address_register
drd_req_addr
```

If those signals do not exist in your file, the snippet is not compile-ready.

A compile-ready example needs:

- full module context
- correct ports
- correct BAR index
- correct offset calculation
- correct latency
- correct completion path
- successful build proof

### 11.4 Stateful Behavior Examples

Real drivers may expect:

- reset bit self-clears
- status bit changes after reset
- interrupt mask register stores writes
- EEPROM/NVM window returns specific values
- MAC address appears in a device-specific location
- MSI-X table writes stick
- queue/doorbell registers behave safely

If your donor driver reads these and gets nonsense, Code 10 is normal.

### 11.5 When the Driver Does Not Bind

If driver binding fails, stop changing VID/DID.

Check:

- BAR readback
- MSI/MSI-X
- PMCSR
- EEPROM/NVM window
- reset bit
- status bit
- interrupt mask
- Device Manager Events
- Windows Event Viewer if needed

Once identity is correct, VID/DID is no longer the variable.

### 11.6 Completion Latency Shaping

BAR data is only half the job. Timing matters too.

Real devices do not answer every MMIO read with one permanent pattern. Reads may depend on state or settle after reset. A fixed DWORD with fixed timing proves the completion path is alive; it does not model the device.

Use the real upstream-style files:

| File | What to touch |
|------|---------------|
| `src/pcileech_pcie_a7.sv` | Xilinx 7 Series PCIe wrapper. RX from the core is commonly wired as `m_axis_rx_tdata` into `tlp_rx.data`. |
| `src/pcileech_pcie_tlp_a7.sv` | TLP pipeline around RX/TX handling. |
| `src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv` | BAR routing and BAR responder selection. This is the usual place for BAR behavior work. |
| `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv` | Config/control context and PCIe interrupt interface signals. |

Critical rule from `pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv`: user BAR responder cores must keep a known read latency. Do not make BAR0 two clocks, BAR1 random, and BAR2 instant unless you understand the completion mux and timing.

A clean way to add controlled latency is to pipeline the response context/data after your BAR logic has produced a DWORD:

```systemverilog
// Drop this helper near the BAR implementation area in:
// src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
//
// Keep LATENCY_CLKS consistent with the rest of your BAR responders.
// 16 clocks at 62.5 MHz is about 256 ns. Microsecond-level behavior
// needs tens or hundreds of clocks depending on your PCIe user clock.
module pcileech_bar_latency_pipe #(
    parameter integer LATENCY_CLKS = 16
)(
    input               rst,
    input               clk,

    input  [87:0]       rd_req_ctx,
    input  [31:0]       rd_req_data,
    input               rd_req_valid,

    output bit [87:0]   rd_rsp_ctx,
    output bit [31:0]   rd_rsp_data,
    output bit          rd_rsp_valid
);

    bit [87:0] ctx_pipe   [0:LATENCY_CLKS-1];
    bit [31:0] data_pipe  [0:LATENCY_CLKS-1];
    bit        valid_pipe [0:LATENCY_CLKS-1];
    integer i;

    always @ (posedge clk) begin
        if (rst) begin
            for (i = 0; i < LATENCY_CLKS; i = i + 1) begin
                ctx_pipe[i]   <= 88'd0;
                data_pipe[i]  <= 32'd0;
                valid_pipe[i] <= 1'b0;
            end
        end else begin
            ctx_pipe[0]   <= rd_req_ctx;
            data_pipe[0]  <= rd_req_data;
            valid_pipe[0] <= rd_req_valid;

            for (i = 1; i < LATENCY_CLKS; i = i + 1) begin
                ctx_pipe[i]   <= ctx_pipe[i-1];
                data_pipe[i]  <= data_pipe[i-1];
                valid_pipe[i] <= valid_pipe[i-1];
            end
        end
    end

    always @ (*) begin
        rd_rsp_ctx   = ctx_pipe[LATENCY_CLKS-1];
        rd_rsp_data  = data_pipe[LATENCY_CLKS-1];
        rd_rsp_valid = valid_pipe[LATENCY_CLKS-1];
    end

endmodule
```

Use it inside a real BAR implementation, not as a random top-level patch:

```systemverilog
wire [87:0] raw_rsp_ctx;
wire [31:0] raw_rsp_data;
wire        raw_rsp_valid;

// Your donor-specific register decode produces raw_rsp_* first.
// Then the latency pipe shapes the external completion timing.
pcileech_bar_latency_pipe #(
    .LATENCY_CLKS(16)
) i_bar0_latency (
    .rst            ( rst           ),
    .clk            ( clk           ),
    .rd_req_ctx     ( raw_rsp_ctx   ),
    .rd_req_data    ( raw_rsp_data  ),
    .rd_req_valid   ( raw_rsp_valid ),
    .rd_rsp_ctx     ( rd_rsp_ctx    ),
    .rd_rsp_data    ( rd_rsp_data   ),
    .rd_rsp_valid   ( rd_rsp_valid  )
);
```

If you add this to one exposed BAR, normalize the other exposed responders or prove they never participate in the same path. The existing example cores are often two-clock responders; mixing active responders with different unknown latencies is a debugging trap.

Start with fixed delay classes:

| Register type | Practical lab delay model |
|---------------|---------------------------|
| simple status/capability read | fixed short delay |
| reset/status transition | delay until your reset state machine completes |
| EEPROM/NVM-like window | longer fixed delay or staged ready bit |
| queue/doorbell register | write stores state, readback follows donor behavior |

Do not blindly add random jitter to config reads. If the host is sizing BARs, walking capabilities, or clearing status bits during early enumeration, inconsistent timing can turn a normal bug into a POST hang.

### 11.7 Interrupt Activity Heartbeat for Lab Driver Validation

Interrupts are not decoration. If the donor driver expects MSI/MSI-X activity and your firmware never drives the interrupt path, a driver bind can still fail or look dead under normal workload.

Not a substitute for real device logic. Use it as a lab heartbeat for the PCIe interrupt path, Windows driver event path, and config/MSI wiring.

> [!NOTE]
> **Do not confuse the two `rw[206]` locations**
>
> `src/pcileech_fifo.sv` uses `rw[206]` for config-shadow write enable. `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv` also has a local `rw[206]`, but there it drives `ctx.cfg_interrupt`. Same index, different module context. Editing the wrong one is how old tutorials create fake fixes.

Patch this into the existing update path of `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv`. Do not create multiple always blocks that drive the same `rw[]` bits.

```systemverilog
// Lab interrupt heartbeat for MSI path validation.
// File: src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv
//
// Integrate into the existing rw[] update path. Do not double-drive
// rw[205], rw[206], rw[207], rw[199:192], or rw[204:200].

localparam integer IRQ_HEARTBEAT_CLKS = 32'd6_250_000; // ~100 ms at 62.5 MHz

bit [31:0] irq_heartbeat_ctr;
bit [3:0]  irq_pulse_ctr;

always @ (posedge clk) begin
    if (rst) begin
        irq_heartbeat_ctr <= 32'd0;
        irq_pulse_ctr     <= 4'd0;

        rw[199:192] <= 8'h00; // cfg_interrupt_di
        rw[204:200] <= 5'd0;  // cfg_pciecap_interrupt_msgnum
        rw[205]     <= 1'b0;  // cfg_interrupt_assert
        rw[206]     <= 1'b0;  // cfg_interrupt
        rw[207]     <= 1'b0;  // cfg_interrupt_stat
    end else begin
        rw[205] <= 1'b0;
        rw[206] <= 1'b0;
        rw[207] <= 1'b0;

        if (ctx.cfg_interrupt_msienable && ctx.cfg_interrupt_rdy) begin
            if (irq_heartbeat_ctr == IRQ_HEARTBEAT_CLKS) begin
                irq_heartbeat_ctr <= 32'd0;
                irq_pulse_ctr     <= 4'd4;
            end else begin
                irq_heartbeat_ctr <= irq_heartbeat_ctr + 1'b1;
            end

            if (irq_pulse_ctr != 0) begin
                irq_pulse_ctr <= irq_pulse_ctr - 1'b1;

                rw[199:192] <= 8'h00; // MSI data/vector input
                rw[204:200] <= 5'd0;  // interrupt message number
                rw[206]     <= 1'b1;  // one-cycle cfg_interrupt pulse
            end
        end else begin
            irq_heartbeat_ctr <= 32'd0;
            irq_pulse_ctr     <= 4'd0;
        end
    end
end
```

Important limits:

- This validates the interrupt path; it does not make your BAR model correct.
- MSI-X is not "done" just because an interrupt pulse exists.
- If MSI-X is exposed, the BAR that contains the MSI-X table and PBA must behave correctly.
- If the donor only raises interrupts after queue setup, a blind heartbeat can look wrong. Gate it behind a real BAR write if your donor behavior needs that.
- Save Windows Event Viewer, driver logs, and Arbor/TeleScan readback after testing. No readback means no proof.

### 11.8 TLP Lifecycle and PMCSR State Alignment

Static IDs are the easy part. The endpoint still has to behave consistently under real PCIe transactions.

The transaction lifecycle cannot contradict the config space, BAR behavior, power state, or interrupt plan.

#### 11.8.1 TLP Lifecycle Inside the FPGA

A Type 0 PCIe endpoint sees three practical transaction families during early bring-up:

```text
Host Root Complex
    |
    | 1. CfgRd0 / CfgWr0
    v
Xilinx 7 Series PCIe IP
    |
    | m_axis_rx_tdata / tlp_rx.data
    v
PCILeech TLP pipeline
    |
    +--> Config TLP path
    |       src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv
    |       - CfgRd0 returns shadow config data
    |       - CfgWr0 updates shadow data through WriteMask
    |
    +--> BAR path
    |       src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
    |       - MemRd routes to selected BAR model
    |       - MemWr updates BAR model state
    |
    +--> Interrupt/control context
            src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv
            - MSI/MSI-X enable state
            - PMCSR state from core context
            - function-level reset and link state signals
```

The important decode already exists in current upstream-style PCILeech files:

```systemverilog
// File: src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv
wire pcie_rx_rden = tlps_in.tvalid
                  && tlps_in.tuser[0]
                  && (tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0000010); // CfgRd0/CfgRd1

wire pcie_rx_wren = tlps_in.tvalid
                  && tlps_in.tuser[0]
                  && (tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0100010); // CfgWr0/CfgWr1

wire [9:0]  pcie_rx_addr  = tlps_in.tdata[75:66];
wire [31:0] pcie_rx_data  = tlps_in.tdata[127:96];
wire [3:0]  pcie_rx_be    = {tlps_in.tdata[32], tlps_in.tdata[33], tlps_in.tdata[34], tlps_in.tdata[35]};
```

BAR reads/writes then move through:

```text
src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv

MemRd TLP -> read engine -> rd_req_valid / rd_req_bar / rd_req_addr
selected BAR model -> rd_rsp_ctx / rd_rsp_data / rd_rsp_valid
completion engine -> Completion with Data

MemWr TLP -> write engine -> wr_valid / wr_bar / wr_addr / wr_be / wr_data
selected BAR model -> state update
```

The firmware must keep these answers coherent:

| Host action | Firmware behavior that must line up |
|------------|--------------------------------------|
| `CfgRd0` reads PM capability | PM capability exists at the advertised offset and links cleanly. |
| `CfgWr0` writes PMCSR D3hot | PMCSR readback changes and BAR model enters a low-power-safe state. |
| `CfgWr0` writes Command Memory Space Enable | BAR reads should only become meaningful after memory space is enabled. |
| `CfgWr0` enables MSI/MSI-X | Interrupt behavior must match the exposed capability and BAR table/PBA plan. |
| `MemRd` reads reset/status register | State machine must return a stable donor-like transition, not random zeros. |
| `MemWr` writes reset bit | Reset bit should self-clear if the donor does that. |

> [!NOTE]
> **Under the Hood - dynamic behavior beats static cloning**
>
> Raw config bytes are not enough when runtime behavior contradicts them. PMCSR in D3hot with D0-style BAR activity is wrong. So is enabled MSI-X with a dead table/PBA BAR. That is a config-space snapshot, not donor behavior.

#### 11.8.2 PMCSR Bits That Matter

Power Management Capability ID is `0x01`. PMCSR is normally at:

```text
PMCSR byte offset = PM capability base + 0x04
PMCSR size        = 16 bits
```

Core bits:

| PMCSR bit | Name | Practical behavior |
|----------|------|--------------------|
| `1:0` | PowerState | `00b` D0, `11b` D3hot are the states you will actually see most often. |
| `8` | PME Enable | Host may set this before low-power transitions. |
| `15` | PME Status | RW1C in real hardware. A plain WriteMask is not enough to model RW1C perfectly. |

Do not hardcode PMCSR at `0x44` unless your donor PM capability actually starts at `0x40`. Parse the capability chain.

#### 11.8.3 PMCSR State Mirror for Lab Builds

This module mirrors PMCSR state from Config Write TLPs. It does not replace the shadow BRAM path. It gives the BAR model a power-state signal so D0/D3 behavior stays aligned with PMCSR.

Feed it from the config-shadow decode in `src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv` or an equivalent tapped decode path.

```systemverilog
// File: src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv or a small included helper
//
// Purpose:
// - Track PMCSR PowerState and PME Enable from CfgWr0 traffic.
// - Provide device_in_d3hot to BAR responder logic.
// - Keep PME Status separate because plain WriteMask cannot model RW1C correctly.
//
// cfg_wr_addr is a DWORD address, matching pcie_rx_addr in the shadow module.
// PM_CAP_BASE is a byte offset from the donor capability chain.

module pcileech_pmcsr_state_model #(
    parameter integer PM_CAP_BASE = 8'h40
)(
    input              rst,
    input              clk,

    input              cfg_wr_valid,
    input      [9:0]   cfg_wr_addr,
    input      [3:0]   cfg_wr_be,
    input      [31:0]  cfg_wr_data,

    input              function_level_reset,

    output reg [1:0]   pm_power_state,
    output reg         pm_pme_enable,
    output reg         pm_pme_status,
    output wire        device_in_d0,
    output wire        device_in_d3hot
);

    localparam integer PMCSR_BYTE_OFFSET = PM_CAP_BASE + 4;
    localparam [9:0]   PMCSR_DW_ADDR     = ((PM_CAP_BASE + 4) >> 2);
    localparam integer PMCSR_BYTE_LANE   = ((PM_CAP_BASE + 4) & 3);

    wire cfg_wr_hits_pmcsr = cfg_wr_valid && (cfg_wr_addr == PMCSR_DW_ADDR);

    wire [15:0] pmcsr_wr_value =
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 0) ? cfg_wr_data[15:0]  :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 1) ? cfg_wr_data[23:8]  :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 2) ? cfg_wr_data[31:16] :
                                 16'h0000;

    wire pmcsr_low_byte_written =
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 0) ? cfg_wr_be[0] :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 1) ? cfg_wr_be[1] :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 2) ? cfg_wr_be[2] :
                                 cfg_wr_be[3];

    wire pmcsr_high_byte_written =
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 0) ? cfg_wr_be[1] :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 1) ? cfg_wr_be[2] :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 2) ? cfg_wr_be[3] :
                                 1'b0;

    assign device_in_d0    = (pm_power_state == 2'b00);
    assign device_in_d3hot = (pm_power_state == 2'b11);

    always @ (posedge clk) begin
        if (rst || function_level_reset) begin
            pm_power_state <= 2'b00;
            pm_pme_enable  <= 1'b0;
            pm_pme_status  <= 1'b0;
        end else begin
            if (cfg_wr_hits_pmcsr && pmcsr_low_byte_written) begin
                pm_power_state <= pmcsr_wr_value[1:0];
                pm_pme_enable  <= pmcsr_wr_value[8];
            end

            if (cfg_wr_hits_pmcsr && pmcsr_high_byte_written && pmcsr_wr_value[15]) begin
                pm_pme_status <= 1'b0;
            end
        end
    end

endmodule
```

Use the state in your BAR responder. In D3hot, do not keep pretending the device is fully active:

```systemverilog
// Example BAR read behavior gated by PMCSR state.
// Drop inside a donor-specific BAR implementation in:
// src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv

always @ (posedge clk) begin
    if (rst) begin
        rd_rsp_ctx   <= 88'd0;
        rd_rsp_data  <= 32'd0;
        rd_rsp_valid <= 1'b0;
    end else begin
        rd_rsp_ctx   <= rd_req_ctx;
        rd_rsp_valid <= rd_req_valid;

        if (device_in_d3hot) begin
            case (rd_req_addr[11:0])
                12'h000: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                12'h004: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                12'h008: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                default: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
            endcase
        end else begin
            case (rd_req_addr[11:0])
                12'h000: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h81680001;
                12'h004: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000001;
                12'h008: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                12'h00C: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                default: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
            endcase
        end
    end
end
```

Keep the first version deterministic. Once the state transition works, replace the example DWORDs with behavior taken from the BAR dump and driver trace.

#### 11.8.4 PMCSR Bring-Up Checklist

For PMCSR, collect proof for each item below:

- PM capability base is parsed from the donor, not guessed;
- PMCSR offset is documented;
- PMCSR WriteMask allows PowerState and PME Enable at the correct offset;
- PME Status RW1C is either modeled or explicitly marked unimplemented;
- BAR behavior changes or safely idles when PMCSR enters D3hot;
- function-level reset returns the model to D0;
- Windows readback confirms the PMCSR transition;
- cold boot still enumerates cleanly.

If PMCSR is still ignored, record it as unimplemented.

### 11.9 Hold Off on More Logic

Do not stack more state machines on top until the current path meets all of these:

- BAR controller builds cleanly
- timing still passes
- BAR readback works on Windows
- required offsets return planned values
- required writes are handled
- driver behavior improves or failure reason is understood

---

## 12. Alternative: Zero4K Method

### 12.1 When Zero4K Is Useful

Zero4K is useful when:

- you need a simple first BAR response
- the donor uses a small BAR region
- tested offsets are within 4KB
- the driver mostly reads static registers

Zero4K is **not** full BAR emulation.

Zero4K proves only this:

```text
The first 4KB of one static BAR response can be read.
```

> [!NOTE]
> **Under the Hood - what Zero4K actually does**
>
> Zero4K is a static 4KB MMIO responder. It gives basic BAR probes stable readback instead of timeout, zeroes, or all-`FF`. It says nothing about reset logic, MSI-X table/PBA, EEPROM/NVM windows, or driver state machines.

Zero4K does **not** prove:

- larger BAR coverage
- MSI-X table behavior
- MSI-X PBA behavior
- reset bit behavior
- status bit behavior
- EEPROM/NVM window behavior
- write/readback behavior
- driver binding

If the donor BAR is larger than 4KB, document:

```text
BAR size:
Covered by Zero4K:
Not covered:
Offsets tested:
Offsets not tested:
MSI-X table/PBA inside covered range:
Driver-critical offsets inside covered range:
```

If you cannot fill that out, you do not understand what Zero4K is covering.

### 12.2 Generate `pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe` on Windows

Create a CSV:

```csv
offset,dword
0x000,12345678
0x004,00000000
0x008,ABCDEF01
```

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/make_zero4k_coe.py
```

```python
import csv
import sys

if len(sys.argv) != 3:
    print("Usage: python make_zero4k_coe.py bar_dwords.csv pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe")
    sys.exit(1)

csv_path = sys.argv[1]
out_path = sys.argv[2]

dwords = ["00000000"] * 1024

with open(csv_path, newline="") as f:
    reader = csv.DictReader(f)
    for row in reader:
        offset = int(row["offset"], 16)
        value = row["dword"].strip().replace("0x", "").replace("0X", "").upper()
        if offset % 4 != 0:
            raise SystemExit(f"Offset not aligned: 0x{offset:03X}")
        if offset >= 4096:
            raise SystemExit(f"Zero4K only supports first 4KB: 0x{offset:03X}")
        if len(value) != 8:
            raise SystemExit(f"DWORD must be 8 hex digits: {value}")
        dwords[offset // 4] = value

with open(out_path, "w", newline="\n") as f:
    f.write("memory_initialization_radix=16;\n")
    f.write("memory_initialization_vector=\n")
    for i, value in enumerate(dwords):
        f.write(value)
        f.write(";\n" if i == len(dwords) - 1 else ",\n")

print("Generated Zero4K COE:", out_path)
print("0x000:", dwords[0])
print("0x004:", dwords[1])
print("0xFFC:", dwords[1023])
```

Run:

```powershell
python C:\dma\tools\make_zero4k_coe.py C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\bar0_dwords.csv C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe
```

### 12.3 Install Zero4K COE in Vivado

Replace:

```text
ip/pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe
```

Then:

1. Find `bram_bar_zero4k`
2. Reset output products if needed
3. Generate output products
4. Rebuild
5. Test BAR readback on Windows

### 12.4 Zero4K Failure Signs

Zero4K has reached its limit if:

```text
BAR is 16KB but only first 4KB works
MSI-X table offset is outside 4KB
driver writes register but readback never changes
BAR read returns all zero
BAR read returns all F
BAR read times out
MSI-X table is outside 4KB
driver expects EEPROM/NVM window
reset/status register needs stateful behavior
```

Do not blame Vivado if your BAR model is incomplete.

### 12.5 When Zero4K Is Enough

Zero4K is a finished answer only when:

- COE generated with 1024 DWORDs
- byte order checked
- `bram_bar_zero4k` regenerated
- first DWORD reads correctly
- first 4KB reads without timeout
- covered and uncovered BAR ranges are documented
- MSI-X table/PBA coverage is documented if MSI-X exists
- you clearly document that this is not full large-BAR emulation

---

## 13. Build and Flash

### 13.1 Pre-Build Checklist

Before build:

```text
[ ] Stock firmware already works
[ ] Donor capture complete
[ ] Correct board folder selected
[ ] Correct FPGA part and package confirmed
[ ] Vivado version recorded
[ ] PCIe IP IDs configured
[ ] BAR type/size configured
[ ] cfg_dsn set if needed
[ ] rw[203] set in pcileech_fifo.sv
[ ] rw[206] set in pcileech_fifo.sv if using WriteMask
[ ] pcileech_cfgspace.coe generated and checked
[ ] pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe generated and checked
[ ] pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe generated if using Zero4K
[ ] BAR responder plan documented
[ ] recovery method confirmed
```

### 13.2 Vivado GUI Build Route

In Vivado:

1. Generate output products for changed IP
2. Run Synthesis
3. Open Synthesized Design only if needed
4. Run Implementation
5. Generate Bitstream
6. Open timing summary
7. Open utilization report
8. Save logs and reports

A build worth flashing ends with:

```text
Synthesis completed successfully
Implementation completed successfully
write_bitstream completed successfully
Timing constraints are met
```

Stop before flashing on:

```text
Synthesis failed
Implementation failed
Timing failed
Critical warning about clock/pin/part
IP output products out of date
```

Do not flash if implementation failed or timing is obviously broken.

### 13.3 Vivado Tcl Shortcut Route

Open:

```text
Start Menu -> Vivado Tcl Shell
```

Then:

```tcl
cd C:/dma/work/squirrel-rtl8125
source vivado_generate_project.tcl -notrace
source vivado_build.tcl -notrace
report_timing_summary -file timing_summary.txt
report_utilization -file utilization.txt
```

PowerShell log capture example:

```powershell
mkdir C:\dma\builds\logs
& "C:\Xilinx\Vivado\2023.2\bin\vivado.bat" -mode batch -source C:\dma\work\squirrel-rtl8125\vivado_build.tcl -notrace 2>&1 | Tee-Object C:\dma\builds\logs\vivado_build.log
```

Output paths vary, but commonly:

```text
<project>.runs/impl_1/*.bit
<project>.runs/impl_1/*.bin
```

### 13.4 Save Evidence Every Time

Do not make a mystery firmware. Save evidence.

The minimum set proves what was flashed. The full set lets someone reproduce it later.

**Minimum Evidence**

```text
C:/dma/builds/2026-xx-xx-board-donor-v1/
  windows-version.txt
  vivado-version.txt
  driver-version.txt
  board-folder.txt
  fpga-part-package.txt
  donor_specs.md
  vivado_build.log
  timing_summary.txt
  utilization.txt
  firmware.bit
  firmware.bin
  sha256.txt
  flash-tool-screenshot.png
  device-manager-hardware-ids.png
  device-manager-resources.png
  arbor-or-telescan-target-readback.txt
  cold-boot-result.txt
```

If you are missing minimum evidence, do not claim the step is finished.

**Full Evidence**

```text
C:/dma/builds/2026-xx-xx-board-donor-v1/
  windows-version.txt
  vivado-version.txt
  driver-version.txt
  board-folder.txt
  fpga-part-package.txt
  donor_specs.md
  git-diff.patch
  vivado_build.log
  timing_summary.txt
  utilization.txt
  firmware.bit
  firmware.bin
  sha256.txt
  flash-tool-screenshot.png
  device-manager-hardware-ids.png
  device-manager-resources.png
  arbor-target-readback.txt
  telescan-target.tlscan
