  device-manager-events.png
  device-manager-driver-status.png
  arbor-donor-export.txt
  telescan-donor.tlscan
  config-dwords.csv
  generated-coe-check-output.txt
  writemask-check-notes.txt
  bar-readback-notes.txt
  flash-tool-log.txt
  photos/
```

PowerShell hash:

```powershell
Get-FileHash .\firmware.bit -Algorithm SHA256
Get-FileHash .\firmware.bin -Algorithm SHA256
```

### 13.5 Windows Flashing by Board Family

There is no universal flash command.

Before any board-specific flashing:

```text
[ ] Programmer appears in Windows Device Manager
[ ] Flashing tool can detect the programmer
[ ] Stock firmware or recovery image is available
[ ] Correct FPGA part/package is written down
[ ] Correct board folder is written down
[ ] You know whether the operation is SRAM load or flash programming
[ ] You saved the build hash
```

If the programmer is not detected before flashing, there is no tested recovery path.

**Squirrel / LeetDMA**

Possible tools:

- OpenOCD for Windows
- Squirrel update port workflow
- vendor tool

Warnings:

- `pld load` may only load SRAM
- persistent flash programming is different
- cold boot proves persistence

**CaptainDMA**

Possible tools:

- CH347 FPGA tool
- vendor tool
- M2-FW module for some M.2 boards

Warnings:

- 35T CSG325 and 35T FGG484 are not interchangeable
- 75T and 100T images are not interchangeable
- wrong image can stop enumeration

**Enigma X1**

Possible tools:

- Vivado Hardware Manager
- upstream/vendor flash script

Warnings:

- confirm exact FPGA part
- confirm flash memory part
- do not assume Squirrel commands apply

**ZDMA**

Possible tools:

- Vivado Hardware Manager
- vendor flow

Warnings:

- may involve more than one device/FPGA path
- confirm which image is being programmed

**AC701**

Possible tools:

- Vivado Hardware Manager
- official Xilinx/JTAG flow

Warnings:

- choose correct memory part
- board is not the same as cheap Artix-7 DMA boards

### 13.6 SRAM Load vs Flash Programming

SRAM and flash are easy to confuse.

| Operation | What happens |
|----------|--------------|
| SRAM / volatile load | FPGA runs new image until power is removed |
| Flash programming | Image persists after power loss |

If warm reboot shows new firmware but cold boot returns old firmware, you probably only loaded SRAM.

How to tell you only loaded SRAM:

```text
new firmware works immediately after programming
Windows restart still may show it
full power-off makes old firmware return
flash tool log does not show flash erase/program/verify
command name says load, configure, or pld load instead of program flash
```

How to tell flash programming probably happened:

```text
tool erased flash
tool programmed flash
tool verified flash
device still shows new firmware after full power removal
```

### 13.7 Cold Boot Verification

After flashing:

1. Shut down Windows
2. Turn off PSU or remove power if needed
3. Wait 10-30 seconds
4. Power on
5. Boot Windows
6. Check Device Manager
7. Check Arbor/TeleScan readback

Warm reboot normal does not prove flash persistence.

### 13.8 Save the Build Before Leaving the Bench

Do not pack up after seeing the progress bar hit 100%. Save and verify:

- bit/bin generated
- timing reviewed
- utilization saved
- hash saved
- correct flash tool used
- flash screenshot saved
- cold boot performed
- Windows sees the expected device after cold boot

---

## 14. Windows Validation and Troubleshooting

### 14.1 Device Manager Is Only Step One

Open:

```text
Device Manager -> target device -> Properties
```

Check:

- General tab
- Driver tab
- Details -> Hardware Ids
- Details -> Compatible Ids
- Resources tab
- Events tab

A clean Device Manager result:

```text
Device status: This device is working properly.
Hardware IDs show expected VEN/DEV/SUBSYS/REV.
Resources show expected memory ranges.
No conflict listed.
```

Enumeration or driver work remains if:

```text
Unknown device
Code 10
Code 12
Code 31
No Resources tab
BAR resource missing
Device failed to start
```

### 14.2 Arbor/TeleScan Target Readback

After flashing, use Arbor or TeleScan PE on the Windows target.

Compare target against donor notes:

| Area | Must check |
|------|------------|
| `0x00` | VID/DID |
| `0x04` | Command/Status |
| `0x08` | Revision/Class |
| `0x10-0x24` | BARs |
| `0x2C` | Subsystem IDs |
| `0x34` | Capability Pointer |
| `0x40+` | Standard capabilities |
| `0x100+` | Extended capabilities |

Then classify differences:

| Difference type | Examples | What to do |
|-----------------|----------|------------|
| Stable field | VID/DID, Revision/Class, Subsystem IDs, capability IDs | Should match the donor plan. Fix if wrong. |
| Runtime field | Command, Status, BAR assigned address, MSI enable, PM state | Record it. Do not panic if it changes. |
| Intentional difference | FPGA link width differs, MSI-X intentionally disabled for a test | Document why. |
| Bug | broken capability pointer, wrong BAR size, missing extended cap, stale VID/DID | Fix before claiming success. |

Your diff table should not say "close enough". It should say stable, runtime, intentional, or bug.

Readback problems:

```text
0x40 and later all zero
capability chain broken
extended capabilities missing
BAR values look like donor runtime addresses
VID/DID still default PCILeech
```

Fix the relevant firmware step. Do not randomly change more IDs.

### 14.3 Windows WriteMask and Command Register Test

Use Arbor/TeleScan or another trusted PCI config editor if it supports controlled writes.

Test:

1. Read Command register
2. Toggle allowed Command bits
3. Read back
4. Try writing VID/DID
5. Confirm VID/DID did not change
6. Clear reasonable Status/RW1C bits
7. Confirm device remains alive

The config write path is behaving when:

```text
Command writable bits stick.
VID/DID remain unchanged.
Status behavior is reasonable.
Device remains present.
```

WriteMask or shadow bugs look like:

```text
Command never changes
VID/DID become corrupted
device disappears after config write
MSI enable cannot stick
```

Those are WriteMask/shadow-write failures.

### 14.4 Windows BAR Readback Test

Use Arbor, TeleScan, vendor diagnostic tools, or your own lab BAR read tool.

Minimum:

- BAR first DWORD
- BAR first 4KB
- unsupported offset
- high offset if BAR is larger than 4KB
- MSI-X table/PBA offset if MSI-X exists

A working BAR path:

```text
BAR read completes.
Values are stable.
Unsupported offsets return safe values.
Target does not freeze.
```

A broken or incomplete BAR path:

```text
read timeout
all zero unexpectedly
all FFFFFFFF
random values
target freezes
driver fails after BAR access
```

Fix BAR response path.

### 14.5 Driver Binding Failures

Driver binding debug order:

```text
1. Confirm stock firmware still works.
2. Confirm PCIe identity: VID/DID/Revision/Class/Subsys.
3. Confirm BAR type, size, 64-bit pairing, and Resources tab.
4. Confirm config-space readback in Arbor/TeleScan.
5. Confirm WriteMask and Command register behavior.
6. Confirm BAR readback.
7. Confirm MSI/MSI-X capability and table/PBA behavior.
8. Confirm PMCSR behavior.
9. Confirm reset/status registers in BAR space.
10. Then read Driver tab and Events.
```

If you jump from Code 10 straight back to changing VID/DID, you are guessing.

**Code 10 - device cannot start**

Real causes:

- BAR register behavior missing
- MSI/MSI-X broken
- PMCSR broken
- EEPROM/NVM window missing
- reset bit never clears
- status bit never changes
- interrupt mask behavior wrong
- driver expects real hardware state

Do not fix Code 10 by changing VID/DID again.

**Code 12 - not enough resources**

Likely causes:

- BAR size too large
- invalid BAR pairing
- 64-bit BAR configured wrong
- resource conflict
- target BIOS/slot issue

**Code 31 - driver failed to load**

Likely causes:

- wrong class/subsystem
- driver mismatch
- missing capability behavior
- Windows driver package issue

**Unknown device**

Likely causes:

- VID/DID/class mismatch
- driver not installed
- config space incomplete
- subsystem mismatch

### 14.6 Common Windows Failure Cases

| Symptom | Likely cause | First thing to check |
|---------|--------------|----------------------|
| Device Manager completely does not show device | flash failed, wrong bitstream, PCIe link issue, board not powered | stock firmware recovery and PCIe link |
| Unknown device | identity/class/subsystem mismatch | Hardware IDs and Class Code |
| Code 10 | BAR/MSI/PMCSR/state behavior missing | BAR readback and Events tab |
| Code 12 | BAR resource conflict or bad size | Resources tab |
| Code 31 | driver package or matching issue | Driver tab and Events |
| Resources tab empty | BAR disabled, enumeration incomplete, driver/device failed too early | Vivado BAR settings and config readback |
| BAR size wrong | Vivado IP BAR size/type wrong or shadow overwrote BAR registers | PCIe IP BAR tab and target BAR sizing |
| Config after 0x40 all zero | `rw[203]` still zero-data or COE not loaded | `pcileech_fifo.sv` and BRAM regenerate |
| Extended capability missing | COE only covers 256B, extended chain broken, wrong takeover | COE depth and `0x100` readback |
| VID/DID did not change | IP not regenerated or stale flash | PCIe IP, bitstream timestamp |
| VID/DID got corrupted | WriteMask allows writes at `0x00` | WriteMask at `0x00` |
| Command write does not stick | `rw[206]` disabled or mask wrong | WriteMask |
| MSI Enable does not stick | MSI capability mask wrong or MSI offset assumed incorrectly | donor capability offset and WriteMask |
| BAR read timeout | no completion path | BAR controller |
| BAR reads all zero | Zero/static responder used incorrectly, COE not loaded, wrong BAR index | BAR COE and BAR routing |
| BAR reads all F | no device response, unsupported path, failed completion | BAR controller and PCIe completion path |
| Cold boot returns old firmware | SRAM load only | persistent flash process |
| Vivado erased manual edit | output products regenerated | generated file diff |
| COE not used by BRAM | wrong COE path, BRAM not regenerated, stale IP output | Vivado IP customization and generated output products |
| Build fails after paste | pasted pseudocode | module ports/signals |
| Wrong board folder used | wrong pins/part/project | upstream board matrix and FPGA package |
| FPGA part/package wrong | wrong constraints and bitstream | Vivado part settings and board marking |
| CH347/OpenOCD/Vivado HW Manager does not see board | programmer driver, wrong cable, board mode, power | Windows Device Manager programmer entry |
| Board dead after flash | wrong board folder, wrong FPGA package, bad image | recovery image/tool |

### 14.7 Failure Matrix

Match the symptom, collect the listed evidence, and fix the first failing layer.

Work from the lowest failing layer:

| Level | Layer | What must be proven | Primary evidence |
|------|-------|---------------------|------------------|
| 0 | Power / clock / reset | Board powers, FPGA configures, PCIe refclk/reset are sane | programmer detect, flash log, ILA reset/link probes |
| 1 | Link training | Endpoint reaches a stable link before OS driver work | BIOS visibility, `pl_ltssm_state`, `pl_phy_lnk_up`, cold boot |
| 2 | Enumeration / config | Type 0 config reads/writes behave | Device Manager, Arbor/TeleScan, `CfgRd0/CfgWr0` ILA |
| 3 | BAR / TLP | MMIO reads/writes complete and state changes | BAR readback, ILA `rd_rsp_valid`, dynamic BAR state |
| 4 | Driver workload | Driver starts and survives normal operations | Events tab, driver logs, workload test, cold boot repeat |

#### 14.7.1 POST Hang / BIOS Freeze / No Boot

| Symptom | Likely cause | Evidence | Fix | Avoid |
|---------|-----------------|--------------------------|--------------|----------------|
| Motherboard freezes before OS boot | BAR request is too large for firmware MMIO allocation window | BIOS POST code, resources differ between stock and custom firmware, BAR size in PCIe IP | Reduce BAR size to donor-realistic value; disable unused BARs; confirm 64-bit pairing | Do not increase BAR size because "bigger looks real" |
| POST hangs only with custom bitstream | PCIe link training timeout or unstable LTSSM transition | ILA `pl_ltssm_state`, `pl_phy_lnk_up`, `pl_initial_link_width`, cold boot capture | Fix PCIe IP speed/lane settings; test Gen1 first; verify slot/adaptor signal integrity | Do not edit VID/DID for a link training failure |
| Board works in one slot but not another | MMIO aperture, ASPM, bifurcation, or lane wiring difference | Same firmware across two slots, BIOS resource map, link width/speed readback | Test simple x1 Gen1 profile; change slot; disable aggressive ASPM in BIOS for lab testing | Do not assume the FPGA image is proven because one slot works |
| Device disappears after cold boot but warm reboot works | SRAM load only, flash not persistent, or PCIe training marginal after power loss | flash tool log, cold boot result, bit/bin hash, programmer verify output | Program persistent flash; verify erase/program/verify; power-cycle and re-read config | Do not call warm reboot a flash validation |
| POST fail after changing board folder | Wrong FPGA part/package or wrong `.xdc` pins | Vivado part name, package, board marking, `.xdc` diff, timing critical warnings | Use correct board folder; verify FPGA package; restore known-good constraints | Do not force bitstream generation with wrong constraints |
| Board does not enumerate after timing failure | PCIe user clock / reset crossing broken by failed implementation | `timing_summary.rpt`, worst negative slack, unconstrained clocks | Fix timing before flashing; reduce logic; pipeline BAR state machine | Do not flash a bitstream with obvious timing failure |
| Flash succeeds but card is dead | Wrong image family, wrong flash offset, or vendor tool wrote incompatible image | IDCODE, flash log, board silkscreen, stock recovery test | Restore stock firmware; confirm exact FPGA and flash part; rebuild from correct project | Do not try random board images |

POST-level rule:

```text
No stable PCIe link = do not debug WriteMask.
No stable flash persistence = do not debug Windows driver binding.
No correct FPGA package = do not debug BAR behavior.
```

#### 14.7.2 Device Manager Yellow Triangle: Code 10 / Code 43

Code 10 and Code 43 are not solved by changing IDs. They mean the driver or Windows device stack hit behavior that did not match the device contract.

| Symptom | Likely cause | Evidence | Test | Fix |
|---------|-----------------|---------------------|---------------|--------------|
| Code 10 immediately after driver start | BAR read returns timeout/all-zero/all-`FF` | Arbor/TeleScan BAR read, Events tab, ILA BAR `rd_req_valid` vs `rd_rsp_valid` | Read first DWORD, first 4KB, unsupported offset | Implement BAR responder for the register path the driver touches |
| Code 10 after config writes | WriteMask blocks required writable bits | Arbor/TeleScan before/after `CfgWr0`, ILA `pcie_rx_wren`, target config diff | Toggle Command, MSI Enable, PMCSR PowerState at donor offsets | Regenerate capability-aware WriteMask |
| Code 10 after reset register write | BAR reset bit never self-clears | BAR trace: write reset bit, repeated status reads | Write reset bit, poll status | Add reset timer/state transition in BAR model |
| Code 43 / device reported problem | Driver sees impossible status/capability combination | Device Events, config readback, BAR status values | Compare donor and target after driver start | Fix contradictions: MSI-X exposed but table dead, PMCSR D3hot but BAR active, AER broken |
| MSI enable cannot stick | Wrong capability offset or WriteMask bit | Config diff at actual MSI capability base | Write MSI Message Control, read back | Parse donor capability chain; mask actual offset |
| MSI-X enabled then driver fails | MSI-X table/PBA BAR region missing | MSI-X capability table offset/BIR, BAR read at table/PBA | Read/write MSI-X table entry and PBA area | Implement table/PBA behavior or do not expose MSI-X |
| PMCSR write breaks driver start | Power-state bits not writable or no D0/D3 behavior | PM capability base, PMCSR readback, BAR behavior after D3hot | Write D3hot then D0, read PMCSR and BAR status | Add PMCSR WriteMask and PM-aware BAR state |
| VID/DID corrupts after test write | WriteMask permits identity writes | Arbor/TeleScan write test at `0x00` | Attempt write `0x00.L`, read back | Set identity area read-only; restore donor shadow COE |

WriteMask targeting flow:

```text
1. Capture donor capability offsets.
2. Capture target config before driver bind.
3. Start driver.
4. Capture target config after failure.
5. Diff runtime fields only.
6. For each failed field:
   - Is the bit supposed to be writable?
   - Is it RW1C?
   - Is the offset donor-correct?
   - Did the write hit `pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv`?
   - Did `rw[206]` in `src/pcileech_fifo.sv` allow the write path?
7. Regenerate WriteMask.
8. Re-test only that field.
```

The fix for Code 10/43 is usually one layer deeper than Device Manager says.

#### 14.7.3 Driver Load Causes BSOD

A BSOD during driver load is a hard failure. Treat it as a protocol crash until proven otherwise.

| Crash timing | Likely cause | Evidence | ILA / software probe | Fix |
|-------------|-----------------|---------------------|----------------------|--------------|
| BSOD immediately after driver starts | Driver MMIO read gets no completion or illegal response | Windows crash time, BAR readback, ILA `rd_req_valid` without `rd_rsp_valid` | Trigger on first MemRd to BAR after driver bind | Return safe completion for every decoded and unsupported offset |
| BSOD after a BAR write handshake | FPGA ignores doorbell/mailbox write | ILA `wr_valid`, `wr_addr`, `wr_data`, following status polls | Trigger on write to doorbell/status/control offset | Add dynamic BAR state machine; update busy/status/response |
| BSOD after MSI/MSI-X enable | Interrupt capability says yes, behavior says no | MSI/MSI-X config diff, IRQ status, table/PBA BAR access | Watch MSI enable write and table writes | Implement MSI-X table/PBA or disable MSI-X in donor plan |
| BSOD during reset path | Reset bit never clears or clears too fast/late | BAR reset write, repeated status reads, driver timeout | Trigger on reset register write | Add reset timer and self-clear behavior from donor trace |
| BSOD under workload | Queue/descriptor/stream registers are static | BAR write/read sequence, packet/audio counters, driver logs | Capture doorbell writes and status polling loop | Add queue depth, counter, descriptor, or stream-state modeling |
| BSOD only after cold boot | Flash persistence or link training unstable | cold boot capture, link state, flash verify | Compare warm vs cold ILA traces | Fix flash programming or PCIe PHY/link settings |

BSOD triage order:

```text
1. Restore stock firmware and prove target machine is stable.
2. Boot custom firmware without binding the donor driver if possible.
3. Read config space with Arbor/TeleScan.
4. Read BAR first DWORD and unsupported offset.
5. Enable ILA trigger on BAR MemRd/MemWr.
6. Bind driver and capture the last successful TLP.
7. If the last TLP is MemRd with no completion, fix completion path.
8. If the last TLP is MemWr doorbell followed by polling, fix BAR state machine.
9. If the last TLP is MSI-X table write, fix table/PBA behavior.
10. Re-test from cold boot.
```

Do not keep rebooting into BSOD and changing random IDs. Capture the failing transaction.

#### 14.7.4 Evidence Map

| Evidence | Proves | Does not prove |
|----------|--------|----------------|
| Device Manager visible | Basic enumeration | Driver correctness |
| Resources tab | BAR allocation | BAR response |
| Arbor/TeleScan config diff | Config identity and write behavior | BAR state machine |
| BAR readback | Completion path and basic MMIO | Driver workload correctness |
| ILA CfgRd/CfgWr trigger | Enumeration transaction path | BAR model behavior |
| ILA MemRd/MemWr trigger | Driver register traffic | Correct high-level device semantics |
| Timing report | Build timing health | Functional correctness |
| Cold boot | Flash persistence and link training | Full driver behavior |

A "yellow triangle" is not a diagnosis. Tie the failure to a layer, capture the artifact, then fix the first broken part.

### 14.8 Reading the Output

**Vivado normal**

```text
Synthesis completed successfully.
Implementation completed successfully.
write_bitstream completed successfully.
Timing constraints are met.
```

**Vivado bad**

```text
CRITICAL WARNING: timing constraints not met
ERROR: part not found
ERROR: module not found
ERROR: failed to generate output products
```

**PCIe IP regenerate normal**

```text
Generate Output Products completed.
IP status is current.
Expected `.xci` changes remain.
Expected generated-file edits still exist if you made any.
```

**PCIe IP regenerate bad**

```text
IP output products failed.
Vivado upgraded the IP unexpectedly.
Generated wrapper edit disappeared.
COE path reverted.
```

**COE parse normal**

```text
memory_initialization_radix=16 accepted
memory_initialization_vector accepted
BRAM/ROM output products generated
sanity-check script shows expected 0x00/0x08/0x2C/0x34/0x100
```

**COE parse bad**

```text
invalid radix
invalid memory initialization vector
wrong number of DWORDs
0x000 is 00000000
capability chain loop detected
runtime BAR-looking value warning
```

**Device Manager normal**

```text
This device is working properly.
Hardware IDs contain expected VEN/DEV/SUBSYS/REV.
Resources show memory ranges.
```

**Device Manager bad**

```text
Code 10
Code 12
Code 31
Unknown device
No resources
```

**Arbor/TeleScan normal**

```text
Header decodes correctly.
Capability chain is valid.
BAR sizes match donor plan.
Extended capabilities are present if expected.
```

**Arbor/TeleScan bad**

```text
FFFF:FFFF
capability pointer invalid
0x40+ all zero
BAR size wrong
extended config missing
```

**BAR read normal**

```text
first DWORD returns expected value
4KB read completes
unsupported offset returns safe default
```

**BAR read bad**

```text
timeout
all zero
all F
random changing values
system freeze
```

**Flash normal**

```text
programmer detected
target FPGA ID matches expected family
programming completes without verify error
tool log saved
```

**Flash bad**

```text
programmer not found
unexpected IDCODE
verify failed
tool only performed SRAM load when you expected flash programming
```

**Cold boot normal**

```text
power removed
system powered back on
device enumerates with new firmware
Arbor/TeleScan readback still matches target plan
```

**Cold boot bad**

```text
device returns to old firmware
device disappears
target hangs at POST
BAR/resources differ from warm reboot
```

### 14.9 Final Validation Checklist

```text
[ ] Donor capture folder complete
[ ] Windows driver version saved
[ ] Stock firmware baseline works
[ ] Correct board folder used
[ ] Correct FPGA part/package used
[ ] PCIe IP IDs correct
[ ] BAR type/size correct
[ ] Shadow config COE generated by offset
[ ] 0x00/0x08/0x2C/0x34/0x100 validated
[ ] rw[203] edited in pcileech_fifo.sv
[ ] WriteMask COE generated
[ ] rw[206] edited in pcileech_fifo.sv
[ ] cfg_dsn matches DSN plan
[ ] MSI/MSI-X plan documented
[ ] Zero4K limitation documented
[ ] Build log saved
[ ] Timing report saved
[ ] Utilization report saved
[ ] bit/bin hashes saved
[ ] Flash tool screenshot saved
[ ] Cold boot completed
[ ] Device Manager screenshots saved
[ ] Arbor/TeleScan target readback saved
[ ] BAR readback tested
[ ] Driver status recorded
```

If you cannot show the evidence, you did not finish the step.

### 14.10 Keep a Test Record

Save the following with the build:

- Device Manager status is saved
- Hardware IDs are saved
- Resources are saved
- Events are saved
- Arbor or TeleScan target readback is saved
- donor-target diff is classified
- WriteMask behavior is tested or explicitly marked untested
- BAR validation level is recorded
- driver binding result is recorded
- cold boot result is recorded

### 14.11 Before Calling It Final

Only call the build final after:

- Windows donor capture reaches at least Level 3
- COE generation is reproducible
- COE sanity check passes
- WriteMask level is declared
- BAR validation level is declared
- Zero4K coverage is documented if used
- recovery path is documented
- minimum evidence folder exists
- all known differences are classified as stable, runtime, intentional, or bug
- the README does not imply that VID/DID-only work is complete firmware

Anything short of this stays experimental.

---

## Advanced: Hardware Debugging with Vivado ILA

When a board enumerates once and then randomly dies, screenshots are not enough. Use ILA and look at the bus.

Use ILA for the ugly cases:

- target hangs during POST
- device appears only after warm reboot
- config space reads as zero after offset `0x40`
- BAR sizing works once and then fails
- Windows shows Code 10 but the donor identity looks correct
- a generated IP change silently changed the TLP path

### ILA.1 Probe the Right RX Path

In current upstream-style PCILeech 7 Series projects, the PCIe endpoint receive interface is usually wired in:

```text
src/pcileech_pcie_a7.sv
```

Look for:

```systemverilog
.m_axis_rx_tdata  ( tlp_rx.data  ),
.m_axis_rx_tkeep  ( tlp_rx.keep  ),
.m_axis_rx_tlast  ( tlp_rx.last  ),
.m_axis_rx_tvalid ( tlp_rx.valid )
```

Some generated Xilinx wrapper views label the endpoint RX side as `s_axis_rx_*` or expose it through a different hierarchy. Do not fight the name. The real rule is simple:

```text
Probe the RX stream coming out of the PCIe core and entering the PCILeech TLP pipeline.
```

Useful probes:

| Probe | Why |
|------|-----|
| `tlp_rx.data[63:0]` | Raw TLP header/data from PCIe core in the 64-bit RX path |
| `tlp_rx.keep[7:0]` | Which bytes are valid |
| `tlp_rx.last` | End of packet |
| `tlp_rx.valid` | Packet beat valid |
| `tlp_rx.user[21:0]` | Sideband flags if exposed in your build |
| `tlps_in.tdata[127:0]` | Repacked 128-bit TLP stream used by shadow/BAR logic |
| `tlps_in.tuser[0]` | First DWORD marker in `IfAXIS128` |
| `pcie_rx_rden` | Config read detected in `pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv` |
| `pcie_rx_wren` | Config write detected in `pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv` |
| `bram_rd_valid` | Shadow config read response generated |
| `rd_rsp_valid` | BAR read completion generated |

If you only probe `VID/DID`, you are not debugging. Probe the packet path.

### ILA.2 Trigger on Config Reads and Writes

The config-shadow module already shows the useful decode:

```text
src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv
```

Current upstream-style decode:

```systemverilog
wire pcie_rx_rden = tlps_in.tvalid
                  && tlps_in.tuser[0]
                  && (tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0000010); // CfgRd0/CfgRd1

wire pcie_rx_wren = tlps_in.tvalid
                  && tlps_in.tuser[0]
                  && (tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0100010); // CfgWr0/CfgWr1
```

ILA trigger plan:

```text
Trigger 1: tlps_in.tvalid == 1
Trigger 2: tlps_in.tuser[0] == 1
Trigger 3: tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0000010 or 7'b0100010
Capture:  tlps_in.tdata, tlps_in.tkeepdw, tlps_in.tuser, pcie_rx_rden, pcie_rx_wren, bram_rd_valid
Depth:    4096 samples minimum if your FPGA has enough BRAM
Window:   pre-trigger 25%, post-trigger 75%
```

What this tells you:

| ILA result | Meaning |
|-----------|---------|
| No config TLPs arrive | Link training, reset, clocking, or PCIe core problem. Stop editing COE. |
| `CfgRd0` arrives but no response path fires | Shadow config decode, `rw[203]`, filter, or BRAM path is wrong. |
| `CfgWr0` arrives before hang | Host is changing Command/Status/BAR/PM state; check WriteMask and writable behavior. |
| Config path works, BAR read never completes | BAR controller or selected BAR implementation is wrong. |
| Completion exists but data is shifted | Endian/order/offset bug. Check DWORD indexing. |

### ILA.3 POST-Fail Workflow

Do this in order. Do not change five things at once.

1. Build a known-good stock or baseline bitstream with ILA.
2. Save the baseline capture for normal enumeration.
3. Build your modified firmware with the same ILA probes.
4. Cold boot the target, not just Windows restart.
5. Capture the first `CfgRd0` and first `CfgWr0`.
6. Compare against the baseline:
   - first config read offset
   - first config write offset
   - Command register write
   - BAR sizing sequence
   - capability pointer walk
   - first BAR MMIO read
7. Fix the first broken branch only.
8. Rebuild and repeat.

A routine early-enumeration trace is boring:

```text
CfgRd0 arrives
shadow/config response returns
CfgWr0 updates expected writable bits
BAR sizing reads/writes complete
capability chain reads continue
BAR MMIO reads complete if the driver starts
```

The first break often looks like:

```text
CfgRd0 arrives once, then nothing
CfgWr0 to Command register happens, then device disappears
BAR sizing request receives nonsense
capability pointer jumps into zero space
BAR read request appears but rd_rsp_valid never fires
```

If ILA says the host never sent the packet, the bug is not in your BAR responder. If ILA says the packet arrived and you never replied, the bug is yours.

### ILA.4 What to Save

An ILA session is useful only if you leave with:

- ILA probes are attached to the actual RX/TLP path
- trigger catches `CfgRd0` and `CfgWr0`
- baseline capture is saved
- failing firmware capture is saved
- first divergence from baseline is identified
- fix is applied to the first broken branch only
- new cold boot capture confirms the fix

---

## Automation Tools & Scripts

Automation must preserve offsets. A one-DWORD shift can pass a quick visual check while breaking every offset after it.

### AUTO.1 Convert Raw Config Hex to SystemVerilog Array

The parser accepts common `lspci -xxxx` and TeleScan-style hex lines. Plain `lspci -vvv` usually has capability text but not the raw byte image. If there are no offset-prefixed hex lines, use `lspci -xxxxxxx` from Appendix A or export raw config bytes from TeleScan.

```text
00: ec 10 25 81 07 04 10 00 05 00 00 02 10 00 00 00
10: 04 00 00 f0 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 f2 00 00 00 00
```

Output is a little-endian DWORD array for SystemVerilog test logic or manual comparison.

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/config_hex_to_sv.py
```

```python
import re
import sys

if len(sys.argv) != 3:
    print("Usage: python config_hex_to_sv.py config_hex.txt cfg_space.sv")
    sys.exit(1)

src_path = sys.argv[1]
out_path = sys.argv[2]

cfg = [0x00] * 4096
line_re = re.compile(r"^\s*([0-9a-fA-F]{2,3}):\s*((?:[0-9a-fA-F]{2}\s*)+)")

with open(src_path, "r", encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore") as f:
    for line in f:
        m = line_re.match(line)
        if not m:
            continue

        offset = int(m.group(1), 16)
        values = [int(x, 16) for x in re.findall(r"[0-9a-fA-F]{2}", m.group(2))]

        for i, value in enumerate(values):
            pos = offset + i
            if pos >= len(cfg):
                raise SystemExit(f"Offset outside 4KB config space: 0x{pos:03X}")
            cfg[pos] = value

def dword_at(offset):
    # PCIe config bytes are byte-addressed. SystemVerilog DWORD value here
    # is little-endian: byte 0 becomes bits [7:0], byte 3 becomes bits [31:24].
    return (
        cfg[offset]
        | (cfg[offset + 1] << 8)
        | (cfg[offset + 2] << 16)
        | (cfg[offset + 3] << 24)
    )

with open(out_path, "w", encoding="utf-8", newline="\n") as f:
    f.write("// Generated from raw config hex. Verify key offsets before use.\n")
    f.write("logic [31:0] cfg_space [0:1023] = '{\n")
    for idx in range(1024):
        offset = idx * 4
        comma = "," if idx != 1023 else ""
        f.write(f"    10'd{idx}: 32'h{dword_at(offset):08X}{comma} // 0x{offset:03X}\n")
    f.write("};\n")

for offset in (0x000, 0x008, 0x02C, 0x034, 0x100):
    print(f"0x{offset:03X}: 32'h{dword_at(offset):08X}")

print("Wrote:", out_path)
```

Run:

```powershell
python C:\dma\tools\config_hex_to_sv.py C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\config_hex.txt C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\cfg_space.sv
```

Reject output like:

```text
0x000: 32'hFFFFFFFF
0x008: 32'h00000000
0x034: points outside captured range
```

Usable output starts like:

```text
0x000: vendor/device DWORD matches donor
0x008: revision/class DWORD matches donor
0x02C: subsystem DWORD matches donor
0x034: capability pointer matches donor plan
0x100: extended capability header matches donor plan if present
```

Do not paste this array blindly into a COE file. COE generation has its own format and offset rules. Use this as a conversion/checking tool unless you intentionally wire a SystemVerilog array into your design.

### AUTO.2 Minimal Vivado Batch Build Script

For repeat builds, keep a small Tcl wrapper and save logs. Project scripts differ by board folder; the build sequence does not:

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/build_pcileech_batch.tcl
```

```tcl
if { $argc < 2 } {
    puts "Usage: vivado -mode batch -source build_pcileech_batch.tcl -tclargs <board_dir> <jobs>"
    exit 1
}

set board_dir [lindex $argv 0]
set jobs      [lindex $argv 1]

cd $board_dir

if {[file exists vivado_generate_project.tcl]} {
    source vivado_generate_project.tcl
}

if {[file exists vivado_build.tcl]} {
    source vivado_build.tcl
} else {
    reset_run synth_1
    launch_runs synth_1 -jobs $jobs
    wait_on_run synth_1

    launch_runs impl_1 -to_step write_bitstream -jobs $jobs
    wait_on_run impl_1
}

open_run impl_1
report_timing_summary -file build_timing_summary.rpt
report_utilization     -file build_utilization.rpt

puts "Build finished."
puts "Timing report:      [file normalize build_timing_summary.rpt]"
puts "Utilization report: [file normalize build_utilization.rpt]"
```

Run from **Vivado Tcl Shell** or a PowerShell that can see `vivado.bat`:

```powershell
vivado.bat -mode batch -source C:\dma\tools\build_pcileech_batch.tcl -tclargs C:\dma\pcileech-fpga\PCIeSquirrel 8
```

Archive after every build:

```text
Vivado version
Windows version
board folder
FPGA part/package
build log
build_timing_summary.rpt
build_utilization.rpt
bit/bin file
SHA256 hash
flash tool screenshot
cold boot result
```

If the saved folder and logs cannot reproduce the bitstream, the build is not reproducible.

## Appendix A: Advanced Linux Raw Capture

This appendix is the stronger evidence path. It stays optional for the first Windows build; use it when clean raw capture is available.

Use this appendix when:

- you want a full 4KB config-space byte capture;
- you want BAR binary dumps;
- you want Linux-side `setpci` write tests;
- you want a stronger donor-target diff than GUI screenshots alone.

Linux stays optional. Nothing in this appendix replaces the Windows-first route.

### A.1 Identify the Donor BDF

On the Linux donor capture machine:

```bash
lspci -nn
lspci -Dnn
```

Example:

```text
0000:03:00.0 Ethernet controller [0200]: Realtek Semiconductor Co., Ltd. RTL8125 2.5GbE Controller [10ec:8125] (rev 05)
```

Set:

```bash
BDF=0000:03:00.0
mkdir -p donor-capture
```

### A.2 Capture Human-Readable PCIe Data

```bash
lspci -s "$BDF" -nn > donor-capture/lspci-nn.txt
lspci -s "$BDF" -vvv > donor-capture/lspci-vvv.txt
lspci -s "$BDF" -xxxx > donor-capture/config-256.txt
lspci -s "$BDF" -xxxxxxx > donor-capture/config-4096.txt
```

What this gives you:

| File | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `lspci-nn.txt` | identity and class summary |
| `lspci-vvv.txt` | BARs, capabilities, link info, MSI/MSI-X |
| `config-256.txt` | standard 256-byte config view |
| `config-4096.txt` | extended 4KB config view when accessible |

If `lspci -xxxxxxx` does not show a full 4KB view, document the limitation. Do not silently call it a full raw capture.

### A.3 Capture Raw 4KB Config Bytes

```bash
cp "/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/config" donor-capture/config-4096.bin
hexdump -C donor-capture/config-4096.bin | head -40
```

Check the file size:

```text
00000000  ec 10 25 81 ...
```

That example would correspond to:

```text
Vendor ID: 10ec
Device ID: 8125
```

If the file is only 256 bytes or cannot be read, record it:

```text
Capture limitation: Linux sysfs config file did not provide full 4KB.
```

### A.4 Capture BAR Resource Layout

```bash
cat "/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/resource" > donor-capture/resource.txt
ls -l "/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/resource"* > donor-capture/resource-files.txt
```

Use it to map:

- BAR index;
- assigned runtime address;
- resource flags;
- which `resourceN` file maps to which BAR.

The runtime BAR address is not a firmware constant. Keep it out of config-space COE.

### A.5 BAR Binary Dump

Dump the first 4KB of BAR0:

```bash
sudo dd if="/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/resource0" of=donor-capture/bar0-4k.bin bs=4096 count=1 iflag=direct
hexdump -C donor-capture/bar0-4k.bin | head -40
```

If BAR0 is larger and you need more:

```bash
sudo dd if="/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/resource0" of=donor-capture/bar0-64k.bin bs=4096 count=16 iflag=direct
```

Record when the dump was taken:

```text
BAR dump state:
- before driver bind:
- after driver bind:
- after device reset:
- after MSI/MSI-X enabled:
- after normal traffic:
```

BAR reads can have side effects on some devices. Capture on a lab machine, not on a production system.

### A.6 VFIO/IOMMU Note

Some capture workflows bind the donor to `vfio-pci` to prevent the normal driver from touching it.

That usually requires IOMMU enabled on the donor capture machine.

That does not conflict with a separate target configured differently for DMA testing.

### A.7 Offline 4096-Byte Physical Config Dump

Use this fallback when HVCI/VBS, kernel isolation, or driver policy blocks Arbor/TeleScan beyond `0x100`: move the donor to a Linux lab box and capture the raw bytes.

Capture a 4096-byte config-space artifact that can be reviewed, hashed, and converted by script.

> [!NOTE]
> **Pro-Tip - Secure Boot and kernel lockdown**
>
> Some Linux distributions restrict raw PCI config or MMIO access when Secure Boot enables kernel lockdown. If `/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/config` refuses full reads, disable Secure Boot for the capture machine, reboot, and try again. Document the state. Do not silently downgrade a failed 4KB capture into a screenshot.

Capture workflow:

```bash
#!/usr/bin/env bash
set -euo pipefail

BDF="${1:-0000:01:00.0}"
OUT="${2:-donor-offline-capture}"

mkdir -p "$OUT"

echo "[*] Capture target: $BDF"
echo "[*] Output folder:  $OUT"

if command -v mokutil >/dev/null 2>&1; then
    mokutil --sb-state | tee "$OUT/secure-boot-state.txt"
else
    echo "mokutil not installed; Secure Boot state not recorded" | tee "$OUT/secure-boot-state.txt"
fi

test -e "/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/config"
test -r "/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/config"

lspci -s "$BDF" -nn      | tee "$OUT/lspci-nn.txt"
lspci -s "$BDF" -vvv     | tee "$OUT/lspci-vvv.txt"
lspci -s "$BDF" -xxxx    > "$OUT/config-256.txt"
lspci -s "$BDF" -xxxxxxx > "$OUT/config-4096.txt" || true

cat "/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/resource" > "$OUT/resource.txt"
ls -l "/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF"/resource* > "$OUT/resource-files.txt"

sudo dd \
    if="/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/config" \
    of="$OUT/donor_extended_cfg.bin" \
    bs=1 \
    count=4096 \
    status=progress

ACTUAL_SIZE="$(stat -c '%s' "$OUT/donor_extended_cfg.bin")"
echo "$ACTUAL_SIZE" > "$OUT/donor_extended_cfg.size"

if [ "$ACTUAL_SIZE" -ne 4096 ]; then
    echo "[!] Bad capture size: expected 4096 bytes, got $ACTUAL_SIZE"
    exit 1
fi

hexdump -C "$OUT/donor_extended_cfg.bin" | tee "$OUT/donor_extended_cfg.hexdump.txt" >/dev/null
sha256sum "$OUT"/* | tee "$OUT/SHA256SUMS"

echo "[+] Raw 4096-byte config capture complete:"
echo "    $OUT/donor_extended_cfg.bin"
```

Run:

```bash
chmod +x capture-donor-raw.sh
sudo ./capture-donor-raw.sh 0000:01:00.0 donor-rtl8125-raw
```

The same capture as a single command:

```bash
sudo dd if=/sys/bus/pci/devices/0000:01:00.0/config of=donor_extended_cfg.bin bs=1 count=4096 status=progress
```

A complete dump run ends with:

```text
4096 bytes copied
donor_extended_cfg.bin size = 4096
SHA256SUMS generated
0x000 bytes match donor VID/DID
0x100 contains extended capability header or documented zero
```

The capture is incomplete if:

```text
Permission denied
Operation not permitted
Only 256 bytes copied
0x100-0xFFF all zero when donor should expose extended capabilities
```

Fix the capture machine. Do not patch around a bad donor dump.

### A.8 Convert Raw Binary Dump to PCILeech COE and WriteMask

The script reads `donor_extended_cfg.bin`, sanitizes fields that should not be cloned, and writes both COE files, `vivado_pci_core_config.tcl`, and a short report.

COE and WriteMask generation stay unchanged. The script also builds Vivado Tcl from the identity bytes and BAR0 size/type in Linux `resource.txt`. Source that file instead of retyping the hard-IP settings in the GUI.

Install the outputs here:

| Output | Install location |
|--------|------------------|
| `pcileech_cfgspace.coe` | `ip/pcileech_cfgspace.coe` |
| `pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe` | `ip/pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe` |
| `vivado_pci_core_config.tcl` | source in Vivado Tcl Console before regenerating PCIe IP output products |
| `donor_raw_report.md` | keep in donor evidence folder |

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/linux_raw_cfg_to_pcileech_coe.py
```

```python
import argparse
import hashlib
from pathlib import Path

CONFIG_SIZE = 4096
DWORD_COUNT = CONFIG_SIZE // 4

CAP_ID_PM = 0x01
CAP_ID_MSI = 0x05
CAP_ID_PCIE = 0x10
CAP_ID_MSIX = 0x11

EXT_ID_AER = 0x0001
EXT_ID_DSN = 0x0003

def u16le(buf, off):
    return buf[off] | (buf[off + 1] << 8)

def u32le(buf, off):
    return (
        buf[off]
        | (buf[off + 1] << 8)
        | (buf[off + 2] << 16)
        | (buf[off + 3] << 24)
    )

def put_u16le(buf, off, value):
    buf[off] = value & 0xFF
    buf[off + 1] = (value >> 8) & 0xFF

def put_u32le(buf, off, value):
    buf[off] = value & 0xFF
    buf[off + 1] = (value >> 8) & 0xFF
    buf[off + 2] = (value >> 16) & 0xFF
    buf[off + 3] = (value >> 24) & 0xFF

def coe_dwords_from_bytes(buf):
    return [u32le(buf, i * 4) for i in range(DWORD_COUNT)]

def write_coe(path, dwords):
    with open(path, "w", encoding="ascii", newline="\n") as f:
        f.write("memory_initialization_radix=16;\n")
        f.write("memory_initialization_vector=\n")
        for index, value in enumerate(dwords):
            f.write(f"{value:08X}")
            f.write(";\n" if index == len(dwords) - 1 else ",\n")

def sha256_file(path):
    h = hashlib.sha256()
    with open(path, "rb") as f:
        for block in iter(lambda: f.read(1024 * 1024), b""):
            h.update(block)
    return h.hexdigest()

def walk_standard_caps(buf):
    caps = []
    ptr = buf[0x34]
    seen = set()

    while ptr:
        if ptr in seen:
            raise SystemExit(f"Standard capability loop at 0x{ptr:02X}")
        if ptr < 0x40 or ptr > 0xFC:
            raise SystemExit(f"Bad standard capability pointer 0x{ptr:02X}")
        if ptr & 0x03:
            raise SystemExit(f"Unaligned standard capability pointer 0x{ptr:02X}")

        seen.add(ptr)
        cap_id = buf[ptr]
        next_ptr = buf[ptr + 1]
        caps.append((ptr, cap_id, next_ptr))
        ptr = next_ptr

    return caps

def walk_extended_caps(buf):
    caps = []
    ptr = 0x100
    seen = set()

    while ptr:
        if ptr in seen:
            raise SystemExit(f"Extended capability loop at 0x{ptr:03X}")
        if ptr < 0x100 or ptr >= CONFIG_SIZE:
            raise SystemExit(f"Bad extended capability pointer 0x{ptr:03X}")
        if ptr & 0x03:
            raise SystemExit(f"Unaligned extended capability pointer 0x{ptr:03X}")

        hdr = u32le(buf, ptr)
        if hdr == 0:
            break

        ext_id = hdr & 0xFFFF
        version = (hdr >> 16) & 0xF
        next_ptr = (hdr >> 20) & 0xFFF
        caps.append((ptr, ext_id, version, next_ptr))

        seen.add(ptr)
        ptr = next_ptr

    return caps

def mask_bits(mask_dwords, byte_offset, bit_count, bit_mask):
    for bit in range(bit_count):
        if bit_mask & (1 << bit):
            absolute_bit = byte_offset * 8 + bit
            dword_index = absolute_bit // 32
            bit_index = absolute_bit % 32
            if dword_index >= len(mask_dwords):
                raise SystemExit(f"WriteMask bit outside config space: byte 0x{byte_offset:03X}")
            mask_dwords[dword_index] |= (1 << bit_index)

def sanitize_cfg(buf, keep_command, keep_bars):
    out = bytearray(buf)

    if not keep_command:
        status = u16le(out, 0x06)
        put_u16le(out, 0x04, 0x0000)
        put_u16le(out, 0x06, status)

    if not keep_bars:
        for off in range(0x10, 0x28, 4):
            put_u32le(out, off, 0x00000000)

    return out

def parse_linux_resource_file(path):
    entries = []

    with open(path, "r", encoding="ascii", errors="strict") as f:
        for index, line in enumerate(f):
            parts = line.strip().split()
            if len(parts) < 3:
                continue

            start = int(parts[0], 16)
            end = int(parts[1], 16)
            flags = int(parts[2], 16)

            if start == 0 and end == 0:
                size = 0
            elif end >= start:
                size = end - start + 1
            else:
                size = 0

            entries.append({
                "index": index,
                "start": start,
                "end": end,
                "flags": flags,
                "size": size,
            })

    return entries

def vivado_bar_size_name(size_bytes):
    size_map = {
        128: "128_Bytes",
        256: "256_Bytes",
        512: "512_Bytes",
        1024: "1_KB",
        2048: "2_KB",
        4096: "4_KB",
        8192: "8_KB",
        16384: "16_KB",
        32768: "32_KB",
        65536: "64_KB",
        131072: "128_KB",
        262144: "256_KB",
        524288: "512_KB",
        1048576: "1_MB",
        2097152: "2_MB",
        4194304: "4_MB",
        8388608: "8_MB",
        16777216: "16_MB",
        33554432: "32_MB",
        67108864: "64_MB",
        134217728: "128_MB",
        268435456: "256_MB",
    }

    if size_bytes not in size_map:
        raise SystemExit(f"Unsupported BAR size for Vivado Tcl mapping: {size_bytes} bytes")

    return size_map[size_bytes]

def build_bar0_vivado_config(buf, resource_entries, override_bar0_size):
    bar0_raw = u32le(buf, 0x10)
    bar0_is_io = bool(bar0_raw & 0x1)
    bar0_type = "IO" if bar0_is_io else "Memory"

    if override_bar0_size is not None:
        bar0_size_bytes = override_bar0_size
    elif resource_entries and len(resource_entries) >= 1:
        bar0_size_bytes = resource_entries[0]["size"]
    else:
        raise SystemExit(
            "BAR0 size cannot be derived from config bytes alone. "
            "Place Linux resource.txt next to donor_extended_cfg.bin or pass --bar0-size-bytes."
        )

    bar0_enabled = bar0_size_bytes > 0
    bar0_size = vivado_bar_size_name(bar0_size_bytes) if bar0_enabled else "4_KB"

    return {
        "enabled": bar0_enabled,
        "size_bytes": bar0_size_bytes,
        "size": bar0_size,
        "type": bar0_type,
        "raw": bar0_raw,
    }

def write_vivado_pci_core_tcl(path, vendor_id, device_id, revision_id, class_code, subsystem_vendor, subsystem_id, bar0_config):
    bar0_enabled_text = "true" if bar0_config["enabled"] else "false"

    lines = [
        "# Auto-generated from donor physical PCIe config capture.",
        "# Do not hand-type these values in Vivado GUI.",
        "# Let code align code.",
        "",
        "set pcie_ip [get_ips pcie_7x_0]",
        "if { [llength $pcie_ip] != 1 } {",
        "  error \"Expected exactly one PCIe IP named pcie_7x_0\"",
        "}",
        "",
        "# Auto-generated PCIe Core alignment from donor physical config capture.",
        "# Do not align IDs and BAR sizes by hand in Vivado GUI.",
        "set_property -dict [list \\",
        f"  CONFIG.vendor_id {{{vendor_id:04X}}} \\",
        f"  CONFIG.device_id {{{device_id:04X}}} \\",
        f"  CONFIG.revision_id {{{revision_id:02X}}} \\",
        f"  CONFIG.class_code {{{class_code:06X}}} \\",
        f"  CONFIG.subsystem_vendor_id {{{subsystem_vendor:04X}}} \\",
        f"  CONFIG.subsystem_id {{{subsystem_id:04X}}} \\",
        f"  CONFIG.bar0_enabled {{{bar0_enabled_text}}} \\",
        f"  CONFIG.bar0_size {{{bar0_config['size']}}} \\",
        f"  CONFIG.bar0_type {{{bar0_config['type']}}} \\",
        "] [get_ips pcie_7x_0]",
        "",
        "report_property [get_ips pcie_7x_0]",
        "",
    ]

    with open(path, "w", encoding="utf-8", newline="\n") as f:
        f.write("\n".join(lines))

def build_writemask(buf, standard_caps, extended_caps):
    mask = [0] * DWORD_COUNT

    # Type 0 header basics.
    # Command Register bits: I/O Space, Memory Space, Bus Master, Interrupt Disable.
    # Status RW1C is not modeled by a plain mask; leave it read-only here.
    mask_bits(mask, 0x04, 16, 0x0407)

    # Interrupt Line is commonly writable. Interrupt Pin remains read-only.
    mask_bits(mask, 0x3C, 8, 0xFF)

    for ptr, cap_id, _next_ptr in standard_caps:
        if cap_id == CAP_ID_PM:
            # PMCSR at PM capability + 0x04:
            # bits 1:0 PowerState, bit 8 PME Enable.
            # bit 15 PME Status is RW1C; do not claim plain WriteMask models it.
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x04, 16, 0x0103)

        elif cap_id == CAP_ID_MSI:
            msg_ctl = u16le(buf, ptr + 0x02)
            is_64bit = bool(msg_ctl & (1 << 7))
            per_vector_masking = bool(msg_ctl & (1 << 8))

            # Message Control: MSI Enable and Multiple Message Enable.
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x02, 16, 0x0071)

            # Message Address.
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x04, 32, 0xFFFFFFFF)

            if is_64bit:
                mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x08, 32, 0xFFFFFFFF)
                data_off = ptr + 0x0C
                mask_off = ptr + 0x10
            else:
                data_off = ptr + 0x08
                mask_off = ptr + 0x0C

            # Message Data.
            mask_bits(mask, data_off, 16, 0xFFFF)

            # Per-vector Mask Bits are writable; Pending Bits are not.
            if per_vector_masking:
                mask_bits(mask, mask_off, 32, 0xFFFFFFFF)

        elif cap_id == CAP_ID_MSIX:
            # MSI-X Message Control: Function Mask and MSI-X Enable.
            # Table/PBA behavior lives in BAR memory, not in this config mask.
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x02, 16, 0xC000)

        elif cap_id == CAP_ID_PCIE:
            # Device Control and Link Control are writable in real devices.
            # Refine per donor after readback.
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x08, 16, 0xFFFF)
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x10, 16, 0xFFFF)

    for ptr, ext_id, _version, _next_ptr in extended_caps:
        if ext_id == EXT_ID_AER:
            # AER status registers are RW1C and need real logic for perfect behavior.
            # Masks/control registers are writable.
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x08, 32, 0xFFFFFFFF)  # Uncorrectable Error Mask
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x0C, 32, 0xFFFFFFFF)  # Uncorrectable Error Severity
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x14, 32, 0xFFFFFFFF)  # Correctable Error Mask
            mask_bits(mask, ptr + 0x18, 32, 0xFFFFFFFF)  # Advanced Error Cap/Control
        elif ext_id == EXT_ID_DSN:
            # DSN is identity data. Keep it read-only.
            pass

    return mask

def format_caps_report(standard_caps, extended_caps):
    lines = []
    lines.append("## Standard Capabilities")
    if standard_caps:
        for ptr, cap_id, next_ptr in standard_caps:
            lines.append(f"- 0x{ptr:02X}: id=0x{cap_id:02X}, next=0x{next_ptr:02X}")
    else:
        lines.append("- none")

    lines.append("")
    lines.append("## Extended Capabilities")
    if extended_caps:
        for ptr, ext_id, version, next_ptr in extended_caps:
            lines.append(f"- 0x{ptr:03X}: id=0x{ext_id:04X}, version={version}, next=0x{next_ptr:03X}")
    else:
        lines.append("- none")

    return "\n".join(lines)

def main():
    parser = argparse.ArgumentParser(
        description="Convert a 4096-byte Linux sysfs PCI config dump into PCILeech COE files."
    )
    parser.add_argument("input_bin", help="4096-byte donor_extended_cfg.bin from Linux sysfs")
    parser.add_argument("output_dir", help="Output directory for COE files and report")
    parser.add_argument("--keep-command", action="store_true", help="Do not clear captured Command register bits in cfgspace COE")
    parser.add_argument("--keep-bars", action="store_true", help="Do not clear captured runtime BAR values in cfgspace COE")
    parser.add_argument("--resource-file", default=None, help="Linux sysfs resource.txt. Defaults to resource.txt next to input_bin")
    parser.add_argument("--bar0-size-bytes", type=int, default=None, help="Manual BAR0 size override if resource.txt is unavailable")
    args = parser.parse_args()

    input_path = Path(args.input_bin)
    output_dir = Path(args.output_dir)
    output_dir.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)

    raw = input_path.read_bytes()
    if len(raw) != CONFIG_SIZE:
        raise SystemExit(f"Expected 4096 bytes, got {len(raw)} bytes: {input_path}")

    vendor_id = u16le(raw, 0x00)
    device_id = u16le(raw, 0x02)
    revision_id = raw[0x08]
    class_code = (raw[0x0B] << 16) | (raw[0x0A] << 8) | raw[0x09]
    subsystem_vendor = u16le(raw, 0x2C)
    subsystem_id = u16le(raw, 0x2E)

    standard_caps = walk_standard_caps(raw) if (u16le(raw, 0x06) & (1 << 4)) else []
    extended_caps = walk_extended_caps(raw)

    resource_path = Path(args.resource_file) if args.resource_file else (input_path.parent / "resource.txt")
    resource_entries = parse_linux_resource_file(resource_path) if resource_path.exists() else []
    bar0_config = build_bar0_vivado_config(raw, resource_entries, args.bar0_size_bytes)

    sanitized = sanitize_cfg(raw, keep_command=args.keep_command, keep_bars=args.keep_bars)
    cfg_dwords = coe_dwords_from_bytes(sanitized)
    mask_dwords = build_writemask(raw, standard_caps, extended_caps)

    cfg_path = output_dir / "pcileech_cfgspace.coe"
    mask_path = output_dir / "pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe"
    tcl_path = output_dir / "vivado_pci_core_config.tcl"
    report_path = output_dir / "donor_raw_report.md"

    write_coe(cfg_path, cfg_dwords)
    write_coe(mask_path, mask_dwords)
    write_vivado_pci_core_tcl(
        tcl_path,
        vendor_id,
        device_id,
        revision_id,
        class_code,
        subsystem_vendor,
        subsystem_id,
        bar0_config,
    )

    report = []
    report.append("# Donor Raw Config Conversion Report")
    report.append("")
    report.append(f"- Input: `{input_path}`")
    report.append(f"- Input SHA256: `{sha256_file(input_path)}`")
    report.append(f"- Linux resource file: `{resource_path}`")
    report.append(f"- Vendor ID: `0x{vendor_id:04X}`")
    report.append(f"- Device ID: `0x{device_id:04X}`")
    report.append(f"- Revision ID: `0x{revision_id:02X}`")
    report.append(f"- Class Code: `0x{class_code:06X}`")
    report.append(f"- Subsystem Vendor ID: `0x{subsystem_vendor:04X}`")
    report.append(f"- Subsystem ID: `0x{subsystem_id:04X}`")
    report.append(f"- BAR0 enabled: `{bar0_config['enabled']}`")
    report.append(f"- BAR0 raw config DWORD: `0x{bar0_config['raw']:08X}`")
    report.append(f"- BAR0 size bytes: `{bar0_config['size_bytes']}`")
    report.append(f"- BAR0 Vivado size: `{bar0_config['size']}`")
    report.append(f"- BAR0 Vivado type: `{bar0_config['type']}`")
    report.append(f"- Command register cleared in COE: `{not args.keep_command}`")
    report.append(f"- Runtime BAR values cleared in COE: `{not args.keep_bars}`")
    report.append("")
    report.append(format_caps_report(standard_caps, extended_caps))
    report.append("")
    report.append("## Generated Files")
    report.append(f"- `{cfg_path.name}`")
    report.append(f"- `{mask_path.name}`")
    report.append(f"- `{tcl_path.name}`")
    report.append("")
    report.append("## Hard Warnings")
    report.append("- Plain WriteMask does not perfectly model RW1C status behavior.")
    report.append("- MSI-X table and PBA behavior must be implemented in BAR memory.")
    report.append("- Runtime BAR addresses from Linux/Windows are cleared by default.")
    report.append("- BAR size for Vivado Tcl comes from Linux resource.txt or --bar0-size-bytes, not from the runtime BAR DWORD alone.")
    report.append("- Review every writable bit against donor readback before calling it final.")
    with open(report_path, "w", encoding="utf-8", newline="\n") as f:
        f.write("\n".join(report) + "\n")

    print("Generated:", cfg_path)
    print("Generated:", mask_path)
    print("Generated:", tcl_path)
    print("Generated:", report_path)
    print(f"VID/DID: {vendor_id:04X}:{device_id:04X}")
    print(f"Class/Revision: {class_code:06X} rev {revision_id:02X}")
    print(f"Subsystem: {subsystem_vendor:04X}:{subsystem_id:04X}")
    print(f"BAR0: enabled={bar0_config['enabled']} size={bar0_config['size']} type={bar0_config['type']}")
    print("Standard capabilities:", len(standard_caps))
    print("Extended capabilities:", len(extended_caps))

if __name__ == "__main__":
    main()
```

Run:

```bash
python3 linux_raw_cfg_to_pcileech_coe.py donor-rtl8125-raw/donor_extended_cfg.bin donor-rtl8125-raw/generated
```

The script automatically looks for:

```text
donor-rtl8125-raw/resource.txt
```

That file is required for automatic BAR0 size extraction. PCI config bytes alone show runtime BAR flags/address bits; they do not prove aperture size. The Linux `resource.txt` file gives the assigned resource window size.

Windows PowerShell works too:

```powershell
python C:\dma\tools\linux_raw_cfg_to_pcileech_coe.py C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\donor_extended_cfg.bin C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\generated
```

Install the generated files:

```text
generated/pcileech_cfgspace.coe            -> ip/pcileech_cfgspace.coe
generated/pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe  -> ip/pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe
generated/vivado_pci_core_config.tcl        -> source in Vivado Tcl Console
generated/donor_raw_report.md              -> donor evidence folder
```

Source the generated Tcl instead of retyping IDs and BAR sizes in the Vivado GUI:

```tcl
source C:/dma/donor/rtl8125/generated/vivado_pci_core_config.tcl
```

This keeps the hard-IP settings tied to the same donor capture as the COE files.

Example generated Tcl:

```tcl
# Auto-generated from donor physical PCIe config capture.
# Do not hand-type these values in Vivado GUI.
# Keep the capture data and PCIe IP settings in sync.

set pcie_ip [get_ips pcie_7x_0]
if { [llength $pcie_ip] != 1 } {
  error "Expected exactly one PCIe IP named pcie_7x_0"
}

# Auto-generated PCIe Core alignment from donor physical config capture.
# Do not align IDs and BAR sizes by hand in Vivado GUI.
set_property -dict [list \
  CONFIG.vendor_id {10EC} \
  CONFIG.device_id {8125} \
  CONFIG.revision_id {05} \
  CONFIG.class_code {020000} \
  CONFIG.subsystem_vendor_id {10EC} \
  CONFIG.subsystem_id {0123} \
  CONFIG.bar0_enabled {true} \
  CONFIG.bar0_size {16_KB} \
  CONFIG.bar0_type {Memory} \
] [get_ips pcie_7x_0]

report_property [get_ips pcie_7x_0]
```

After sourcing it:

```text
Reset output products for the PCIe IP.
Regenerate output products.
Rebuild.
Then verify target readback.
```

A clean conversion prints:

```text
Generated: donor-rtl8125-raw/generated/pcileech_cfgspace.coe
Generated: donor-rtl8125-raw/generated/pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe
Generated: donor-rtl8125-raw/generated/vivado_pci_core_config.tcl
Generated: donor-rtl8125-raw/generated/donor_raw_report.md
VID/DID: 10EC:8125
Class/Revision: 020000 rev 05
Subsystem: 10EC:0123
BAR0: enabled=True size=16_KB type=Memory
Standard capabilities: 5
Extended capabilities: 3
```

Stop and inspect the capture on:

```text
Expected 4096 bytes, got 256 bytes
BAR0 size cannot be derived from config bytes alone
Standard capability loop at 0x40
Bad extended capability pointer 0xFFC
```

If the script fails, the donor capture is bad or the donor has a layout you must inspect manually. Do not force the script to produce a COE from broken evidence.

### A.9 Raw Dump Conversion Review Checklist

Before Vivado:

```text
[ ] donor_extended_cfg.bin is exactly 4096 bytes
[ ] SHA256SUMS saved
[ ] 0x00 VID/DID matches donor
[ ] 0x08 class/revision matches donor
[ ] 0x2C subsystem IDs match donor
[ ] 0x34 capability pointer walks cleanly
[ ] 0x100 extended capability chain walks cleanly or is documented absent
[ ] runtime BAR values were cleared unless you intentionally own that path
[ ] Command register initial state was reviewed
[ ] PMCSR offset found from capability chain
[ ] MSI/MSI-X writable fields found from capability chain
[ ] RW1C limitations documented
[ ] generated COE files installed into the correct Vivado IP
[ ] vivado_pci_core_config.tcl generated
[ ] Vivado PCIe IP sourced from Tcl instead of hand-entered GUI values
[ ] PCIe IP output products regenerated after Tcl source
```

Raw bytes are better than screenshots. Raw bytes converted blindly are still a fast way to build broken firmware.

### A.10 What a Complete Raw Capture Contains

For a complete raw capture, save:

- `lspci -nn` saved;
- `lspci -vvv` saved;
- `lspci -xxxxxxx` attempted and limitation recorded if incomplete;
- `/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/config` copied if accessible;
- `donor_extended_cfg.bin` is exactly 4096 bytes when claiming full capture;
- `pcileech_cfgspace.coe` generated from raw bytes or the limitation is documented;
- `pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe` generated or the WriteMask source is documented;
- resource layout saved;
- required BAR binary dumps saved;
- SHA256 hashes saved;
- donor state during capture documented.

---

## Appendix B: Advanced Validation Commands

Appendix B supplements the Windows readback path.

### B.1 Linux Config Readback

After flashing the target firmware and booting a Linux test target:

```bash
lspci -nn
lspci -s "$BDF" -vvv
lspci -s "$BDF" -xxxx
lspci -s "$BDF" -xxxxxxx
```

Compare against donor:

```text
0x00  VID/DID
0x08  Revision/Class
0x10  BAR0
0x2C  Subsystem IDs
0x34  Capability Pointer
0x100 Extended Capability Header
```

Classify differences as:

- stable field mismatch;
- runtime field difference;
- intentional difference;
- bug.

### B.2 `setpci` Write Tests

Use only on a lab machine.

Read Command:

```bash
sudo setpci -s "$BDF" COMMAND
```

Save original value:

```bash
ORIG=$(sudo setpci -s "$BDF" COMMAND)
```

Test writable Command bits:

```bash
sudo setpci -s "$BDF" COMMAND=0006
sudo setpci -s "$BDF" COMMAND
sudo setpci -s "$BDF" COMMAND="$ORIG"
```

Test read-only identity behavior:

```bash
sudo setpci -s "$BDF" 00.L=ffffffff
sudo setpci -s "$BDF" 00.L
```

What should happen:

- VID/DID should not become `ffff:ffff`;
- allowed Command bits should change;
- unsupported bits should not stick;
- device should remain present.

If Command does not change, check `rw[206]` in `src/pcileech_fifo.sv` and the WriteMask COE.

If VID/DID changes, your WriteMask is dangerous.

### B.3 BAR Readback on Linux

First 4KB of BAR0:

```bash
sudo dd if="/sys/bus/pci/devices/$BDF/resource0" of=target-bar0-4k.bin bs=4096 count=1 iflag=direct
hexdump -C target-bar0-4k.bin | head -40
```

Compare hashes only when static content is expected:

```bash
sha256sum donor-bar0-4k.bin target-bar0-4k.bin
```

Do not expect hashes to match for stateful registers, counters, interrupt tables, or status fields.

### B.4 PCILeech Probe and Benchmark

From the PCILeech control machine:

```text
pcileech probe
pcileech benchmark
```

Record:

```text
pcileech version:
connection type:
board:
target:
probe output:
benchmark output:
stability notes:
```

PCILeech benchmark proves the DMA communication path works. It does not prove donor BAR behavior, WriteMask correctness, or driver compatibility.

### B.5 Build Archive and Hashes

Linux:

```bash
sha256sum *.bit *.bin > SHA256SUMS.txt
```

Windows PowerShell:

```powershell
Get-FileHash .\firmware.bit -Algorithm SHA256
Get-FileHash .\firmware.bin -Algorithm SHA256
```

Recommended archive:

```text
builds/2026-xx-xx-board-donor-v1/
  notes.md
  git-diff.patch
  vivado-version.txt
  windows-version.txt
  upstream-commit.txt
  board-folder.txt
  fpga-part-package.txt
  build.log
  timing-summary.rpt
  utilization.rpt
  firmware.bit
  firmware.bin
  SHA256SUMS.txt
  donor-config-4096.bin
  target-config-4096.bin
  donor-bar0-4k.bin
  target-bar0-4k.bin
  pcileech-probe.txt
  pcileech-benchmark.txt
  screenshots/
```

Do not ship or archive a file named `final.bin` with no provenance.

### B.6 Useful Vivado Tcl Commands

```tcl
source vivado_generate_project.tcl -notrace
source vivado_build.tcl -notrace
report_timing_summary -file timing_summary.txt
report_utilization -file utilization.txt
```

Optional IP management check:

```tcl
report_ip_status
```

If you manually edited generated files, re-check them after every IP regenerate.

---

## Appendix C: Glossary

| Term | Definition |
|------|------------|
| **AER** | Advanced Error Reporting, a PCIe extended capability for error reporting and control. |
| **BAR** | Base Address Register; declares memory or I/O resources requested by a PCIe device. |
| **BDF** | Bus:Device.Function address of a PCI/PCIe function. |
| **BRAM** | Block RAM inside the FPGA. Used for static config-space or BAR response data. |
| **CFGTLP** | PCIe configuration transaction layer packet. |
| **COE** | Vivado memory initialization file used to initialize BRAM/ROM IP. |
| **Command Register** | PCI config register controlling I/O Space, Memory Space, Bus Master, and other bits. |
| **DSN** | Device Serial Number, a PCIe extended capability containing a 64-bit serial value. |
| **DWORD** | 32-bit value. |
| **Endpoint** | PCIe device below the root complex; the donor and DMA board present as endpoints. |
| **Extended Capability** | PCIe capability structure beginning at config-space offset `0x100`. |
| **IOMMU / VT-d / AMD-Vi** | DMA remapping/protection features. Useful in some donor capture workflows; may block DMA testing depending on target setup. |
| **MSI** | Message Signaled Interrupt. Interrupt data is configured through PCI config-space fields. |
| **MSI-X** | Extended MSI. Uses config-space capability plus table/PBA structures inside a BAR. |
| **PMCSR** | Power Management Control/Status Register inside the PM capability. |
| **PIO** | Programmed I/O, often used for simple BAR access handling. |
| **RW1C** | Read/Write-1-to-Clear. Writing `1` clears the status bit. |
| **Shadow Config Space** | BRAM-backed config-space response path used to return donor-like config bytes. |
| **TLP** | Transaction Layer Packet, the packet format used by PCIe transactions. |
| **WriteMask** | Per-bit mask controlling which config-space bits may be updated by host writes. |
| **XCI** | Xilinx Core Instance file containing Vivado IP configuration. |
| **Zero4K** | Simple 4KB static BAR responder. Useful, but not full BAR emulation. |

---

## Appendix D: File Reference

| File | Purpose |
|------|---------|
| `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv` | PCIe config management, `cfg_dsn`, Command Register auto-set `rw[21]`, Status auto-clear `rw[20]`. |
| `src/pcileech_fifo.sv` | CFGTLP shadow switches. Shadow `rw[203]` and shadow write-enable `rw[206]` are here. |
| `src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv` | Shadow config-space read/write logic and WriteMask application. |
| `src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv` | BAR routing and BAR responder logic. |
| `ip/pcileech_cfgspace.coe` | Shadow config-space BRAM initialization. |
| `ip/pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe` | Config-space WriteMask ROM initialization. |
| `ip/pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe` | Zero4K BAR BRAM initialization. |
| `pcie_7x_0.xci` | Vivado PCIe IP configuration, including IDs and BAR settings when exposed. |
| `.gen/sources_1/ip/.../pcie_7x_0_core_top.v` | Vivado-generated PCIe wrapper. It may be overwritten by IP regeneration. |
| `vivado_generate_project.tcl` | Board project generation script. Use the script from the correct board folder. |
| `vivado_build.tcl` | Board build script. Use the script from the correct board folder. |
| `*.bit` | Vivado bitstream file. |
| `*.bin` | Raw/programming image when generated by the project flow. |

Critical reminders:

- `rw[203]` and shadow `rw[206]` are in `src/pcileech_fifo.sv`.
- `rw[21]` in `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv` is Command Register auto-set, not master abort enable.
- Generated `.gen` files are not stable hand-written source.
- COE files must be attached to the correct generated BRAM/ROM IP and regenerated.

---
