- EEPROM/NVM window returns specific values
- MAC address appears in a device-specific location
- MSI-X table writes stick
- queue/doorbell registers behave safely

If your donor driver reads these and gets nonsense, Code 10 is normal.

### 11.5 When the Driver Does Not Bind

If driver binding fails, stop changing VID/DID.

Check:

- BAR readback
- MSI/MSI-X
- PMCSR
- EEPROM/NVM window
- reset bit
- status bit
- interrupt mask
- Device Manager Events
- Windows Event Viewer if needed

Once identity is correct, VID/DID is no longer the variable.

### 11.6 Completion Latency Shaping

BAR data is only half the job. Timing matters too.

Real devices do not answer every MMIO read with one permanent pattern. Reads may depend on state or settle after reset. A fixed DWORD with fixed timing proves the completion path is alive; it does not model the device.

Use the real upstream-style files:

| File | What to touch |
|------|---------------|
| `src/pcileech_pcie_a7.sv` | Xilinx 7 Series PCIe wrapper. RX from the core is commonly wired as `m_axis_rx_tdata` into `tlp_rx.data`. |
| `src/pcileech_pcie_tlp_a7.sv` | TLP pipeline around RX/TX handling. |
| `src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv` | BAR routing and BAR responder selection. This is the usual place for BAR behavior work. |
| `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv` | Config/control context and PCIe interrupt interface signals. |

Critical rule from `pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv`: user BAR responder cores must keep a known read latency. Do not make BAR0 two clocks, BAR1 random, and BAR2 instant unless you understand the completion mux and timing.

A clean way to add controlled latency is to pipeline the response context/data after your BAR logic has produced a DWORD:

```systemverilog
// Drop this helper near the BAR implementation area in:
// src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
//
// Keep LATENCY_CLKS consistent with the rest of your BAR responders.
// 16 clocks at 62.5 MHz is about 256 ns. Microsecond-level behavior
// needs tens or hundreds of clocks depending on your PCIe user clock.
module pcileech_bar_latency_pipe #(
    parameter integer LATENCY_CLKS = 16
)(
    input               rst,
    input               clk,

    input  [87:0]       rd_req_ctx,
    input  [31:0]       rd_req_data,
    input               rd_req_valid,

    output bit [87:0]   rd_rsp_ctx,
    output bit [31:0]   rd_rsp_data,
    output bit          rd_rsp_valid
);

    bit [87:0] ctx_pipe   [0:LATENCY_CLKS-1];
    bit [31:0] data_pipe  [0:LATENCY_CLKS-1];
    bit        valid_pipe [0:LATENCY_CLKS-1];
    integer i;

    always @ (posedge clk) begin
        if (rst) begin
            for (i = 0; i < LATENCY_CLKS; i = i + 1) begin
                ctx_pipe[i]   <= 88'd0;
                data_pipe[i]  <= 32'd0;
                valid_pipe[i] <= 1'b0;
            end
        end else begin
            ctx_pipe[0]   <= rd_req_ctx;
            data_pipe[0]  <= rd_req_data;
            valid_pipe[0] <= rd_req_valid;

            for (i = 1; i < LATENCY_CLKS; i = i + 1) begin
                ctx_pipe[i]   <= ctx_pipe[i-1];
                data_pipe[i]  <= data_pipe[i-1];
                valid_pipe[i] <= valid_pipe[i-1];
            end
        end
    end

    always @ (*) begin
        rd_rsp_ctx   = ctx_pipe[LATENCY_CLKS-1];
        rd_rsp_data  = data_pipe[LATENCY_CLKS-1];
        rd_rsp_valid = valid_pipe[LATENCY_CLKS-1];
    end

endmodule
```

Use it inside a real BAR implementation, not as a random top-level patch:

```systemverilog
wire [87:0] raw_rsp_ctx;
wire [31:0] raw_rsp_data;
wire        raw_rsp_valid;

// Your donor-specific register decode produces raw_rsp_* first.
// Then the latency pipe shapes the external completion timing.
pcileech_bar_latency_pipe #(
    .LATENCY_CLKS(16)
) i_bar0_latency (
    .rst            ( rst           ),
    .clk            ( clk           ),
    .rd_req_ctx     ( raw_rsp_ctx   ),
    .rd_req_data    ( raw_rsp_data  ),
    .rd_req_valid   ( raw_rsp_valid ),
    .rd_rsp_ctx     ( rd_rsp_ctx    ),
    .rd_rsp_data    ( rd_rsp_data   ),
    .rd_rsp_valid   ( rd_rsp_valid  )
);
```

If you add this to one exposed BAR, normalize the other exposed responders or prove they never participate in the same path. The existing example cores are often two-clock responders; mixing active responders with different unknown latencies is a debugging trap.

Start with fixed delay classes:

| Register type | Practical lab delay model |
|---------------|---------------------------|
| simple status/capability read | fixed short delay |
| reset/status transition | delay until your reset state machine completes |
| EEPROM/NVM-like window | longer fixed delay or staged ready bit |
| queue/doorbell register | write stores state, readback follows donor behavior |

Do not blindly add random jitter to config reads. If the host is sizing BARs, walking capabilities, or clearing status bits during early enumeration, inconsistent timing can turn a normal bug into a POST hang.

### 11.7 Interrupt Activity Heartbeat for Lab Driver Validation

Interrupts are not decoration. If the donor driver expects MSI/MSI-X activity and your firmware never drives the interrupt path, a driver bind can still fail or look dead under normal workload.

Not a substitute for real device logic. Use it as a lab heartbeat for the PCIe interrupt path, Windows driver event path, and config/MSI wiring.

> [!NOTE]
> **Do not confuse the two `rw[206]` locations**
>
> `src/pcileech_fifo.sv` uses `rw[206]` for config-shadow write enable. `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv` also has a local `rw[206]`, but there it drives `ctx.cfg_interrupt`. Same index, different module context. Editing the wrong one is how old tutorials create fake fixes.

Patch this into the existing update path of `src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv`. Do not create multiple always blocks that drive the same `rw[]` bits.

```systemverilog
// Lab interrupt heartbeat for MSI path validation.
// File: src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv
//
// Integrate into the existing rw[] update path. Do not double-drive
// rw[205], rw[206], rw[207], rw[199:192], or rw[204:200].

localparam integer IRQ_HEARTBEAT_CLKS = 32'd6_250_000; // ~100 ms at 62.5 MHz

bit [31:0] irq_heartbeat_ctr;
bit [3:0]  irq_pulse_ctr;

always @ (posedge clk) begin
    if (rst) begin
        irq_heartbeat_ctr <= 32'd0;
        irq_pulse_ctr     <= 4'd0;

        rw[199:192] <= 8'h00; // cfg_interrupt_di
        rw[204:200] <= 5'd0;  // cfg_pciecap_interrupt_msgnum
        rw[205]     <= 1'b0;  // cfg_interrupt_assert
        rw[206]     <= 1'b0;  // cfg_interrupt
        rw[207]     <= 1'b0;  // cfg_interrupt_stat
    end else begin
        rw[205] <= 1'b0;
        rw[206] <= 1'b0;
        rw[207] <= 1'b0;

        if (ctx.cfg_interrupt_msienable && ctx.cfg_interrupt_rdy) begin
            if (irq_heartbeat_ctr == IRQ_HEARTBEAT_CLKS) begin
                irq_heartbeat_ctr <= 32'd0;
                irq_pulse_ctr     <= 4'd4;
            end else begin
                irq_heartbeat_ctr <= irq_heartbeat_ctr + 1'b1;
            end

            if (irq_pulse_ctr != 0) begin
                irq_pulse_ctr <= irq_pulse_ctr - 1'b1;

                rw[199:192] <= 8'h00; // MSI data/vector input
                rw[204:200] <= 5'd0;  // interrupt message number
                rw[206]     <= 1'b1;  // one-cycle cfg_interrupt pulse
            end
        end else begin
            irq_heartbeat_ctr <= 32'd0;
            irq_pulse_ctr     <= 4'd0;
        end
    end
end
```

Important limits:

- This validates the interrupt path; it does not make your BAR model correct.
- MSI-X is not "done" just because an interrupt pulse exists.
- If MSI-X is exposed, the BAR that contains the MSI-X table and PBA must behave correctly.
- If the donor only raises interrupts after queue setup, a blind heartbeat can look wrong. Gate it behind a real BAR write if your donor behavior needs that.
- Save Windows Event Viewer, driver logs, and Arbor/TeleScan readback after testing. No readback means no proof.

### 11.8 TLP Lifecycle and PMCSR State Alignment

Static IDs are the easy part. The endpoint still has to behave consistently under real PCIe transactions.

The transaction lifecycle cannot contradict the config space, BAR behavior, power state, or interrupt plan.

#### 11.8.1 TLP Lifecycle Inside the FPGA

A Type 0 PCIe endpoint sees three practical transaction families during early bring-up:

```text
Host Root Complex
    |
    | 1. CfgRd0 / CfgWr0
    v
Xilinx 7 Series PCIe IP
    |
    | m_axis_rx_tdata / tlp_rx.data
    v
PCILeech TLP pipeline
    |
    +--> Config TLP path
    |       src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv
    |       - CfgRd0 returns shadow config data
    |       - CfgWr0 updates shadow data through WriteMask
    |
    +--> BAR path
    |       src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv
    |       - MemRd routes to selected BAR model
    |       - MemWr updates BAR model state
    |
    +--> Interrupt/control context
            src/pcileech_pcie_cfg_a7.sv
            - MSI/MSI-X enable state
            - PMCSR state from core context
            - function-level reset and link state signals
```

The important decode already exists in current upstream-style PCILeech files:

```systemverilog
// File: src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv
wire pcie_rx_rden = tlps_in.tvalid
                  && tlps_in.tuser[0]
                  && (tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0000010); // CfgRd0/CfgRd1

wire pcie_rx_wren = tlps_in.tvalid
                  && tlps_in.tuser[0]
                  && (tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0100010); // CfgWr0/CfgWr1

wire [9:0]  pcie_rx_addr  = tlps_in.tdata[75:66];
wire [31:0] pcie_rx_data  = tlps_in.tdata[127:96];
wire [3:0]  pcie_rx_be    = {tlps_in.tdata[32], tlps_in.tdata[33], tlps_in.tdata[34], tlps_in.tdata[35]};
```

BAR reads/writes then move through:

```text
src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv

MemRd TLP -> read engine -> rd_req_valid / rd_req_bar / rd_req_addr
selected BAR model -> rd_rsp_ctx / rd_rsp_data / rd_rsp_valid
completion engine -> Completion with Data

MemWr TLP -> write engine -> wr_valid / wr_bar / wr_addr / wr_be / wr_data
selected BAR model -> state update
```

The firmware must keep these answers coherent:

| Host action | Firmware behavior that must line up |
|------------|--------------------------------------|
| `CfgRd0` reads PM capability | PM capability exists at the advertised offset and links cleanly. |
| `CfgWr0` writes PMCSR D3hot | PMCSR readback changes and BAR model enters a low-power-safe state. |
| `CfgWr0` writes Command Memory Space Enable | BAR reads should only become meaningful after memory space is enabled. |
| `CfgWr0` enables MSI/MSI-X | Interrupt behavior must match the exposed capability and BAR table/PBA plan. |
| `MemRd` reads reset/status register | State machine must return a stable donor-like transition, not random zeros. |
| `MemWr` writes reset bit | Reset bit should self-clear if the donor does that. |

> [!NOTE]
> **Under the Hood - dynamic behavior beats static cloning**
>
> Raw config bytes are not enough when runtime behavior contradicts them. PMCSR in D3hot with D0-style BAR activity is wrong. So is enabled MSI-X with a dead table/PBA BAR. That is a config-space snapshot, not donor behavior.

#### 11.8.2 PMCSR Bits That Matter

Power Management Capability ID is `0x01`. PMCSR is normally at:

```text
PMCSR byte offset = PM capability base + 0x04
PMCSR size        = 16 bits
```

Core bits:

| PMCSR bit | Name | Practical behavior |
|----------|------|--------------------|
| `1:0` | PowerState | `00b` D0, `11b` D3hot are the states you will actually see most often. |
| `8` | PME Enable | Host may set this before low-power transitions. |
| `15` | PME Status | RW1C in real hardware. A plain WriteMask is not enough to model RW1C perfectly. |

Do not hardcode PMCSR at `0x44` unless your donor PM capability actually starts at `0x40`. Parse the capability chain.

#### 11.8.3 PMCSR State Mirror for Lab Builds

This module mirrors PMCSR state from Config Write TLPs. It does not replace the shadow BRAM path. It gives the BAR model a power-state signal so D0/D3 behavior stays aligned with PMCSR.

Feed it from the config-shadow decode in `src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv` or an equivalent tapped decode path.

```systemverilog
// File: src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv or a small included helper
//
// Purpose:
// - Track PMCSR PowerState and PME Enable from CfgWr0 traffic.
// - Provide device_in_d3hot to BAR responder logic.
// - Keep PME Status separate because plain WriteMask cannot model RW1C correctly.
//
// cfg_wr_addr is a DWORD address, matching pcie_rx_addr in the shadow module.
// PM_CAP_BASE is a byte offset from the donor capability chain.

module pcileech_pmcsr_state_model #(
    parameter integer PM_CAP_BASE = 8'h40
)(
    input              rst,
    input              clk,

    input              cfg_wr_valid,
    input      [9:0]   cfg_wr_addr,
    input      [3:0]   cfg_wr_be,
    input      [31:0]  cfg_wr_data,

    input              function_level_reset,

    output reg [1:0]   pm_power_state,
    output reg         pm_pme_enable,
    output reg         pm_pme_status,
    output wire        device_in_d0,
    output wire        device_in_d3hot
);

    localparam integer PMCSR_BYTE_OFFSET = PM_CAP_BASE + 4;
    localparam [9:0]   PMCSR_DW_ADDR     = ((PM_CAP_BASE + 4) >> 2);
    localparam integer PMCSR_BYTE_LANE   = ((PM_CAP_BASE + 4) & 3);

    wire cfg_wr_hits_pmcsr = cfg_wr_valid && (cfg_wr_addr == PMCSR_DW_ADDR);

    wire [15:0] pmcsr_wr_value =
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 0) ? cfg_wr_data[15:0]  :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 1) ? cfg_wr_data[23:8]  :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 2) ? cfg_wr_data[31:16] :
                                 16'h0000;

    wire pmcsr_low_byte_written =
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 0) ? cfg_wr_be[0] :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 1) ? cfg_wr_be[1] :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 2) ? cfg_wr_be[2] :
                                 cfg_wr_be[3];

    wire pmcsr_high_byte_written =
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 0) ? cfg_wr_be[1] :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 1) ? cfg_wr_be[2] :
        (PMCSR_BYTE_LANE == 2) ? cfg_wr_be[3] :
                                 1'b0;

    assign device_in_d0    = (pm_power_state == 2'b00);
    assign device_in_d3hot = (pm_power_state == 2'b11);

    always @ (posedge clk) begin
        if (rst || function_level_reset) begin
            pm_power_state <= 2'b00;
            pm_pme_enable  <= 1'b0;
            pm_pme_status  <= 1'b0;
        end else begin
            if (cfg_wr_hits_pmcsr && pmcsr_low_byte_written) begin
                pm_power_state <= pmcsr_wr_value[1:0];
                pm_pme_enable  <= pmcsr_wr_value[8];
            end

            if (cfg_wr_hits_pmcsr && pmcsr_high_byte_written && pmcsr_wr_value[15]) begin
                pm_pme_status <= 1'b0;
            end
        end
    end

endmodule
```

Use the state in your BAR responder. In D3hot, do not keep pretending the device is fully active:

```systemverilog
// Example BAR read behavior gated by PMCSR state.
// Drop inside a donor-specific BAR implementation in:
// src/pcileech_tlps128_bar_controller.sv

always @ (posedge clk) begin
    if (rst) begin
        rd_rsp_ctx   <= 88'd0;
        rd_rsp_data  <= 32'd0;
        rd_rsp_valid <= 1'b0;
    end else begin
        rd_rsp_ctx   <= rd_req_ctx;
        rd_rsp_valid <= rd_req_valid;

        if (device_in_d3hot) begin
            case (rd_req_addr[11:0])
                12'h000: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                12'h004: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                12'h008: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                default: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
            endcase
        end else begin
            case (rd_req_addr[11:0])
                12'h000: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h81680001;
                12'h004: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000001;
                12'h008: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                12'h00C: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
                default: rd_rsp_data <= 32'h00000000;
            endcase
        end
    end
end
```

Keep the first version deterministic. Once the state transition works, replace the example DWORDs with behavior taken from the BAR dump and driver trace.

#### 11.8.4 PMCSR Bring-Up Checklist

For PMCSR, collect proof for each item below:

- PM capability base is parsed from the donor, not guessed;
- PMCSR offset is documented;
- PMCSR WriteMask allows PowerState and PME Enable at the correct offset;
- PME Status RW1C is either modeled or explicitly marked unimplemented;
- BAR behavior changes or safely idles when PMCSR enters D3hot;
- function-level reset returns the model to D0;
- Windows readback confirms the PMCSR transition;
- cold boot still enumerates cleanly.

If PMCSR is still ignored, record it as unimplemented.

### 11.9 Hold Off on More Logic

Do not stack more state machines on top until the current path meets all of these:

- BAR controller builds cleanly
- timing still passes
- BAR readback works on Windows
- required offsets return planned values
- required writes are handled
- driver behavior improves or failure reason is understood

---

## 12. Alternative: Zero4K Method

### 12.1 When Zero4K Is Useful

Zero4K is useful when:

- you need a simple first BAR response
- the donor uses a small BAR region
- tested offsets are within 4KB
- the driver mostly reads static registers

Zero4K is **not** full BAR emulation.

Zero4K proves only this:

```text
The first 4KB of one static BAR response can be read.
```

> [!NOTE]
> **Under the Hood - what Zero4K actually does**
>
> Zero4K is a static 4KB MMIO responder. It gives basic BAR probes stable readback instead of timeout, zeroes, or all-`FF`. It says nothing about reset logic, MSI-X table/PBA, EEPROM/NVM windows, or driver state machines.

Zero4K does **not** prove:

- larger BAR coverage
- MSI-X table behavior
- MSI-X PBA behavior
- reset bit behavior
- status bit behavior
- EEPROM/NVM window behavior
- write/readback behavior
- driver binding

If the donor BAR is larger than 4KB, document:

```text
BAR size:
Covered by Zero4K:
Not covered:
Offsets tested:
Offsets not tested:
MSI-X table/PBA inside covered range:
Driver-critical offsets inside covered range:
```

If you cannot fill that out, you do not understand what Zero4K is covering.

### 12.2 Generate `pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe` on Windows

Create a CSV:

```csv
offset,dword
0x000,12345678
0x004,00000000
0x008,ABCDEF01
```

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/make_zero4k_coe.py
```

```python
import csv
import sys

if len(sys.argv) != 3:
    print("Usage: python make_zero4k_coe.py bar_dwords.csv pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe")
    sys.exit(1)

csv_path = sys.argv[1]
out_path = sys.argv[2]

dwords = ["00000000"] * 1024

with open(csv_path, newline="") as f:
    reader = csv.DictReader(f)
    for row in reader:
        offset = int(row["offset"], 16)
        value = row["dword"].strip().replace("0x", "").replace("0X", "").upper()
        if offset % 4 != 0:
            raise SystemExit(f"Offset not aligned: 0x{offset:03X}")
        if offset >= 4096:
            raise SystemExit(f"Zero4K only supports first 4KB: 0x{offset:03X}")
        if len(value) != 8:
            raise SystemExit(f"DWORD must be 8 hex digits: {value}")
        dwords[offset // 4] = value

with open(out_path, "w", newline="\n") as f:
    f.write("memory_initialization_radix=16;\n")
    f.write("memory_initialization_vector=\n")
    for i, value in enumerate(dwords):
        f.write(value)
        f.write(";\n" if i == len(dwords) - 1 else ",\n")

print("Generated Zero4K COE:", out_path)
print("0x000:", dwords[0])
print("0x004:", dwords[1])
print("0xFFC:", dwords[1023])
```

Run:

```powershell
python C:\dma\tools\make_zero4k_coe.py C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\bar0_dwords.csv C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe
```

### 12.3 Install Zero4K COE in Vivado

Replace:

```text
ip/pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe
```

Then:

1. Find `bram_bar_zero4k`
2. Reset output products if needed
3. Generate output products
4. Rebuild
5. Test BAR readback on Windows

### 12.4 Zero4K Failure Signs

Zero4K has reached its limit if:

```text
BAR is 16KB but only first 4KB works
MSI-X table offset is outside 4KB
driver writes register but readback never changes
BAR read returns all zero
BAR read returns all F
BAR read times out
MSI-X table is outside 4KB
driver expects EEPROM/NVM window
reset/status register needs stateful behavior
```

Do not blame Vivado if your BAR model is incomplete.

### 12.5 When Zero4K Is Enough

Zero4K is a finished answer only when:

- COE generated with 1024 DWORDs
- byte order checked
- `bram_bar_zero4k` regenerated
- first DWORD reads correctly
- first 4KB reads without timeout
- covered and uncovered BAR ranges are documented
- MSI-X table/PBA coverage is documented if MSI-X exists
- you clearly document that this is not full large-BAR emulation

---

## 13. Build and Flash

### 13.1 Pre-Build Checklist

Before build:

```text
[ ] Stock firmware already works
[ ] Donor capture complete
[ ] Correct board folder selected
[ ] Correct FPGA part and package confirmed
[ ] Vivado version recorded
[ ] PCIe IP IDs configured
[ ] BAR type/size configured
[ ] cfg_dsn set if needed
[ ] rw[203] set in pcileech_fifo.sv
[ ] rw[206] set in pcileech_fifo.sv if using WriteMask
[ ] pcileech_cfgspace.coe generated and checked
[ ] pcileech_cfgspace_writemask.coe generated and checked
[ ] pcileech_bar_zero4k.coe generated if using Zero4K
[ ] BAR responder plan documented
[ ] recovery method confirmed
```

### 13.2 Vivado GUI Build Route

In Vivado:

1. Generate output products for changed IP
2. Run Synthesis
3. Open Synthesized Design only if needed
4. Run Implementation
5. Generate Bitstream
6. Open timing summary
7. Open utilization report
8. Save logs and reports

A build worth flashing ends with:

```text
Synthesis completed successfully
Implementation completed successfully
write_bitstream completed successfully
Timing constraints are met
```

Stop before flashing on:

```text
Synthesis failed
Implementation failed
Timing failed
Critical warning about clock/pin/part
IP output products out of date
```

Do not flash if implementation failed or timing is obviously broken.

### 13.3 Vivado Tcl Shortcut Route

Open:

```text
Start Menu -> Vivado Tcl Shell
```

Then:

```tcl
cd C:/dma/work/squirrel-rtl8125
source vivado_generate_project.tcl -notrace
source vivado_build.tcl -notrace
report_timing_summary -file timing_summary.txt
report_utilization -file utilization.txt
```

PowerShell log capture example:

```powershell
mkdir C:\dma\builds\logs
& "C:\Xilinx\Vivado\2023.2\bin\vivado.bat" -mode batch -source C:\dma\work\squirrel-rtl8125\vivado_build.tcl -notrace 2>&1 | Tee-Object C:\dma\builds\logs\vivado_build.log
```

Output paths vary, but commonly:

```text
<project>.runs/impl_1/*.bit
<project>.runs/impl_1/*.bin
```

### 13.4 Save Evidence Every Time

Do not make a mystery firmware. Save evidence.

The minimum set proves what was flashed. The full set lets someone reproduce it later.

**Minimum Evidence**

```text
C:/dma/builds/2026-xx-xx-board-donor-v1/
  windows-version.txt
  vivado-version.txt
  driver-version.txt
  board-folder.txt
  fpga-part-package.txt
  donor_specs.md
  vivado_build.log
  timing_summary.txt
  utilization.txt
  firmware.bit
  firmware.bin
  sha256.txt
  flash-tool-screenshot.png
  device-manager-hardware-ids.png
  device-manager-resources.png
  arbor-or-telescan-target-readback.txt
  cold-boot-result.txt
```

If you are missing minimum evidence, do not claim the step is finished.

**Full Evidence**

```text
C:/dma/builds/2026-xx-xx-board-donor-v1/
  windows-version.txt
  vivado-version.txt
  driver-version.txt
  board-folder.txt
  fpga-part-package.txt
  donor_specs.md
  git-diff.patch
  vivado_build.log
  timing_summary.txt
  utilization.txt
  firmware.bit
  firmware.bin
  sha256.txt
  flash-tool-screenshot.png
  device-manager-hardware-ids.png
  device-manager-resources.png
  arbor-target-readback.txt
  telescan-target.tlscan
  cold-boot-result.txt
  device-manager-events.png
  device-manager-driver-status.png
  arbor-donor-export.txt
  telescan-donor.tlscan
  config-dwords.csv
  generated-coe-check-output.txt
  writemask-check-notes.txt
  bar-readback-notes.txt
  flash-tool-log.txt
  photos/
```

PowerShell hash:

```powershell
Get-FileHash .\firmware.bit -Algorithm SHA256
Get-FileHash .\firmware.bin -Algorithm SHA256
```

### 13.5 Windows Flashing by Board Family

There is no universal flash command.

Before any board-specific flashing:

```text
[ ] Programmer appears in Windows Device Manager
[ ] Flashing tool can detect the programmer
[ ] Stock firmware or recovery image is available
[ ] Correct FPGA part/package is written down
[ ] Correct board folder is written down
[ ] You know whether the operation is SRAM load or flash programming
[ ] You saved the build hash
```

If the programmer is not detected before flashing, there is no tested recovery path.

**Squirrel / LeetDMA**

Possible tools:

- OpenOCD for Windows
- Squirrel update port workflow
- vendor tool

Warnings:

- `pld load` may only load SRAM
- persistent flash programming is different
- cold boot proves persistence

**CaptainDMA**

Possible tools:

- CH347 FPGA tool
- vendor tool
- M2-FW module for some M.2 boards

Warnings:

- 35T CSG325 and 35T FGG484 are not interchangeable
- 75T and 100T images are not interchangeable
- wrong image can stop enumeration

**Enigma X1**

Possible tools:

- Vivado Hardware Manager
- upstream/vendor flash script

Warnings:

- confirm exact FPGA part
- confirm flash memory part
- do not assume Squirrel commands apply

**ZDMA**

Possible tools:

- Vivado Hardware Manager
- vendor flow

Warnings:

- may involve more than one device/FPGA path
- confirm which image is being programmed

**AC701**

Possible tools:

- Vivado Hardware Manager
- official Xilinx/JTAG flow

Warnings:

- choose correct memory part
- board is not the same as cheap Artix-7 DMA boards

### 13.6 SRAM Load vs Flash Programming

SRAM and flash are easy to confuse.

| Operation | What happens |
|----------|--------------|
| SRAM / volatile load | FPGA runs new image until power is removed |
| Flash programming | Image persists after power loss |

If warm reboot shows new firmware but cold boot returns old firmware, you probably only loaded SRAM.

How to tell you only loaded SRAM:

```text
new firmware works immediately after programming
Windows restart still may show it
full power-off makes old firmware return
flash tool log does not show flash erase/program/verify
command name says load, configure, or pld load instead of program flash
```

How to tell flash programming probably happened:

```text
tool erased flash
tool programmed flash
tool verified flash
device still shows new firmware after full power removal
```

### 13.7 Cold Boot Verification

After flashing:

1. Shut down Windows
2. Turn off PSU or remove power if needed
3. Wait 10-30 seconds
4. Power on
5. Boot Windows
6. Check Device Manager
7. Check Arbor/TeleScan readback

Warm reboot normal does not prove flash persistence.

### 13.8 Save the Build Before Leaving the Bench

Do not pack up after seeing the progress bar hit 100%. Save and verify:

- bit/bin generated
- timing reviewed
- utilization saved
- hash saved
- correct flash tool used
- flash screenshot saved
- cold boot performed
- Windows sees the expected device after cold boot

---

## 14. Windows Validation and Troubleshooting

### 14.1 Device Manager Is Only Step One

Open:

```text
Device Manager -> target device -> Properties
```

Check:

- General tab
- Driver tab
- Details -> Hardware Ids
- Details -> Compatible Ids
- Resources tab
- Events tab

A clean Device Manager result:

```text
Device status: This device is working properly.
Hardware IDs show expected VEN/DEV/SUBSYS/REV.
Resources show expected memory ranges.
No conflict listed.
```

Enumeration or driver work remains if:

```text
Unknown device
Code 10
Code 12
Code 31
No Resources tab
BAR resource missing
Device failed to start
```

### 14.2 Arbor/TeleScan Target Readback

After flashing, use Arbor or TeleScan PE on the Windows target.

Compare target against donor notes:

| Area | Must check |
|------|------------|
| `0x00` | VID/DID |
| `0x04` | Command/Status |
| `0x08` | Revision/Class |
| `0x10-0x24` | BARs |
| `0x2C` | Subsystem IDs |
| `0x34` | Capability Pointer |
| `0x40+` | Standard capabilities |
| `0x100+` | Extended capabilities |

Then classify differences:

| Difference type | Examples | What to do |
|-----------------|----------|------------|
| Stable field | VID/DID, Revision/Class, Subsystem IDs, capability IDs | Should match the donor plan. Fix if wrong. |
| Runtime field | Command, Status, BAR assigned address, MSI enable, PM state | Record it. Do not panic if it changes. |
| Intentional difference | FPGA link width differs, MSI-X intentionally disabled for a test | Document why. |
| Bug | broken capability pointer, wrong BAR size, missing extended cap, stale VID/DID | Fix before claiming success. |

Your diff table should not say "close enough". It should say stable, runtime, intentional, or bug.

Readback problems:

```text
0x40 and later all zero
capability chain broken
extended capabilities missing
BAR values look like donor runtime addresses
VID/DID still default PCILeech
```

Fix the relevant firmware step. Do not randomly change more IDs.

### 14.3 Windows WriteMask and Command Register Test

Use Arbor/TeleScan or another trusted PCI config editor if it supports controlled writes.

Test:

1. Read Command register
2. Toggle allowed Command bits
3. Read back
4. Try writing VID/DID
5. Confirm VID/DID did not change
6. Clear reasonable Status/RW1C bits
7. Confirm device remains alive

The config write path is behaving when:

```text
Command writable bits stick.
VID/DID remain unchanged.
Status behavior is reasonable.
Device remains present.
```

WriteMask or shadow bugs look like:

```text
Command never changes
VID/DID become corrupted
device disappears after config write
MSI enable cannot stick
```

Those are WriteMask/shadow-write failures.

### 14.4 Windows BAR Readback Test

Use Arbor, TeleScan, vendor diagnostic tools, or your own lab BAR read tool.

Minimum:

- BAR first DWORD
- BAR first 4KB
- unsupported offset
- high offset if BAR is larger than 4KB
- MSI-X table/PBA offset if MSI-X exists

A working BAR path:

```text
BAR read completes.
Values are stable.
Unsupported offsets return safe values.
Target does not freeze.
```

A broken or incomplete BAR path:

```text
read timeout
all zero unexpectedly
all FFFFFFFF
random values
target freezes
driver fails after BAR access
```

Fix BAR response path.

### 14.5 Driver Binding Failures

Driver binding debug order:

```text
1. Confirm stock firmware still works.
2. Confirm PCIe identity: VID/DID/Revision/Class/Subsys.
3. Confirm BAR type, size, 64-bit pairing, and Resources tab.
4. Confirm config-space readback in Arbor/TeleScan.
5. Confirm WriteMask and Command register behavior.
6. Confirm BAR readback.
7. Confirm MSI/MSI-X capability and table/PBA behavior.
8. Confirm PMCSR behavior.
9. Confirm reset/status registers in BAR space.
10. Then read Driver tab and Events.
```

If you jump from Code 10 straight back to changing VID/DID, you are guessing.

**Code 10 - device cannot start**

Real causes:

- BAR register behavior missing
- MSI/MSI-X broken
- PMCSR broken
- EEPROM/NVM window missing
- reset bit never clears
- status bit never changes
- interrupt mask behavior wrong
- driver expects real hardware state

Do not fix Code 10 by changing VID/DID again.

**Code 12 - not enough resources**

Likely causes:

- BAR size too large
- invalid BAR pairing
- 64-bit BAR configured wrong
- resource conflict
- target BIOS/slot issue

**Code 31 - driver failed to load**

Likely causes:

- wrong class/subsystem
- driver mismatch
- missing capability behavior
- Windows driver package issue

**Unknown device**

Likely causes:

- VID/DID/class mismatch
- driver not installed
- config space incomplete
- subsystem mismatch

### 14.6 Common Windows Failure Cases

| Symptom | Likely cause | First thing to check |
|---------|--------------|----------------------|
| Device Manager completely does not show device | flash failed, wrong bitstream, PCIe link issue, board not powered | stock firmware recovery and PCIe link |
| Unknown device | identity/class/subsystem mismatch | Hardware IDs and Class Code |
| Code 10 | BAR/MSI/PMCSR/state behavior missing | BAR readback and Events tab |
| Code 12 | BAR resource conflict or bad size | Resources tab |
| Code 31 | driver package or matching issue | Driver tab and Events |
| Resources tab empty | BAR disabled, enumeration incomplete, driver/device failed too early | Vivado BAR settings and config readback |
| BAR size wrong | Vivado IP BAR size/type wrong or shadow overwrote BAR registers | PCIe IP BAR tab and target BAR sizing |
| Config after 0x40 all zero | `rw[203]` still zero-data or COE not loaded | `pcileech_fifo.sv` and BRAM regenerate |
| Extended capability missing | COE only covers 256B, extended chain broken, wrong takeover | COE depth and `0x100` readback |
| VID/DID did not change | IP not regenerated or stale flash | PCIe IP, bitstream timestamp |
| VID/DID got corrupted | WriteMask allows writes at `0x00` | WriteMask at `0x00` |
| Command write does not stick | `rw[206]` disabled or mask wrong | WriteMask |
| MSI Enable does not stick | MSI capability mask wrong or MSI offset assumed incorrectly | donor capability offset and WriteMask |
| BAR read timeout | no completion path | BAR controller |
| BAR reads all zero | Zero/static responder used incorrectly, COE not loaded, wrong BAR index | BAR COE and BAR routing |
| BAR reads all F | no device response, unsupported path, failed completion | BAR controller and PCIe completion path |
| Cold boot returns old firmware | SRAM load only | persistent flash process |
| Vivado erased manual edit | output products regenerated | generated file diff |
| COE not used by BRAM | wrong COE path, BRAM not regenerated, stale IP output | Vivado IP customization and generated output products |
| Build fails after paste | pasted pseudocode | module ports/signals |
| Wrong board folder used | wrong pins/part/project | upstream board matrix and FPGA package |
| FPGA part/package wrong | wrong constraints and bitstream | Vivado part settings and board marking |
| CH347/OpenOCD/Vivado HW Manager does not see board | programmer driver, wrong cable, board mode, power | Windows Device Manager programmer entry |
| Board dead after flash | wrong board folder, wrong FPGA package, bad image | recovery image/tool |

### 14.7 Failure Matrix

Match the symptom, collect the listed evidence, and fix the first failing layer.

Work from the lowest failing layer:

| Level | Layer | What must be proven | Primary evidence |
|------|-------|---------------------|------------------|
| 0 | Power / clock / reset | Board powers, FPGA configures, PCIe refclk/reset are sane | programmer detect, flash log, ILA reset/link probes |
| 1 | Link training | Endpoint reaches a stable link before OS driver work | BIOS visibility, `pl_ltssm_state`, `pl_phy_lnk_up`, cold boot |
| 2 | Enumeration / config | Type 0 config reads/writes behave | Device Manager, Arbor/TeleScan, `CfgRd0/CfgWr0` ILA |
| 3 | BAR / TLP | MMIO reads/writes complete and state changes | BAR readback, ILA `rd_rsp_valid`, dynamic BAR state |
| 4 | Driver workload | Driver starts and survives normal operations | Events tab, driver logs, workload test, cold boot repeat |

#### 14.7.1 POST Hang / BIOS Freeze / No Boot

| Symptom | Likely cause | Evidence | Fix | Avoid |
|---------|-----------------|--------------------------|--------------|----------------|
| Motherboard freezes before OS boot | BAR request is too large for firmware MMIO allocation window | BIOS POST code, resources differ between stock and custom firmware, BAR size in PCIe IP | Reduce BAR size to donor-realistic value; disable unused BARs; confirm 64-bit pairing | Do not increase BAR size because "bigger looks real" |
| POST hangs only with custom bitstream | PCIe link training timeout or unstable LTSSM transition | ILA `pl_ltssm_state`, `pl_phy_lnk_up`, `pl_initial_link_width`, cold boot capture | Fix PCIe IP speed/lane settings; test Gen1 first; verify slot/adaptor signal integrity | Do not edit VID/DID for a link training failure |
| Board works in one slot but not another | MMIO aperture, ASPM, bifurcation, or lane wiring difference | Same firmware across two slots, BIOS resource map, link width/speed readback | Test simple x1 Gen1 profile; change slot; disable aggressive ASPM in BIOS for lab testing | Do not assume the FPGA image is proven because one slot works |
| Device disappears after cold boot but warm reboot works | SRAM load only, flash not persistent, or PCIe training marginal after power loss | flash tool log, cold boot result, bit/bin hash, programmer verify output | Program persistent flash; verify erase/program/verify; power-cycle and re-read config | Do not call warm reboot a flash validation |
| POST fail after changing board folder | Wrong FPGA part/package or wrong `.xdc` pins | Vivado part name, package, board marking, `.xdc` diff, timing critical warnings | Use correct board folder; verify FPGA package; restore known-good constraints | Do not force bitstream generation with wrong constraints |
| Board does not enumerate after timing failure | PCIe user clock / reset crossing broken by failed implementation | `timing_summary.rpt`, worst negative slack, unconstrained clocks | Fix timing before flashing; reduce logic; pipeline BAR state machine | Do not flash a bitstream with obvious timing failure |
| Flash succeeds but card is dead | Wrong image family, wrong flash offset, or vendor tool wrote incompatible image | IDCODE, flash log, board silkscreen, stock recovery test | Restore stock firmware; confirm exact FPGA and flash part; rebuild from correct project | Do not try random board images |

POST-level rule:

```text
No stable PCIe link = do not debug WriteMask.
No stable flash persistence = do not debug Windows driver binding.
No correct FPGA package = do not debug BAR behavior.
```

#### 14.7.2 Device Manager Yellow Triangle: Code 10 / Code 43

Code 10 and Code 43 are not solved by changing IDs. They mean the driver or Windows device stack hit behavior that did not match the device contract.

| Symptom | Likely cause | Evidence | Test | Fix |
|---------|-----------------|---------------------|---------------|--------------|
| Code 10 immediately after driver start | BAR read returns timeout/all-zero/all-`FF` | Arbor/TeleScan BAR read, Events tab, ILA BAR `rd_req_valid` vs `rd_rsp_valid` | Read first DWORD, first 4KB, unsupported offset | Implement BAR responder for the register path the driver touches |
| Code 10 after config writes | WriteMask blocks required writable bits | Arbor/TeleScan before/after `CfgWr0`, ILA `pcie_rx_wren`, target config diff | Toggle Command, MSI Enable, PMCSR PowerState at donor offsets | Regenerate capability-aware WriteMask |
| Code 10 after reset register write | BAR reset bit never self-clears | BAR trace: write reset bit, repeated status reads | Write reset bit, poll status | Add reset timer/state transition in BAR model |
| Code 43 / device reported problem | Driver sees impossible status/capability combination | Device Events, config readback, BAR status values | Compare donor and target after driver start | Fix contradictions: MSI-X exposed but table dead, PMCSR D3hot but BAR active, AER broken |
| MSI enable cannot stick | Wrong capability offset or WriteMask bit | Config diff at actual MSI capability base | Write MSI Message Control, read back | Parse donor capability chain; mask actual offset |
| MSI-X enabled then driver fails | MSI-X table/PBA BAR region missing | MSI-X capability table offset/BIR, BAR read at table/PBA | Read/write MSI-X table entry and PBA area | Implement table/PBA behavior or do not expose MSI-X |
| PMCSR write breaks driver start | Power-state bits not writable or no D0/D3 behavior | PM capability base, PMCSR readback, BAR behavior after D3hot | Write D3hot then D0, read PMCSR and BAR status | Add PMCSR WriteMask and PM-aware BAR state |
| VID/DID corrupts after test write | WriteMask permits identity writes | Arbor/TeleScan write test at `0x00` | Attempt write `0x00.L`, read back | Set identity area read-only; restore donor shadow COE |

WriteMask targeting flow:

```text
1. Capture donor capability offsets.
2. Capture target config before driver bind.
3. Start driver.
4. Capture target config after failure.
5. Diff runtime fields only.
6. For each failed field:
   - Is the bit supposed to be writable?
   - Is it RW1C?
   - Is the offset donor-correct?
   - Did the write hit `pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv`?
   - Did `rw[206]` in `src/pcileech_fifo.sv` allow the write path?
7. Regenerate WriteMask.
8. Re-test only that field.
```

The fix for Code 10/43 is usually one layer deeper than Device Manager says.

#### 14.7.3 Driver Load Causes BSOD

A BSOD during driver load is a hard failure. Treat it as a protocol crash until proven otherwise.

| Crash timing | Likely cause | Evidence | ILA / software probe | Fix |
|-------------|-----------------|---------------------|----------------------|--------------|
| BSOD immediately after driver starts | Driver MMIO read gets no completion or illegal response | Windows crash time, BAR readback, ILA `rd_req_valid` without `rd_rsp_valid` | Trigger on first MemRd to BAR after driver bind | Return safe completion for every decoded and unsupported offset |
| BSOD after a BAR write handshake | FPGA ignores doorbell/mailbox write | ILA `wr_valid`, `wr_addr`, `wr_data`, following status polls | Trigger on write to doorbell/status/control offset | Add dynamic BAR state machine; update busy/status/response |
| BSOD after MSI/MSI-X enable | Interrupt capability says yes, behavior says no | MSI/MSI-X config diff, IRQ status, table/PBA BAR access | Watch MSI enable write and table writes | Implement MSI-X table/PBA or disable MSI-X in donor plan |
| BSOD during reset path | Reset bit never clears or clears too fast/late | BAR reset write, repeated status reads, driver timeout | Trigger on reset register write | Add reset timer and self-clear behavior from donor trace |
| BSOD under workload | Queue/descriptor/stream registers are static | BAR write/read sequence, packet/audio counters, driver logs | Capture doorbell writes and status polling loop | Add queue depth, counter, descriptor, or stream-state modeling |
| BSOD only after cold boot | Flash persistence or link training unstable | cold boot capture, link state, flash verify | Compare warm vs cold ILA traces | Fix flash programming or PCIe PHY/link settings |

BSOD triage order:

```text
1. Restore stock firmware and prove target machine is stable.
2. Boot custom firmware without binding the donor driver if possible.
3. Read config space with Arbor/TeleScan.
4. Read BAR first DWORD and unsupported offset.
5. Enable ILA trigger on BAR MemRd/MemWr.
6. Bind driver and capture the last successful TLP.
7. If the last TLP is MemRd with no completion, fix completion path.
8. If the last TLP is MemWr doorbell followed by polling, fix BAR state machine.
9. If the last TLP is MSI-X table write, fix table/PBA behavior.
10. Re-test from cold boot.
```

Do not keep rebooting into BSOD and changing random IDs. Capture the failing transaction.

#### 14.7.4 Evidence Map

| Evidence | Proves | Does not prove |
|----------|--------|----------------|
| Device Manager visible | Basic enumeration | Driver correctness |
| Resources tab | BAR allocation | BAR response |
| Arbor/TeleScan config diff | Config identity and write behavior | BAR state machine |
| BAR readback | Completion path and basic MMIO | Driver workload correctness |
| ILA CfgRd/CfgWr trigger | Enumeration transaction path | BAR model behavior |
| ILA MemRd/MemWr trigger | Driver register traffic | Correct high-level device semantics |
| Timing report | Build timing health | Functional correctness |
| Cold boot | Flash persistence and link training | Full driver behavior |

A "yellow triangle" is not a diagnosis. Tie the failure to a layer, capture the artifact, then fix the first broken part.

### 14.8 Reading the Output

**Vivado normal**

```text
Synthesis completed successfully.
Implementation completed successfully.
write_bitstream completed successfully.
Timing constraints are met.
```

**Vivado bad**

```text
CRITICAL WARNING: timing constraints not met
ERROR: part not found
ERROR: module not found
ERROR: failed to generate output products
```

**PCIe IP regenerate normal**

```text
Generate Output Products completed.
IP status is current.
Expected `.xci` changes remain.
Expected generated-file edits still exist if you made any.
```

**PCIe IP regenerate bad**

```text
IP output products failed.
Vivado upgraded the IP unexpectedly.
Generated wrapper edit disappeared.
COE path reverted.
```

**COE parse normal**

```text
memory_initialization_radix=16 accepted
memory_initialization_vector accepted
BRAM/ROM output products generated
sanity-check script shows expected 0x00/0x08/0x2C/0x34/0x100
```

**COE parse bad**

```text
invalid radix
invalid memory initialization vector
wrong number of DWORDs
0x000 is 00000000
capability chain loop detected
runtime BAR-looking value warning
```

**Device Manager normal**

```text
This device is working properly.
Hardware IDs contain expected VEN/DEV/SUBSYS/REV.
Resources show memory ranges.
```

**Device Manager bad**

```text
Code 10
Code 12
Code 31
Unknown device
No resources
```

**Arbor/TeleScan normal**

```text
Header decodes correctly.
Capability chain is valid.
BAR sizes match donor plan.
Extended capabilities are present if expected.
```

**Arbor/TeleScan bad**

```text
FFFF:FFFF
capability pointer invalid
0x40+ all zero
BAR size wrong
extended config missing
```

**BAR read normal**

```text
first DWORD returns expected value
4KB read completes
unsupported offset returns safe default
```

**BAR read bad**

```text
timeout
all zero
all F
random changing values
system freeze
```

**Flash normal**

```text
programmer detected
target FPGA ID matches expected family
programming completes without verify error
tool log saved
```

**Flash bad**

```text
programmer not found
unexpected IDCODE
verify failed
tool only performed SRAM load when you expected flash programming
```

**Cold boot normal**

```text
power removed
system powered back on
device enumerates with new firmware
Arbor/TeleScan readback still matches target plan
```

**Cold boot bad**

```text
device returns to old firmware
device disappears
target hangs at POST
BAR/resources differ from warm reboot
```

### 14.9 Final Validation Checklist

```text
[ ] Donor capture folder complete
[ ] Windows driver version saved
[ ] Stock firmware baseline works
[ ] Correct board folder used
[ ] Correct FPGA part/package used
[ ] PCIe IP IDs correct
[ ] BAR type/size correct
[ ] Shadow config COE generated by offset
[ ] 0x00/0x08/0x2C/0x34/0x100 validated
[ ] rw[203] edited in pcileech_fifo.sv
[ ] WriteMask COE generated
[ ] rw[206] edited in pcileech_fifo.sv
[ ] cfg_dsn matches DSN plan
[ ] MSI/MSI-X plan documented
[ ] Zero4K limitation documented
[ ] Build log saved
[ ] Timing report saved
[ ] Utilization report saved
[ ] bit/bin hashes saved
[ ] Flash tool screenshot saved
[ ] Cold boot completed
[ ] Device Manager screenshots saved
[ ] Arbor/TeleScan target readback saved
[ ] BAR readback tested
[ ] Driver status recorded
```

If you cannot show the evidence, you did not finish the step.

### 14.10 Keep a Test Record

Save the following with the build:

- Device Manager status is saved
- Hardware IDs are saved
- Resources are saved
- Events are saved
- Arbor or TeleScan target readback is saved
- donor-target diff is classified
- WriteMask behavior is tested or explicitly marked untested
- BAR validation level is recorded
- driver binding result is recorded
- cold boot result is recorded

### 14.11 Before Calling It Final

Only call the build final after:

- Windows donor capture reaches at least Level 3
- COE generation is reproducible
- COE sanity check passes
- WriteMask level is declared
- BAR validation level is declared
- Zero4K coverage is documented if used
- recovery path is documented
- minimum evidence folder exists
- all known differences are classified as stable, runtime, intentional, or bug
- the README does not imply that VID/DID-only work is complete firmware

Anything short of this stays experimental.

## Advanced: Hardware Debugging with Vivado ILA

When a board enumerates once and then randomly dies, screenshots are not enough. Use ILA and look at the bus.

Use ILA for the ugly cases:

- target hangs during POST
- device appears only after warm reboot
- config space reads as zero after offset `0x40`
- BAR sizing works once and then fails
- Windows shows Code 10 but the donor identity looks correct
- a generated IP change silently changed the TLP path

### ILA.1 Probe the Right RX Path

In current upstream-style PCILeech 7 Series projects, the PCIe endpoint receive interface is usually wired in:

```text
src/pcileech_pcie_a7.sv
```

Look for:

```systemverilog
.m_axis_rx_tdata  ( tlp_rx.data  ),
.m_axis_rx_tkeep  ( tlp_rx.keep  ),
.m_axis_rx_tlast  ( tlp_rx.last  ),
.m_axis_rx_tvalid ( tlp_rx.valid )
```

Some generated Xilinx wrapper views label the endpoint RX side as `s_axis_rx_*` or expose it through a different hierarchy. Do not fight the name. The real rule is simple:

```text
Probe the RX stream coming out of the PCIe core and entering the PCILeech TLP pipeline.
```

Useful probes:

| Probe | Why |
|------|-----|
| `tlp_rx.data[63:0]` | Raw TLP header/data from PCIe core in the 64-bit RX path |
| `tlp_rx.keep[7:0]` | Which bytes are valid |
| `tlp_rx.last` | End of packet |
| `tlp_rx.valid` | Packet beat valid |
| `tlp_rx.user[21:0]` | Sideband flags if exposed in your build |
| `tlps_in.tdata[127:0]` | Repacked 128-bit TLP stream used by shadow/BAR logic |
| `tlps_in.tuser[0]` | First DWORD marker in `IfAXIS128` |
| `pcie_rx_rden` | Config read detected in `pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv` |
| `pcie_rx_wren` | Config write detected in `pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv` |
| `bram_rd_valid` | Shadow config read response generated |
| `rd_rsp_valid` | BAR read completion generated |

If you only probe `VID/DID`, you are not debugging. Probe the packet path.

### ILA.2 Trigger on Config Reads and Writes

The config-shadow module already shows the useful decode:

```text
src/pcileech_tlps128_cfgspace_shadow.sv
```

Current upstream-style decode:

```systemverilog
wire pcie_rx_rden = tlps_in.tvalid
                  && tlps_in.tuser[0]
                  && (tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0000010); // CfgRd0/CfgRd1

wire pcie_rx_wren = tlps_in.tvalid
                  && tlps_in.tuser[0]
                  && (tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0100010); // CfgWr0/CfgWr1
```

ILA trigger plan:

```text
Trigger 1: tlps_in.tvalid == 1
Trigger 2: tlps_in.tuser[0] == 1
Trigger 3: tlps_in.tdata[31:25] == 7'b0000010 or 7'b0100010
Capture:  tlps_in.tdata, tlps_in.tkeepdw, tlps_in.tuser, pcie_rx_rden, pcie_rx_wren, bram_rd_valid
Depth:    4096 samples minimum if your FPGA has enough BRAM
Window:   pre-trigger 25%, post-trigger 75%
```

What this tells you:

| ILA result | Meaning |
|-----------|---------|
| No config TLPs arrive | Link training, reset, clocking, or PCIe core problem. Stop editing COE. |
| `CfgRd0` arrives but no response path fires | Shadow config decode, `rw[203]`, filter, or BRAM path is wrong. |
| `CfgWr0` arrives before hang | Host is changing Command/Status/BAR/PM state; check WriteMask and writable behavior. |
| Config path works, BAR read never completes | BAR controller or selected BAR implementation is wrong. |
| Completion exists but data is shifted | Endian/order/offset bug. Check DWORD indexing. |

### ILA.3 POST-Fail Workflow

Do this in order. Do not change five things at once.

1. Build a known-good stock or baseline bitstream with ILA.
2. Save the baseline capture for normal enumeration.
3. Build your modified firmware with the same ILA probes.
4. Cold boot the target, not just Windows restart.
5. Capture the first `CfgRd0` and first `CfgWr0`.
6. Compare against the baseline:
   - first config read offset
   - first config write offset
   - Command register write
   - BAR sizing sequence
   - capability pointer walk
   - first BAR MMIO read
7. Fix the first broken branch only.
8. Rebuild and repeat.

A routine early-enumeration trace is boring:

```text
CfgRd0 arrives
shadow/config response returns
CfgWr0 updates expected writable bits
BAR sizing reads/writes complete
capability chain reads continue
BAR MMIO reads complete if the driver starts
```

The first break often looks like:

```text
CfgRd0 arrives once, then nothing
CfgWr0 to Command register happens, then device disappears
BAR sizing request receives nonsense
capability pointer jumps into zero space
BAR read request appears but rd_rsp_valid never fires
```

If ILA says the host never sent the packet, the bug is not in your BAR responder. If ILA says the packet arrived and you never replied, the bug is yours.

### ILA.4 What to Save

An ILA session is useful only if you leave with:

- ILA probes are attached to the actual RX/TLP path
- trigger catches `CfgRd0` and `CfgWr0`
- baseline capture is saved
- failing firmware capture is saved
- first divergence from baseline is identified
- fix is applied to the first broken branch only
- new cold boot capture confirms the fix

---

## Automation Tools & Scripts

Automation must preserve offsets. A one-DWORD shift can pass a quick visual check while breaking every offset after it.

### AUTO.1 Convert Raw Config Hex to SystemVerilog Array

The parser accepts common `lspci -xxxx` and TeleScan-style hex lines. Plain `lspci -vvv` usually has capability text but not the raw byte image. If there are no offset-prefixed hex lines, use `lspci -xxxxxxx` from Appendix A or export raw config bytes from TeleScan.

```text
00: ec 10 25 81 07 04 10 00 05 00 00 02 10 00 00 00
10: 04 00 00 f0 00 00 00 00 04 00 00 f2 00 00 00 00
```

Output is a little-endian DWORD array for SystemVerilog test logic or manual comparison.

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/config_hex_to_sv.py
```

```python
import re
import sys

if len(sys.argv) != 3:
    print("Usage: python config_hex_to_sv.py config_hex.txt cfg_space.sv")
    sys.exit(1)

src_path = sys.argv[1]
out_path = sys.argv[2]

cfg = [0x00] * 4096
line_re = re.compile(r"^\s*([0-9a-fA-F]{2,3}):\s*((?:[0-9a-fA-F]{2}\s*)+)")

with open(src_path, "r", encoding="utf-8", errors="ignore") as f:
    for line in f:
        m = line_re.match(line)
        if not m:
            continue

        offset = int(m.group(1), 16)
        values = [int(x, 16) for x in re.findall(r"[0-9a-fA-F]{2}", m.group(2))]

        for i, value in enumerate(values):
            pos = offset + i
            if pos >= len(cfg):
                raise SystemExit(f"Offset outside 4KB config space: 0x{pos:03X}")
            cfg[pos] = value

def dword_at(offset):
    # PCIe config bytes are byte-addressed. SystemVerilog DWORD value here
    # is little-endian: byte 0 becomes bits [7:0], byte 3 becomes bits [31:24].
    return (
        cfg[offset]
        | (cfg[offset + 1] << 8)
        | (cfg[offset + 2] << 16)
        | (cfg[offset + 3] << 24)
    )

with open(out_path, "w", encoding="utf-8", newline="\n") as f:
    f.write("// Generated from raw config hex. Verify key offsets before use.\n")
    f.write("logic [31:0] cfg_space [0:1023] = '{\n")
    for idx in range(1024):
        offset = idx * 4
        comma = "," if idx != 1023 else ""
        f.write(f"    10'd{idx}: 32'h{dword_at(offset):08X}{comma} // 0x{offset:03X}\n")
    f.write("};\n")

for offset in (0x000, 0x008, 0x02C, 0x034, 0x100):
    print(f"0x{offset:03X}: 32'h{dword_at(offset):08X}")

print("Wrote:", out_path)
```

Run:

```powershell
python C:\dma\tools\config_hex_to_sv.py C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\config_hex.txt C:\dma\donor\rtl8125\cfg_space.sv
```

Reject output like:

```text
0x000: 32'hFFFFFFFF
0x008: 32'h00000000
0x034: points outside captured range
```

Usable output starts like:

```text
0x000: vendor/device DWORD matches donor
0x008: revision/class DWORD matches donor
0x02C: subsystem DWORD matches donor
0x034: capability pointer matches donor plan
0x100: extended capability header matches donor plan if present
```

Do not paste this array blindly into a COE file. COE generation has its own format and offset rules. Use this as a conversion/checking tool unless you intentionally wire a SystemVerilog array into your design.

### AUTO.2 Minimal Vivado Batch Build Script

For repeat builds, keep a small Tcl wrapper and save logs. Project scripts differ by board folder; the build sequence does not:

Create:

```text
C:/dma/tools/build_pcileech_batch.tcl
```

```tcl
if { $argc < 2 } {
    puts "Usage: vivado -mode batch -source build_pcileech_batch.tcl -tclargs <board_dir> <jobs>"
    exit 1
}

set board_dir [lindex $argv 0]
set jobs      [lindex $argv 1]

cd $board_dir

if {[file exists vivado_generate_project.tcl]} {
    source vivado_generate_project.tcl
}

if {[file exists vivado_build.tcl]} {
    source vivado_build.tcl
} else {
    reset_run synth_1
    launch_runs synth_1 -jobs $jobs
    wait_on_run synth_1

    launch_runs impl_1 -to_step write_bitstream -jobs $jobs
    wait_on_run impl_1
}

open_run impl_1
report_timing_summary -file build_timing_summary.rpt
report_utilization     -file build_utilization.rpt

puts "Build finished."
puts "Timing report:      [file normalize build_timing_summary.rpt]"
puts "Utilization report: [file normalize build_utilization.rpt]"
```

Run from **Vivado Tcl Shell** or a PowerShell that can see `vivado.bat`:

```powershell
vivado.bat -mode batch -source C:\dma\tools\build_pcileech_batch.tcl -tclargs C:\dma\pcileech-fpga\PCIeSquirrel 8
```

Archive after every build:

```text
Vivado version
Windows version
board folder
FPGA part/package
build log
build_timing_summary.rpt
build_utilization.rpt
bit/bin file
SHA256 hash
flash tool screenshot
cold boot result
```

If the saved folder and logs cannot reproduce the bitstream, the build is not reproducible.
